<title>Solitaire Games on Your Table - September 2015</title>
<description>[center][ImageID=2373684large][/center]

[center][size=24][b][COLOR=#0066FF]Welcome to September&#039;s 
Solo Games on Your Table[/COLOR][/b][/size][/center]

[size=14]Well [b]Summer Holidays[/b] are gone (at least for the most of the European people) and we can start to WAIT for the Christmas one :)[/size]


[size=12]So the [b]&quot;Just For Fun Challenges&quot;[/b] this month will be all about waitings.[/size]
Just let us know something related to board games and &quot;waiting&quot;.
Like I&#039;ve waited for about three months to receive the package from my Secret Soloist and... it worth the waiting! Thanks again SeSo!
...or some games you&#039;ve waited so long to buy and it was just disappointing
[size=9][i]This are Just for Fun so don&#039;t expect to receive :bag: on every entries.[/i][/size]


[size=12][b]Rules[/b]
[/size]
:d10-1: Play a solo game, or a multi player game solo...
:d10-2: Post an entry on this geeklist and tell us about it.
:d10-3: Be nice, but most of all have fun.

And if you want try to add some :thumbsup: and more :thumbsdown: just to be wallet-saver

[u][center]:star::star: Let&#039;s break some records and make September list the biggest one! :star::star:[/center][/u]

You need:

One or more holiday locations away from distractions.

A wife, husband or partner who has no or little interesting games but is happy to let you play.

A car full of solo/solo-able games.

Full or occasional Internet access to update the con geeklist or blog.

<comment username="Zouave" date="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 17:08:41 +0000" postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 17:08:41 +0000" editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 17:08:54 +0000" thumbs="6">
Two games that will likely be on my table/tablet:


[thing=133038][/thing].

[q]NDIANAPOLIS -- August 13, 2014 -- Obsidian Entertainment, the developer of Fallout: New Vegas, South Park: the Stick of Truth and the Kickstarter phenomenon Pillars of Eternity, announced that they have entered into a long-term licensing partnership with Paizo Inc. to produce electronic games based on its popular Pathfinder Roleplaying Game intellectual property.
 
Obsidian&#039;s first licensed product will be a tablet game based on the highly successful Pathfinder Adventure Card game, a cooperative game for 1 to 4 players. Players each have a unique character composed of a deck of cards and a set of stats. Characters have classes such as fighter, rogue, wizard and cleric, as well as numbers that define attributes such as strength, wisdom and charisma etc. Players will be able to customize their deck to better suit each individualâ€™s vision of their character.[/q]

[thing=154013][/thing].

[q]Stoic&#039;s tactical role-playing, Viking-themed series The Banner Saga is getting a miniatures board game adaptation called The Banner Saga: Warbands, the developer announced today.

Stoic, along with publisher Versus Evil and board game maker MegaCon Games, will work together on the project. Few other details about Warbands are currently available, though it is expected to gather funding via Kickstarter &quot;soon.&quot; A website for the game is currently online.[/q]


</comment>

Joe Hisaishi needs more exposure, but has done some beautiful work for Ghibli and other projects.

And mostly unknown in the west is Tenmon. Give him a piano and he can break your heart with three notes.

<comment username="CthulhuKid" date="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 17:04:51 +0000" postdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 17:04:51 +0000" editdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 17:04:51 +0000" thumbs="11">
I was taking apart my printed copy of Bios: Megafauna (because I own an actual printed copy now) so that I could use the sleeves for other projects and was set to ditch the paper when I thought, maybe someone in the guild would like them.

So, would anyone like a cheaply printed copy of [thing=97915][/thing]?

You will get:  A deck of paper cards cut by hand.  The card sizes are not uniform, they are meant to be put into sleeves in front of other cards to make their backs uniform.
Two piles of cardstock, one green and one orange with paper glued to one side to be the Mesazoic and Cenazoic tiles.

All will probably fit in a smallish envelope, so I&#039;ll ship it free to the US/Can.  If you&#039;re elsewhere, I&#039;m sure we can work something out.  You&#039;re all nice guys/gals.

Keep in mind, this isn&#039;t well done by ANYONE&#039;S definition.  This was more just so I could play it by hand &#039;cause I loved the game so much.  The printouts are a little blurry, so you may need to reference the Vassal mod if you&#039;re unsure what a card says.  It worked enough for me, though, so if you&#039;re not picky, there you go.  

You&#039;ll need to get yourself quite a few different colored markers for your meeples and either print out a copy of the board or get the Bios: Origins board from Zazzle and play on there (the latter is what I did).

Let me know.  First come first served.  
</comment>

<comment username="Jokemeister" date="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 06:41:20 +0000" postdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 06:41:20 +0000" editdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 06:41:20 +0000" thumbs="4">
[q=&quot;lukather&quot;][q=&quot;Longbombed&quot;][q=&quot;kerskine&quot;]This one:

[url]http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0190374/?ref_=nv_sr_1[/url]

Awful, awful movie[/q]

And I assume many on here had played and were right into D&amp;D at at least one point of their lives as it was such a big thing. I started in &#039;79 and recently got back into 5th edition. I used to watch the cartoon and even liked that. So when this movie came out in 2000, I was so stoked, even though I hadn&#039;t played in years. After watching that steaming heap of... stuff, I was so disappointed. I just couldn&#039;t comprehend why it was so bad. How could anyone let this happen? Everything was so, so bad.[/q]

Never played it. I&#039;ve tried once &quot;Vampire&quot; https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vampire:_The_Masquerade but &quot;table&quot; RPG are weird to me. I mean I just can&#039;t pretend to be someone else sitting around a table with just a player card in front of me, I feel stupid. I&#039;m more of a physical player (boardgames and videogames). And I&#039;m a great books reader...[/q]

The great thing about RPGs is that it can cater to so many different styles of games and gamers.  If you aren&#039;t comfortable pretending to be someone else, then you can just play the character with your own personality.  At that point, you&#039;re not really pretending to be someone else.

Alternatively, there are lots of RPGs with are focused on combat (either abstract or with miniatures) so the RP side is less of a focus.  In fact, that is how we first played D&amp;D as kids.  The GM purchased adventure modules and we would just run around the dungeon causing mayhem and killing orcs, zombies, skellies etc.  At this point, its almost equivalent to a boardgame but with consistent heroes getting more powerful as you play.
</comment>

<comment username="Ibbo" date="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 14:23:17 +0000" postdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 14:23:17 +0000" editdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 14:23:17 +0000" thumbs="4">
Why has there never been a decent D&amp;D style TV series?  The box set era seems ripe for it.  All it needs is a bit of Fugitive, Invaders style weekly adventures with an over-arching storyline tied in with some Game of Thrones style un-sentinmental main character killing offs.

With the popularity of GoT it wouldn&#039;t be a stretch to add a bit in the way of dungeon adventuring.

As an aside, I became very quickly bored with The Chosen One storylines (and I have a feeling lots of people did too) - the lad/lass/hobbit from the prophesy that would be born-to-save-the-world-but-grew-up-not-knowing-it nonsense.  I much prefer every day tale of adventurers having adventures that may or may not be linked style-ee.

</comment>

<comment username="philmcd" date="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 21:54:58 +0000" postdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 21:54:58 +0000" editdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 21:58:47 +0000" thumbs="8">
We had an excellent dungeon master. He turned all the lights off and just had a small torch behind his DM screen to see by, and had a generic sound effect tape playing in the background. We didn&#039;t use maps or minis and he kept track of all the character info. The sensory deprivation meant that there were no visual distractions and we could see the action more clearly in our minds. All we had to focus on was telling him what we wanted to do. It was a truly amazing experience.
</comment>

<comment username="ralsar" date="Sat, 05 Sep 2015 13:26:14 +0000" postdate="Sat, 05 Sep 2015 13:26:14 +0000" editdate="Sat, 05 Sep 2015 13:26:14 +0000" thumbs="4">
I&#039;ve been playing [thing=159228][/thing] on my PS4 lately (on sale right now for $13.49) and it is a pretty fun board game.  It feels like [thing=27627]Talisman[/thing] with all the things I don&#039;t like about Talisman removed.  You get action points for movement instead of random movement.  The map is hex based so you can move anywhere.  It is still very luck based, but you can mitigate your luck with cards and even burn any card to add extra dice to a check.  Even though a lot of the quests and events are random, you still have control over your victory path and decisions.

It evokes an experience similar to [thing=96848][/thing] though much simpler.  The goal is to save the king or kill the king (plus some other ways to win beyond that).  The King hangs out in his castle and causes problems on his turn.  Assaulting the Castle is like attacking a City in Mage Knight.  You have to strengthen your character first before you have a chance to win.  Will you take on a quest?  Explore a dungeon?  Claim a settlement?  Attack another character?  Or other stuff.

It is really quite fun and very much a digital board game.  Also you play big animals.  Check it out!

[IMG]http://cdn.akamai.steamstatic.com/steam/apps/290340/ss_df23796cc6821349698d6b0825ac6d3a016ca589.1920x1080.jpg?t=1441124916[/IMG]
http://store.steampowered.com/app/290340/
</comment>

<comment username="Zouave" date="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 19:04:30 +0000" postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 19:04:30 +0000" editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 22:14:35 +0000" thumbs="7">
Of possible interest. 

http://www.gmtgames.com/p-555-mr-president.aspx

[q]Mr. President is a solitaire game about governing as the President of the United States. It&#039;s not an election game. It begins after you&#039;ve been elected. It&#039;s about sitting in The Chair and trying to advance your agenda while navigating ongoing crises, political enemies, public opinion, your relations with Congress and the press, and keeping your country secure in a world of rival nations and agendas that just seems to keep blowing up around you. Mr. President is a resource management game, where you never have enough resources to achieve your entire agenda, and the path you take through an always unpredictable storyline rests on the choices you make. Depending on the results of those choices, and on the unfolding of a &quot;different every game&quot; story, you&#039;ll either be thinking &quot;POTUS? Piece of Cake!&quot; or &quot;Why was it that I WANTED this job?&quot; many times in each game.[/q]

One nice things about getting a game through GMT&#039;s P-500 system (other than the discount) is that each fall they have a sale that gives you 50% off any of their in-stock games for each game you P-500&#039;ed that year.
</comment>

	<item id="4108257" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="77423" 			
			objectname="The Lord of the Rings: The Card Game"
			username="True_Dave" 
			postdate="Mon, 31 Aug 2015 11:38:54 +0000" 
			editdate="Mon, 31 Aug 2015 13:41:32 +0000"
			thumbs="45"
						imageid="906495">
	<body>Today I tried my hand at deckbuilding, having only previously played &#039;Journey through Mirkwood&#039; using the monosphere decks included in the base game.

I went for a Leadership and Lore deck, mostly because Aragorn was, is and probably always will be, my favourite fictional character. Supporting him I had Theodread and Denethor, with Gandalf showing up when help was most needed (&#039;A wizard is never late, nor is he early, he arrives precisely when he means to.&#039;  It&#039;s true too.)  Maybe not the most thematic group of adventurers, but I thought their abilities would all work well together.

And I romped through the quest, even dispatching an Ungoliantâ€™s Spawn without too much trouble (gotta love the Forest Snare).

I had hoped this game might scratch the Magic: the Gathering deckbuilding itch that I&#039;ve been experiencing lately, and it felt really good to be looking at a fresh set of cards and trying to work out synergies etc.  I guess highest praise I could give is to say that I was looking for some MtG cards on Ebay earlier and quickly switched my search to LotR:CG expansions.

As for waiting; although I had seen Talisman on shelves I never really knew what it was about until GW released their 3rd Edition and ran articles in White Dwarf related to the game.  It really excited me, but as I was only about 15 and didn&#039;t have a proper job, by the time I had saved up the money [thing=1634][/thing] had been released and I bought it instead (because it seemed closer to the WH world, I loved Heroquest and mainly because it weighed more).  It would be another 18 years before a friend of mine would turn up to one of our games days with a copy of [thing=27627][/thing].  We had an absolute blast that day. </body>
	
			
		</item>
	<item id="4109798" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="142638" 			
			objectname="Incredible Expeditions: Quest for Atlantis"
			username="repairmanjack" 
			postdate="Mon, 31 Aug 2015 22:59:53 +0000" 
			editdate="Mon, 31 Aug 2015 22:59:53 +0000"
			thumbs="37"
						imageid="2041633">
	<body>Being in the UK, I&#039;ve had to go on my own incredible expedition to get hold of this; I&#039;m ahead of those poor buggers who kickstarted it only because I bought it from the U.S., via a seller through the geek market. Been unpacking it and thumbing through the cards. The rulebook looks a lot more dense than I&#039;d anticipated, so I&#039;m going to be moving into it during daylight hours tomorrow. (Start the month as you mean to go on...)

First impression: the quality is magnificent. Everything is really robust and sturdy; the card art is gorgeous - unusually so for having live actors in them, but there&#039;s a quality to everything that suggests it&#039;s been in the hands of perfectionists. Ok, the cards are a little thinner than some, but they feel solid enough. Only downside would be my exotic, sculpted dice - which is so warped that it&#039;s unusable. I&#039;ll throw in a spare and see how it goes getting it replaced.

Really looking forward to working through this (and the two expansions). 

[imageid=2649018large]
[imageid=2649019large]</body>
	
			<comment username="Marlowespade" date="Mon, 31 Aug 2015 23:15:57 +0000" postdate="Mon, 31 Aug 2015 23:15:57 +0000" editdate="Mon, 31 Aug 2015 23:15:57 +0000" thumbs="8">
I very much dig this game, and it&#039;s become one of my favorite &quot;quickie&quot; games solo, as I can usually get 2 or 3 games done in 60-90 minutes.

Luckily, the die is hardly ever used in the game (in my experience), so it&#039;s not a huge loss. The game is a lot simpler (especially solo) than the rulebook would indicate, so dive in!
</comment>

<comment username="repairmanjack" date="Mon, 31 Aug 2015 23:23:14 +0000" postdate="Mon, 31 Aug 2015 23:23:14 +0000" editdate="Mon, 31 Aug 2015 23:23:14 +0000" thumbs="3">
[q=&quot;Marlowespade&quot;]I very much dig this game, and it&#039;s become one of my favorite &quot;quickie&quot; games solo, as I can usually get 2 or 3 games done in 60-90 minutes.

Luckily, the die is hardly ever used in the game (in my experience), so it&#039;s not a huge loss. The game is a lot simpler (especially solo) than the rulebook would indicate, so dive in![/q]

I&#039;ll be diving in just as soon as I finish pre-ordering the new Splotter game! Preorders are up on their site. I&#039;m not hunting through the second-hand markets for this one. 

(Antiquity, you will be mine... One day.)

	<item id="4110427" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="94362" 			
			objectname="Rune Age"
			username="Oph1d1an" 
			postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 04:10:52 +0000" 
			editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 04:10:52 +0000"
			thumbs="38"
						imageid="973931">
	<body>So I was perusing Fantasy Flight&#039;s new line of offerings, specifically [thing=181521][/thing] and [thing=181530][/thing]. This led me down a rabbit-trail of FFG&#039;s back catalog where I bumped into Rune Age. I had run into Rune Age in the past and had always decided to pass it up. The game seems to have a very loyal following, but a lot of posts and reviews I saw were pretty &quot;meh,&quot; so Rune Age has always sat just outside my wishlist. But since reading about WH Quest and Runebound got me all fired up for a new fantasy game, and since Rune Age was selling pretty cheap, and since it appears the game is now out of print and probably won&#039;t be as easy to find in 5 years, I decided to go ahead and grab a copy. 

[b]Mini review[/b]
It&#039;s weird that FFG named this as a 2-4 player game when it actually has official solitaire rules built in. And they&#039;re actually [i]good[/i] solitaire rules, not a cheap variant tacked on as an afterthought. 

At its heart, this is a 3-currency, Dominion-style deckbuilder where there are stacks of cards on the table for you to purchase. Some of the cards are race-specific and can only be purchased by the player controlling that race, and some are universally available. Some of the cards you purchase go into your deck; others (namely, cities and strongholds) stay out on the table and give benefits every turn. In the coop scenario, you draw from an enemy deck that does all sorts of nasty things to kill you, and on your turn you fight back to try to survive. Standard stuff, right? But to me, in practice this does not feel like other deckbuilders on the market. For starters, your deck stays small, as cards you draft in are constantly being killed off. In fact, if you don&#039;t watch out, your deck can dwindle to nothing. Second, each race&#039;s set of cards interact in different ways, making you stronger in some aspects of the game and weaker in others. Third, the game does not &quot;autopilot&quot; itself, which a big complaint I have with other deckbuilders. The best choice to make is not always obvious; the game injects some chance into combat encounters, so you&#039;re often called upon to weigh the risk/reward of certain actions vs others. Also unlike a lot of other deckbuilders, the order in which you take your actions makes a [i]huge[/i] difference in your success or failure.

Got its expansion [thing=124300][/thing] on the way, plus a whole buncha card sleeves; I have a feeling this one will be around for a while.

:thumbsup: Official solitaire rules that actually work well.

:thumbsup: The game is scenario-based, so when you are tired of the solo/coop scenarios, you can also recruit some friends to play competitively.

:thumbsup: Feels different from other deckbuilders. You&#039;re doing deck-buildery things, but it feels more like you are playing your own unique deck instead of the whatever was available to smash together.

:thumbsup::thumbsdown: Has a bit of a learning curve. A little more involved than most deckbuilders.

:thumbsdown: Only two scenarios that are soloable, even with the expansion.

:thumbsdown: The scenario decks are pretty thin (maybe 15 cards or so), so not the greatest variety within scnenarios.</body>

I&#039;ve PnP Maquis at the beginning of July. 

[imageid=2589942large]

Resistants used the romans&#039; secret paths - called the &#039;traboules&#039; - all over the city to avoid being spotted by the milice. Very efficient.). 


[imageid=2649295large]

Beautiful countryside, fascinating history, lovely food and quaffable wine - best holiday ever.

<comment username="Bichatse" date="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 19:59:18 +0000" postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 19:59:18 +0000" editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 19:59:18 +0000" thumbs="8">
What a cool thing to do!

If it helps add some authenticity, by coincidence the Maquis du Limousin and the Maquis du Vercors were two of the primary inspirations while I was developing the game - it was largely reading accounts of those groups that determined what kind of missions would feature in the game. For example, I seem to recall that the Limousin group managed to effectively liberate quite a large area on their own before the Allied armies reached them - hence the Liberate mission!

(If you had managed to take the game to Paris as well, you would have covered all the major inspirations - I don&#039;t recall her name off-hand, but the chemist Spare Room is largely the result of reading about a Parisian lady who spent the war making bombs for the resistance in a room above her pharmacy before being caught and executed by the occupiers.)




Despite living so close, I&#039;ve only been to France... three times, I think, myself. Twice to Paris - where I discovered dried apricots in a street market near the bank of the Seine - and once to Caen, in Normandie, as part of a school trip to see the various D-Day beaches, Pegasus bridge and the (supposed) first liberated house in France, and so on.

Unfortunately a rubbish French teacher when I was eleven put me off the language and I switched to German instead for my exams, and I&#039;ve always been very leery about travelling places and just assuming everyone speaks English - it&#039;s kind of arrogant and unfair! More recently - thanks to my Italian partner - I&#039;ve tried Italian instead. She wants to go on holiday to Bretagne or Normandie, though, so there&#039;s still a chance...! (Her mother was even a French-language teacher before she retired.)

(Obviously, I have my own copy already, don&#039;t enter me into the draw!)
</comment>
<comment username="provence" date="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 22:20:09 +0000" postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 22:20:09 +0000" editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 22:20:09 +0000" thumbs="5">
Wow what a generous offer!  I&#039;d love to play this game.

I am both French and American.  I grew up in the Paris suburbs and lived in Provence for a bit before moving to the US.  My grandparents on my father&#039;s side of the family experienced WWII in France and North Africa so I heard resistance stories when I was a kid.

<comment username="koinskyz" date="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 11:22:54 +0000" postdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 11:22:54 +0000" editdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 11:22:54 +0000" thumbs="5">
[q=&quot;Kyuus&quot;]I&#039;ve been to Lyon and loved it. What a beautiful city! We spent a lot of time trying to uncover as many of the traboules as we could. [/q]
Traboules played a major role during the resistance (and all over Lyon&#039;s history. It&#039;s a major reason for the reputation of secrecy of this town during the middle age). 

For those who never heard about that : traboules are a kind of secret paths going from buildings to buildings, almost without going outside. It was possible to enter a building in a street and travel 4 or 5 streets away from the initial door&#039;s entrance without going outside (thus being almost invisible to people searching you). It&#039;s rather hard to clearly explain what a traboule is...

I don&#039;t know how much of the traboules you visited in Lyon, Paul. It depends on [i]when[/i] you visited them.
When I was a child, it was possible to travel from the big central square (place Bellecour) to the Hill of Fourviere (a walk more than a mile long) through traboules going outside only 3 or 4 times. 
Nowadays, most of them are closed for security or privacy purposes. I believe some of them remain, but you visit them with a guide-tour. Sad. I get pretty nostalgic with this evocation, that was so much fun to get lost into the traboules :)
</comment>
<comment username="Kyuss" date="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 11:41:22 +0000" postdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 11:41:22 +0000" editdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 11:41:22 +0000" thumbs="3">
We were there in 1999. I&#039;m not sure whether much has changed since then, but I&#039;m guessing it has. I can&#039;t remember for sure how many we found but there were certainly a few we found once we knew how to recognise them that weren&#039;t in our guide book. Most led through courtyards of otherwise private residences. They were all overground traboules as I believe even then all the underground ones were blocked off. We did do a walking tour of the city that took us through a couple that weren&#039;t otherwise usable.

It must have been an absolutely magical place to grow up with so many secrets awaiting discovery!
</comment>

<comment username="philmcd" date="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 05:05:18 +0000" postdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 05:05:18 +0000" editdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 06:19:29 +0000" thumbs="3">
[q=&quot;Jude&quot;]Long ago, I spent some months living in Paris, and was hoping to be able to move there permanently, but despite my best efforts, I couldn&#039;t get working/residency papers. :(  It&#039;s one of the few places in this world that  I felt at home.[/q]

In 1971 I left school to train as a navigating officer in the merchant navy. For 5 years I travelled the world, seeing exotic places, many of which have now been developed out of all recognition. I just wish I had taken more time to truly experience and appreciate it. There is always tomorrow when you are young, until there isn&#039;t. Sieze the day, my friends.

On this day in 1971 I was in Reunion, a volcanic island in the Indian ocean, east of Madagascar :p

From there we sailed to Townsville, a small town in Queensland, Australia which has since become a major city I believe. The great barrier reef was truly awesome. We had the chance to go snorkelling, which was amazing. Our ship was moored alongside the quay in Townsville while we loaded lead and copper ingots and slabs and I happened to look over the stern, only to see a shark swimming around directly below me. I did not go snorkelling again.

Container ships were only just starting to appear at that time. I was on &#039;dry cargo&#039; ships where everything was lifted out or loaded on pallets. This was a much slower process, and if you were loading or unloading a whole cargo in a single port you could be there for a week in some cases, depending on the cargo. I later worked for BP tankers, where the turnaround time was typically 24-36 hours, not so good for sightseeing.
</comment>
<comment username="ShaunGamer" date="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 09:01:38 +0000" postdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 09:01:38 +0000" editdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 09:01:38 +0000" thumbs="6">
I was born in Townsville, one year earlier.

And yes, I have seen it grow from a small country town to a thriving city.
It is Australia&#039;s 13th biggest population center but as one of Australia&#039;s fastest growing cities, it is expected to overtake those immediately ahead of it.

We still export lead and copper but now we also have nickel, cobalt, zinc and sugar. 
And although we have shark nets in our popular bays, the most dangerous thing in our water is the Irukandji and other Box jellyfish.

I guess that is why we have so many public pools. :shake:


</comment>

<comment username="de_la_poer" date="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 08:31:43 +0000" postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 08:31:43 +0000" editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 08:31:43 +0000" thumbs="7">
It&#039;s a tough little beast. There are 3 small maps / scenarios. France, North Africa and D-Day. I played 15 games and won only 1. But it&#039;s a very good game. The AI is hard and brutal but when you win it really feels like a victory. And it really feels like playing against the game not you vs. you. I like the system of chit pulling battle plans and orders. One of the best AIs I think. The component quality is high but I have the deluxe edition. Never seen the normal one. Not sure if it is what you&#039;re looking for but I would recommend it as an overall game. Maybe there are better ones out there for the Africa part but this is one of my favorite solitaire games. If you have the chance to get it - go for it!
</comment>

I really enjoy this game too. It is not your standard wargame, but the AI is great, and the chit pull battle system is genius. Very tough to beat but always enjoyable to play.

	<body>Played my third game of this solo. I was using the first three expansions: mammas &amp; pappas, advanced visitors, and properties. I got beat so soundly on my first two plays against automa that I played on the easiest difficulty, even though I was using 3 expansions.

Guess what? I... tied automa! I know, that still counts as a loss, but it was my best showing yet. The properties expansion really makes a difference.  I would have won if he hadn&#039;t blocked both the &quot;play a card&quot; and &quot;fill an order&quot; spots on the last turn.

So far, I&#039;m really enjoying this game. Automa is brutal, but brilliant. It&#039;s so simple to implement, and it does a good job of adding uncertainty to the game &amp; keeping each play different. It&#039;s not the same as a real player because you can often predict what a real person will do, and you alternate placing workers with another person. I&#039;m still impressed though.

As far as waiting goes, I just made my first trade offer on BGG this weekend and I gave it a 10 day window. Hoping to get At the Gates of Loyang for Agricola. We&#039;ll see. I haven&#039;t heard anything yet.</body>

			thumbs="41"
						imageid="1063957">
	<body>This arrived on Friday last week and I have spent the weekend learning the (well written and simple) rules. This is another masterpiece by DVG and sits proudly alongside [thing=123955]Thunderbolt Apache Leader[/thing] on my shelf. I have been really enjoying solitaire wargames of late, in particular [thing=67600]D-Day at Tarawa[/thing], TAL, [thing=132028]Awakening the Bear[/thing] (superb) and now this wonderful game. 

The decisions you make just make this such a good game to play at both the strategic level on the main map, and then again on the battle map. The rules are very well written, and the 9 mounted maps give such longevity. So far I matched Napoleon&#039;s efforts in the 1796 Italian campaign, and now find myself struggling against the Marmeluke in Egypt. So looking forward to getting better at this over the next weeks. 

Highly recommended, and for me one of the best solitaire board games you can buy (along with Mage Kinght &amp; TAL). So well designed!</body>

I had taken two enemies out already and carefuly managed my Focus to lure just the Fellstalker toward me.  Then whilst Ghardhak was on his own away from me I had managed to bring him down to 1 HP.

Dodging the Fellstalker&#039;s attack, Ghardhak then closed in and was no longer  open to my attacks whilst the Fellstalker lived.  So came this move:

[center][imageid=2649654medium][/center]

Using the Long Bow&#039;s regular action of dealing 2 damage then Lightning Arrows (all damage becomes magic, +1 damage [i]- 3 magic damage takes care of the Fellstalker -[/i] plus deal 2 magic damage to a different Enemy in the same area) which I then boosted (rightly or wrongly*) with Arcane Bow Mastery (+1 damage) doing 3 to Ghardhak so 1 gets through and finishes him off.

<comment username="Ibbo" date="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 19:34:21 +0000" postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 19:34:21 +0000" editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 19:34:21 +0000" thumbs="3">
Well, it&#039;s still fairly new to me.  I&#039;m currently working my way through each character solo to get a handle on how they play.  There seems to be a fair amount to each characters deck which makes them feel and play a bit different.  Playing solo is hard but very do-able - I can see a real party (2 or more characters) being lots of fun with all the options available.  The card errata is a bit of a pain but hopefully will be fixed soon.  Otherwise I really enjoy it, I like the system of cards and combos and numerous actions plus the cards being your health makes for a tricky balancing act but there&#039;s also a real feeling of progression with attacks getting stronger as you add to your deck.

In my mind it does hold up to Mage Knight comparisons with the emphasis on combat.

I&#039;m look forward to playing this more and eventually then tackling the campaign system.
</comment>

	<item id="4111222" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="154875" 			
			objectname="Silent Victory: U.S. Submarines in the Pacific, 1941-45"
			username="ad79" 
			postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 13:35:11 +0000" 
			editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 15:08:31 +0000"
			thumbs="49"
						imageid="2635114">
	<body>Have had Silent Victory on my table and wrote a session report on it. 

Gonna do a copy/paste here for those not frequenting the games page.

[i](Read this in a hushed tone)[/i]
Let me tell you a story, a story about an American hero, a man that did his duty during WWII, but first, listen to this:

[i](Read this with a movie trailer voice)[/i]
You have already been sunk near the British Isles, depthcharged to oblivion in the Atlantic,  spotted by the aircrafts in the Med, you have failed to survive Gibraltar and you have ended up on the bottom of the Bay of Biscay in June&#039;43. You have even fallen overboard in the Caribbian. 

You have done it, you have failed in every possible way in The battle of the Atlantic, even if you managed to bag the Empress before the flooding forced you to scuttle your boat right into the hands of the Allies, gifting them the Enigma machine and ending your days in a prisoncell in Kent.

[i](Read this like you are approaching the cresendo)[/i]
It is now time to be the Allies. It is time to take the fight to the Pacific. It is time to go hunting [b]the American way![/b]

[i](This you can actually read normally)[/i]
[thing=154875][/thing] is about to set sail.

[i](Que, dramatic voice)[/i]
More subs, more torpedoes, more tubes, more equipment, more missions, more targets, just more, more of everything, even more DUDS! :devil: [i](Evil laughter here)[/i]

[i](And now a sad voice)[/i]
The only thing not here is The Bay of Biscay, but that is actually a thing to be thankful for, because we all hated that Bay.

[i](From now on you can read it like you want to. Even in the voice of your neighbour if you like) [/i]

Let&#039;s get on to the session report. 

[thing=154875][/thing] includes info on 8 famous American subcommanders and includes info on patrols, tonnage sunk, ships sunk and awards recieved. The historical start date is also included which means you will do the patrols during the period of the war the commander operated.

George W. Underwood commanded the Balao Class USS Spadefish from July &#039;44 and he did 3 patrols during the war. 

I stepped into his shoes to try and match his 75,386 tons sunk during those 3 patrols. 

Setup is similar to [thing=113873][/thing] with the exception that this game includes a fancy Patrol map where you can sail around in the actual location of the patrols. This idea I think originated from usercontent made for The Hunters. 

[imageid=2643836medium]
Setup and ready to leave Pearl Harbour to go to the Philippines. 
Yeah, all components for the game are printed on dirtcheap copypapers and is not representative of the final component quality. (Ipad will not be included in the game) The historical captain card are the tan squares in the top of the image.

[i][COLOR=#FF0000]Disclaimer:[/COLOR] I was a proofreader for the game and that is why I have access to the components.[/i]

75, 386 tons is a lot in 3 patrols, so I entered this with a &quot;How am I gonna do this?&quot; attitude.

Transit was peaceful, with not a single airplane or pesky escort in sight. 
Arriving at my first On station box at the North end of the Philippines I spotted a Large Freighter and an Escort alongside it. Take on the escort(which is possible in the game) or go for the sinking and risk the detection roll?
I stayed at Medium range and launched my MK 14 Steam torpedoes, and even if the wake they make gives the Escort an easier time during the day, I go for it. Remember, I&#039;m up against 75, 386 tons so better get cracking.

Hits, no duds and 5700 tons on the logsheet and we exceed test depth to successfully avoid detection. 
Furious calculations about 6 On station boxes, ca. 5000 tons each box should be about 30 00 tons each patrol. Better hit what I spot to catch Underwood, because this is a game of catch up in the early stages.

Box 2 and I spot a convoy during the day, and roll for my 3 ships. 500 tons!!!!! You gotta be kidding me, that is just a small barrel??? Well, there goes my 30000 tons a patrol. 
The two other ships comes up as a 7400 ton Auxillary ship and a large Passenger ship at 5600 tons. 

I ignore the 500 tonner and launches half my torps at each ship. (I like the fact that there are 6 tubes up front in the Balao class)
The Aux goes down with all 7400 tons with a direct hit, but the other one is just damaged.
Escorts spot us and we take some damage, but after fixing our torp doors we go in pursuit and sink it with the Deck gun. 

Two boxes, 3 ships, around 17000 tons. And more importantly, no Duds. 

Third box has 2 rolls and the first one comes up very empty. NO! 
I can&#039;t afford to go without spotting anything. 

Second roll and we are just east of central Philippines. A roll of :d6-1::d6-1:

[b]Capital Ship[/b] WOO HOO!
This game really is a rollercoaster ride.

Roll 20, roll 20, roll 20, NO! No Yamato will be encountered today, no juicy 62 300 tons will be sunk on this day.

We roll and Encounter Hiyo. A 27500 ton Carrier. A smallish capital ship, but a Carrier. Underwood was known as a Carrier killer and gets a to hit die modifier versus these ships. 

We line up our torps, fire and gives it 1 damage, miss, miss, miss, miss and on the 6th torp another damage. 4 left since Hiyo started at 6. We  avoid detection by exceeding test depth. 

Well, now comes the problem. Can we keep up with Hiyo? Capital ships ar no longer automatically followed when damaged. You roll a die and if you roll a 1 you can follow it. What, a 1 to follow? Yes, but you get a -1 on the die for every damage you have dealt it, so with 2 damage already, I will follow on a 3 or less. 

:d6-2: Success. 

Lining up 4 more torps, the first one hits and splits Hiyo in two and it goes down. We did it, 27500 more in the boook. So far a great start.

Take some damage ourself, but gets away after a few rounds of depth charges. 

Encounters a lone 3800 ton Passenger ship which we sink with the deck gun. 
Then we head home, some hull damage, some damaged systems, two torps left and some deck gun ammo, but with 50 000 tons sunk. A sensational start, if I must say so myself. 

[imageid=2648194 medium]
The boat after the first patrol. ( The photographer had a wee too much taste of the celebratory drinks to get a steady camera)

[i][Some observations after the first patrol.
1. The patrol map adds a lot to the experience and it gives you a sense of where you encounter your targets.
2. These boats have a lot more stuff than the Germans in The Hunters. 
3. There are a ton of targets, with lots of variation in both tonnage and type. 
4. Seeing the sub combat mat go to 7 is a scary moment. 
5. This historical scenario thing is awesome. I can already imagine the challenges in the 1 player guild and on the SGoYT.
6. Man there are a lot of Japanese ships with Maru in their name. Could this simply mean ship?][/i]

We spend 4 months in Refit and then head out to the East China Sea for the first of our two patrols there.
25,386 tons left to equal Underwood. 

Transit is again uneventful, first box gives us an easy unescorted small freighter of just 2800 ton. Every little ounce helps, right?

Second bo comes up empty, but luckily we spot a convoy on the first roll in the third box.
1 torp lightly damage a Freighter, 4 torps just barely damages a 10000 tonner Auxillary ship, and the last torp sinks a small 4100 ton freighter. 
Time to exceed test depth, hold on, no exceeding test peth in the China sea, it is too shallow. Ohh, no, imagine meeting a capital ship here...

We survive the depth charges unharmed and follow the Auxillary boat, but Auxillaries can&#039;t be fired upon by deck guns, so even if it ends up unescorted we have to use torps. Fire away from the Aft, and 10 000 tons goes down. 

16700 tons so far this patrol. Now, with only barely 9000 needed to better Underwood, FEAR strikes full flight. What If I&#039;m now sunk, this close to the goal???

We spot a 7300 ton tanker and takes it on, unescorted as she is. Deck guns miss, Aft torps barely damage it and the torps fired from the front missed so much they were probably a bigger threat to fishing boats near Chile, than the Tanker here in the China Sea. 
Roll for additional round of Combat. He who doesn&#039;t dare, are not spotted by escorts, right? 

Lady luck smiles at me and I get a second chance and this time the deck gun hits home. 
74 200 tons, 1,186 tons away from my target, one box left of this patrol. But we have all seen those patrols where all we see are the waves crashing against another wave, endless sea, endless sky and a vast ocean seemingly empty of ships. 
1, 186 tons to go.

Roll for encounter in the last &quot;On station&quot; box. :d6-3::d6-5:

Yes, two ships, but escorted. Hope the target is over 1,186 tons.

Rolling for targets brings up Small Freighter Kori Maru which packs 1 100 tons. You gotta be kidding me??? 
Second target, Large tanker of 10000 tons. Yes. Let&#039;s bring this home!

Completely ignoring the smaller ship, I launch at the tanker. Miss, miss, miss, DUD(my first one), miss(seriously?), and a 1 damage hit. At least I can follow, but no exceeding test depth in the China Sea.

Rolling, rolling, :d6-3:(next one go low!!!) rolling, rolling :d6-2:
Avoided detection, celebratory embarrasing dance, eye rolling from wife, sit down again, launch torps again since the Escort followed.

Booom!!!
84,200 tons. I have managed to beat Underwood. Yeah, more dancing, some serious eye rolling. Sit down. 

What now??? I&#039;ve bettered him after 2 patrols, why go for a third? 

Well, tonnage isn&#039;t all you can match. There are number of ships sunk, and I have so far sunk 10, but that means Underwood has 4 more than me. Next target, ships, lots of ships. 
Ohh, and there is the small matter of decorations. 
Underwood had 3 Navy Crosses for sinking at least 5 ships(or Capital ships) in a patrol.
So I need 5 ships to beat his number of ships sunk, but 5 ships will only match his 3 Navy Crosses, sinking 6 ships can give me more awards. 

[i][Some thoughts after 2 patrols]
1. I hit alot this time.
2. DUDS are on a 1 in this stage of the war, in the beginning of the war they are 1-4. I can only imagine the frustration. 
3. Even when matching the tonnage early on there is more stuff to match. Ships sunk and medals are also a thing to match. And the small matter of surviving, because Underwood did survive the war.][/i]

China sea again.
Transit uneventful. Are there even aircrafts in the Pacific? I do not miss Bay of Biscay in 43. 

Bag a 7600 tonner in the first box and the second box rolls :d6-6::d6-6:

Random event. Bad.

Crew Illness. - 1 to hit. (Insert colorful swearwords here)

Wife: &quot;Did you die now?&quot; 
Me: &quot;No, my crew fell ill.&quot;
Wife: &quot;Ok?&quot; 
Me: &quot;It gives a diemodifier to the To hit table and I am on the hunt for ships because I need to match Underwood&#039;s total....&quot; 
Wife: &quot;Underwood????&quot;
Me: &quot;George W. Underwood, American Sub commander born June 3rd 1910, sailed three patrols and sunk...&quot;
Wife: &quot;Yeah, yeah, go tell someone on boardgamegeek!&quot;
Me: &quot;14 ships...&quot; 

Crew illness is not gonna be good, but I still manage to sink both the 2300 ton Peking Maru(that name again) and a 900 tonner. Ships count now, so everyone is a target. 
Encounter a 10500 tonner and bag that to equal Underwood&#039;s total. 
[b]Take that, Crew Illness![/b]

Second to last box, do not come up empty. Do not dare come up enpty.


SHIP, unescorted. Woo hoo. Boom, Boom. 4400 tons to the bottom. 15 ships. Success. Can I get another one to try and get the Navy Unit Commendation. I will get it on a roll of 1-3 if I sink 6 ships this patrol. 

Last box and two ships turn up with an escort. A massive barrage with all torps is aimed at the 2900 ton Senyo Maru and he goes down in a blace to give me my 16th ship. 
I avoid detection and send a thank you to Lady Luck which have watched over me during dud rolls, detection rolls and even during Escort Attacks. 

I sail uneventful into Pearl Harbour and end my career at 16 ships sunk for a total of 111.900 tons. I&#039;m super satisfied with my performance even if I failed the NUC roll and had to make do with my third Battle Star for successful patrols. 

Me:        111.900 tons, 16 ships, 3 Navy Crosses
Underwood: 75, 386 tons, 14 ships, 3 Navy Crosses. 

I matched awards, and bettered both tonnage and ships sunk. 

Great fun and 7 more Captains to match. 

[i][Thoughts on the game after completing the Underwood scenario.
1. This historical match the captains stuff is brilliant. 
2. While the game (in the late part of the war) can&#039;t match the constant &quot;I&#039;m about to die&quot; feeling The Hunters had, the race for targets, tonnage and awards are cool. 
3. This game is an evolved The Hunters. More targets(720), more subtypes(9), more special missions, patrol maps(in the box) 8 historical captains. Just a lot of stuff. More equipment on the boats, notes on special things on the logsheet(when stuff like radars go into effect)
4. Just a cool experience and I have not tried the frustration of the early war DUD-appaloosa. 

So are there any concerns.
Not much, but I am more famliar with the Battle of the Atlantic than the Pacific subwar, so I more easily get involved in the Atlantic, than in the South China Sea. Therefore, I don&#039;t get the Das Boot feeling I had in The Hunters, but this is a minor thing. I know lots of people have waited for the chance to go out as Americans. 
I missed the Encounter playaid Lines made for The Hunters. That was brilliant and I hope someone makes one for Silent Victory. 
This game screams for an achievement table like videogames do and like the Assassin game from Games Workshop had.
Like this for the historical scenarios:
Survive as Underwood. 
Beat Underwood&#039;s tonnage.
Beat Underwood&#039;s ships sunk.

And like this for the general game:
Survive the war in all types of boats. (9 different)
Be awarded the Medal of Honor
Sink Yamato.[/i]

So, bottom line. I liked the game a lot and look forward to getting the game proper. 

Another hit for Gregory Smith and Consimpress. The game is on p500 with GMT and is expected to ship in November.</body>

	<body>So I got this game last Christmas from my Secret Santa, and although I LOVE it, I have a hard time finding opponents.

Well, the new BattleCON Online Kickstarter (https://www.kickstarter.com/projects/level99games/battlecon-online-the-fighting-card-game-now-online)  got me thinking about this game again a lot, and I decided to pull out the single player Dungeon crawler mode and give it a try.

It was a lot more fun than I expected!  I thought it would feel more tacked on, but there&#039;s a lot to it, with lots of special abilities and items you can buy or find, and lots to think about with the combat, and there&#039;s a lot of replayability here, with several dungeons, and almost 30 characters to try to get through the dungeons using.

So yeah, I&#039;m very impressed, looking forward to playing it more.  I&#039;m not sure why I [b]waited[/b] so long to try the solo mode out.  I highly recommend it.</body>

	<item id="4111617" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="162007" 			
			objectname="Steampunk Rally"
			username="gentle" 
			postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 17:42:42 +0000" 
			editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 17:42:42 +0000"
			thumbs="29"
						imageid="2073821">
	<body>Waiting. Actually a very fitting theme this month. I&#039;m waiting for so many games I backed on kickstarter. When I first discovered kickstarter, I was a bit sceptical but I found a multi purpose tool there that made a great present for a friend of mine. So I backed it. But thats just how I got into it.
Then I discovered the games there. And I went a little crazy. And apparantly, all of the games are arriving this months. The one that took longest will be [thing=150484]Secrets of the lost tomb[/thing], but its shipping already. Hopefully [thing=176524]Hoplomachus[/thing] (Origins. And the lost Cities. And Rise of Rome) will arrive this months, as should [thing=124827]Space Cadets: Away Missions[/thing]...

Thankfully, I don&#039;t back that many games anymore, my wallet had some very serious words with me.

Anyway. The other game I backed back then was this one, Steampunk Rally. And it just arrived today. I had to open it right away and play a test game. First shock: The translucent dice and the metal cogs are missing. Apparently I got a normal retail copy instead of a kickstarter copy with the extras. But alls good, I did ask on kickstarter about it and 5 minutes later the creator had already answered me, saying he was sorry that this happened and that I will get another game, this time the kickstarter copy! Awesome!

Its a racing game. You can play one out of 16 famous inventors (I used Alexander Graham Bell and Albert Einstein) and build steampunk machines for this no-holds-barred race through the Swiss Alps.

The game is divided into different phases. The good thing is, every phase is played simultaneously! So even if you play it with 8 players, it shouldn&#039;t take that much longer than with 2.
First you draft cards which you use to build your machine or get dice or cogs. My machine after a few turns:

[imageid=2649942medium]

Then you vent the machines. The dice you placed there activate them once and then are ballast that you need to get rid off.

Then you actually race. Meaning you place the dice and activate parts of your machine.

You can loose parts, too, because you take damage from cards or terrain.

After the first player has crossed the finishing line, one more round is played. After that round, the winner&#039;s determined.

I only made it about halfway and already my machines had exploded once... Not the worst thing that can happen, you just have to start from scratch and fall back.

[imageid=2649945medium]

There&#039;s a bit of strategy involved on what to build, which dice to get, how many spaces you will move because the terrain might damage or destroy you... And I just love the steampunk theme!


:thumbsup: Great game!
:thumbsup: Rulebook has a lot of examples, after reading it once I didn&#039;t have an questions (so far. I think)

:thumbsdown: No solo rules (at the moment). But its a racing game with hardly any hidden information. Only some of the cards have text that affects the other players. I didn&#039;t mind playing two characters at once and it should be possible to simulate an opponent like in Lewis &amp; Clark.

</body>
	
			<comment username="koinskyz" date="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 18:30:17 +0000" postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 18:30:17 +0000" editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 18:30:17 +0000" thumbs="2">
I gave a closer look to your picture, but was enable to answer. Is there a front and a rear in your machine? [Confusing both could generate a premature explosion during the race ;)]
</comment>
<comment username="gentle" date="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 18:50:27 +0000" postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 18:50:27 +0000" editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 18:50:27 +0000" thumbs="3">
That was a highly experimental machine, built from scratch in just a few moments, meant to put that young upstart Albert Einstein in his place!

The last one did indeed explode, so you might have a point there, hm. Maybe thats why I lost...

In the upper right corner you can see the &quot;main&quot; part of the machine with the picture of Alexander Graham Bell on it. Thats the one part of the machine you can never loose. For everything else, theres these half circles on the cards. They have to connect to at least one other half circle to complete it or you can&#039;t put a new card there.
But you only need to complete one of these circles for it to be allowed. The upper left card is not connected (no half circle on it) to the one below it, but that one is correctly connected to the one to its right. So its allowed :)

So to answer your question: The front part is the one on the right. I don&#039;t have a proper rear machine part in this picture yet, those are all more or less connecting tiles. I still needed a thruster, yes. But it works even with only one tile, you just won&#039;t go very far.

</comment>

	<item id="4111641" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="13122" 			
			objectname="Antiquity"
			username="brrrmanza" 
			postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 17:55:01 +0000" 
			editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 17:55:01 +0000"
			thumbs="31"
						imageid="138460">
	<body>THE friggen&#039; Monolith...

The Wait... an introduction:

Once upon a time, we lived in Philadelphia, PA. I found a great gaming group. We met weekly. Then we started to break out heavier games on the weekend days and dive in head first, while still doing light to medium weight on the weekly Wednesdays. We played High Frontier twice, and the winds of fate called us back home to Ohio. 

Before we left, my friend, [user=tatertot18][/user]  &lt;-- this dude here, was going on a business trip to Canada (the Great North). He mentioned a boutique game shop... one that held new copies of rare euro games, La Valet Äcoeur. He said that they may have Antiquity... Google-fu told me they did!

So I slapped a 100 marked greenback into his hand... and I waited.
It was March. I&#039;d see him in June, at Origins (being Columbus meant it was in my back yard).

It was March, and we packed it all up, and moved in April, and then set it all up again. Shortly sheet the move, I got a picture of the game in shrink! Eeee! It&#039;s gonna happen! Oh wait, the box is too large to fit in my buddy&#039;s carry on! Oh no! Luckily, a coworker is sympathetic to the cause and muled it back to the US for him, for me... and then May came...

... and every day of May, I thought about Antiquity. And then June came. Finally! 
So, it&#039;s Wednesday morning, I&#039;m checking in at registration, getting my Badge. 
I get a text. &quot;I&#039;m here... good news / bad news&quot; and no responses to my reply of &quot;?????!!!??&quot;

I walk across the way, ready to get some gaming on. 
I prepare for dire news.
Apparently, the bus had a leak of water somewhere in the luggage stow. 
He hands me his stack of Star Realms cards, warped, and wet. 
He tells me that his Armada fleets were spared. 
But... Antiquity only fit on the bottom of the suitcase. The foundation sized brick it is...
And the water that destroyed other games... somehow, didn&#039;t (!?!) Kill Antiquity!?!?
He jokes, it must have been the shrink wrap. Well, it must have been. 
The game is bone dry. The box is as pristine as if just off the shelf. 
My eyes melted add I looked upon the brilliance, fellow apes around me shrieked in glory, awe and fear...

We talked about it in February, bid Farwell in March, acquired in April, waited in May, played in June. After traveling from Canada to Philly to my home in CBUS, the eagle had finally landed. 
[The first time I played, we both lost... although I held on for another 4 turns before being strangled under the weight of my own graveyard laden cities].

That was the wait. 

Now, my son is bouncing off of the walls, ready to go to the Park. 

So I guess you&#039;ll have to wait for me too get back and type up my solo play report on this beast of a game. I think I played around 3 hours before I finally crushed the invaders. 



--more later, including pics and the report! :D ;)






</body>

I own both campaign books. 	<item id="4111936" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="142638" 			
			objectname="Incredible Expeditions: Quest for Atlantis"
			username="repairmanjack" 
			postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 20:08:28 +0000" 
			editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 20:08:28 +0000"
			thumbs="33"
						imageid="2041633">
	<body>Lovely new game!

Took the Baroness, along with the Gentleman&#039;s Gentleman (unflappable), a bodyguard, a clergyman, hunter, rigger (cursed) and writer (tossed overboard fairly quickly, actually), on their maiden voyage. Set sail from Port City and immediately encountered a Mirror Dimension; survived that only to shortly end up... um... &quot;Nowhere&quot;. Great success! Surprisingly, I made it to Atlantis, then cheesed it as my boys were too knackered to fight the second encounter. 

Suffered the peril of cramped quarters (hey, all those months at sea...) and some unbelievable phantoms, among other things. Encounters included a Horde of Rats, the beautiful Great Shard Reef, Dreams of Discovery... and the Door of the Living Sacrifice (hence the writer getting kicked overboard).

[imageid=2650070large]

[imageid=2650072large]

It&#039;s a game of two halves: exploration and &quot;resting&quot; which is where you build your crew and resources. In the solo game, you build a market of four possible crewmen and four resources. You can buy s total of four of these things, each round, the rest being discarded. The solo or co-op versions of the game aren&#039;t markedly different from the competitive version - something to be commended. It&#039;s actually fairly simple to learn, although the building up of your resources are what give it its bite, for me. In a four-player game I can see it dragging on, as you&#039;re looking to use your base resources, the deck of cards you&#039;re building, plus any resources or bonuses added by crew you own. Nicely, any crew you buy, you can then use them that same round. So you&#039;re building up some combos to maximise what you can get. 

Initially, I couldn&#039;t see how to afford anything, or survive anything (shades of the tactical play of Shadowrun: Crossfireto be slightly controversial) but it soon swung into view. 

Enjoyed it, a lot, and very happy to have it in the collection. More on this one soon. </body>

I LOVE this game. It&#039;s Vlaada&#039;s other masterpiece and the only non-wargame that I enjoy as much as his Mage Knight.

There is a good vassal module for this game and I also highly recommend boardgamingonline for a very good asynchronous engine.

<comment username="schiavonir" date="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 16:59:55 +0000" postdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 16:59:55 +0000" editdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 16:59:55 +0000" thumbs="1">

<comment username="fortheloveofdice" date="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 17:37:45 +0000" postdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 17:37:45 +0000" editdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 17:37:45 +0000" thumbs="3">
I played my first game yesterday, a 2 player game with someone who knew it pretty well.  The turn order is pretty long so you have to remember quite a few steps but... I wouldn&#039;t say it is a super complicated game, especially if you have a guide.

I wouldn&#039;t start with a full game.  We played the advanced game, which only goes until the end of the second age.  2 player, with setup, teardown, and teaching, was probably 3.5 hours.

Once you get the rules down there is a lot more to the game beyond that, but starting out wasn&#039;t as bad as I feared.
</comment>

<comment username="philmcd" date="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 06:40:54 +0000" postdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 06:40:54 +0000" editdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 06:40:54 +0000" thumbs="3">
[q=&quot;LizzieReads&quot;][q=&quot;schiavonir&quot;]If you like complex civ-builders, DO NOT give up on this one. [/q]

Honestly, I don&#039;t think I&#039;ve ever played a civ-building game, simple or complex. We&#039;ll see how this one goes.  I&#039;m definitely committed to learning it.  [/q]

This game will be too long for some, too complex for others and don&#039;t ever think of playing it with more than 3 players F2F, even 3 is a stretch F2F, but a great experience IMHO.

But if you like this game you will almost certainly love it. The ultimate civ game IMHO.

Tough to learn from the rulebook, not so much if you are taught, and harder still to play well, but so rewarding.

Probably the most unforgiving game I&#039;ve played as you can drive your nation into a dead end, but once you get the hang of it it becomes intuitive.

Enjoy !
</comment>

	<item id="4112006" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="85000" 			
			objectname="We Must Tell the Emperor"
			username="SBGrad" 
			postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 21:18:35 +0000" 
			editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 21:18:35 +0000"
			thumbs="21"
						imageid="847142">
	<body>
After a game of Malta, I naturally had to pull out its stablemate.  Although the battles are better in Malta, I think I prefer Emperor more.  In Malta, you are 100% of the defensive the entire game.  The Early War deck in Emperor is glorious, as the player smashes through one front after another.  Pretty much your only chance at victory in Emperor is to knock out 3 fronts.

Unfortunately, I had bad die rolls, and never really got any front too close to knock out.  The Solomons Islands fortification held up Nimitz until the last card of the game.  I was doing OK, even had Oil maxed out after the initial Sub card came into play.  

But in the Late Deck your resources melt away like snow in Death Valley and this game was no different.  Not to mention that a very nasty card, &#039;B-29 Fire Raids&#039; get reshuffled back into the deck, meaning you can be bombed again and again.  For maximum pain, I was also playing with the expansion deck.

With 10 cards left in Late War, the Brits and Chinese got to Japan Home Islands, but in the Resources Phase every single track went to 0 and that was the end of the game.</body>
	
			
		</item>

	<item id="4112116" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="146652" 			
			objectname="Legendary Encounters: An Alien Deck Building Game"
			username="Turbine2k5" 
			postdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 22:14:56 +0000" 
			editdate="Tue, 01 Sep 2015 22:14:56 +0000"
			thumbs="24"
						imageid="2225180">
	<body>Alright, so it&#039;s my turn to take on the evil Aliens. I started out as the Scout against the 1st movie. Things went pretty well, as I was able to get &quot;Last Survivor of the Nostromo&quot; and &quot;Consult the Star Charts&quot; before the end of the first objective. That, and &quot;Mu-th-ur&#039;s Advice&quot; really boosted me through the game. &quot;Teams of Three&quot; and &quot;You Have Your Orders&quot; are really powerful together. This allowed me to pull a ton of good cards into my deck and to take down that &quot;Perfect Organism&quot;.
[imageid=2650187 large]
Only pulled 3 strikes the whole game, and one went away because of &quot;Jonesy&quot;. I&#039;ll say that this is slightly favorable to Predator in a few ways. All of Predator&#039;s Role cards only trigger with Brothers in Arms abilities (each card Coordinated to you on your turn), so playing solo means they&#039;re only good for their Attack values. The second Predator movie has an objective where you have to discard the top card of everyone&#039;s draw pile, and only completes if there&#039;s as much Attack as there is money, else you draw a strike. It&#039;s almost impossible solo, but I still have three movies here so we&#039;ll see if I run into any single-player snags.</body>

	<body>Score: 17 (not so great)

[floatleft][ImageID=2647905][/floatleft]Got in a play of my favorite PnP game. Love the mix of theme and intricate gameplay in this one. Top notch, IMO. It uses dice in a unique way as a resource, but other resource options are available as well. You&#039;ve got to build up your movie empire to become one of the top studio heads in the business.

[floatright][ImageID=2647908][/floatright]I started out by greenlighting a low budget Historical film. I wanted to get some resources built up so I could lure some higher profile writers, directors and other industry big shots to my studio. I put my only star actor in the film hoping to improve my returns.

Meanwhile, I negotiated to get some extra help on board: a writer who knew some other folks looking to make and Adventure flick and some crew to help reduce production time. I got that one into the production schedule just behind the Historical pic, which released to a solid box office return and some future earnings.

Next on the docket was a mainstream Romance with the help of another writer with a sought-after script. My timing seemed to be good too, as the popularity of the genre was beginning to skyrocket. I just hoped the fickle public would hang on until its release.[clear]

[center][ImageID=2647910medium][/center]

Both the Adventure and Romance films did well, allowing me to start schmoozing some of the big name directors and actors to my side of the fence. However, their specialties were not in the public&#039;s eye, so I had to wait it out a bit.

[floatleft][ImageID=2647911][/floatleft]I needed to start looking for bigger payouts if I was going to hang with the big boys, so I set up a cross-genre Historical Adventure film. Unfortunately, I had to cut the budget down from my initial desire for it to be a huge, epic, cinematic extravaganza down to a mid-level mainstream movie.

[floatright][ImageID=2647906][/floatright]It paid out well upon release and gave me several months of incoming revenue, but the critics didn&#039;t quite go for it. My Fame was not increasing as I had hoped. And by now, the major movie season was winding down. The public&#039;s interest was beginning to wane.

I quickly threw a Musical together and got it out into the theaters, but it only received middling interest from moviegoers.

In the end, my Fame was only subpar. Without one or two big epics to my name, my time as a movie studio head would soon be forgotten. </body>

<comment username="reverendunclebastard" date="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 04:54:50 +0000" postdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 04:54:50 +0000" editdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 04:54:50 +0000" thumbs="2">
[q=&quot;davekuhns&quot;]So I have 31 undiscovered tiles. 14 points from the 2 cairns and eskimo. Am I right saying I discovered 6 islands? I think the rulebook says it&#039;s ok if the map edge is a border. That means 6 points for a &quot;set&quot; of 5+ discovery tokens of one kind (you still get that in the solo). So that&#039;s 20 points. 
The islands themselves are worth 4+4+3+1+1+1 correct? That&#039;s 14. +10 for getting to the Passage by the fourth turn. So I&#039;m up to 38 points? -31 would be 7. 
Did I miss anything?

Are the straits and Franklin wreckage worth it?[/q]

You almost have it! The islands are correct (edge of the board does count). The &quot;set&quot; score is incorrect, it is not 6 points for 5 discovery tokens of one kind, it is 6 points for each complete set of 5 different discovery tokens (i.e. 1 cartography, 1 strait, 1 Franklin, 1 Inuit and 1 cairn). That is what makes the strait and Franklin tokens worth picking up.

So your final score would be 14 for islands, 10 for the passage, 14 for picking up the 2 cairns and one Inuit. That is 38 minus the 31 for missing tiles equals 7. You forgot to add the 6 points that you weren&#039;t allowed when doing your math anyway!


</comment>

<comment username="masil" date="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 10:58:32 +0000" postdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 10:58:32 +0000" editdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 10:58:32 +0000" thumbs="2">
[q=&quot;wery67564&quot;]The bots appear to be the most difficult bit in the ruleset :/[/q]

Yes, the wording of the bot priorities are at times extremely condensed and some bot actions just simply are quite complex (NVAbot March, USbot Assaul/Sweep with Airlift in particular).

Another stumbling block might be the general bot instruction in 8.1 through 8.4. There&#039;s been quite a bit of discussion of late in the FitL forums about the precise import of some of these for example in conjunction with the flowcharts.

On a positive note, you won&#039;t have to get every single detail of each bot action absolutely right (I probably rarely do) to have a challenging and enjoyable solo experience.

Finally, something that gamers new to the bots often miss is that victory works somewhat differently in a game involving the bots than in a all players game. Basically, the player cannot win other than by the victory margin at the end of the last (truncated) Coup round, whereas the bots can win at the start of any Coup round.

</comment>

		</item>

	<body>I just published the latest blog post about my ongoing campaign in [b][thing=149787][/thing][/b]. [b][blogpost=45487][/blogpost][/b] Unfortunately, between that and another game I can&#039;t talk about yet, I&#039;ve been really stretched for time this past month, and will be for the next couple of weeks at least.

However, I am making sure to take time to play the games in the [b][thread=1293768][/thread][/b]. The deadline to vote is coming up soon, and since I have a game in the contest this year, I want to play as many of the other games as I can.

So far, I&#039;ve been able to try out 3: [b][thing=181560][/thing][/b], [b][thing=182086][/thing][/b], and [b][thing=182047][/thing][/b]. The second one didn&#039;t grab my interest, but the first and the third are real winners in my book. Iwanna&#039;s is a great puzzle-style game driven by a mancala or rondel mechanic, and it&#039;s got a great theme attached. I&#039;ve been playing it on Vassal, since my grayscale printer couldn&#039;t do it justice. Austerity has an equally clever theme and is one of those new &quot;bag-building&quot; style games. It&#039;s super easy to build, and I will definitely be playing it again.

On that subject, I&#039;m planning to do a collection of micro-reviews of the contest games on Entropy. When I did a similar post covering previous years, I had a great guest reviewer in Morten Monrad Pederson, and I&#039;d love to share the spotlight again for this year&#039;s contest. Is there anybody out there who would be interested in collaborating on some mini-reviews of print-and-play games, to be compiled and published this weekend?

Finally, while I highly suggest you try out the two games I highlighted above, I&#039;d also love any feedback on my contest entry, [b][thread=1395780]The Death Worms of Qinesh[/thread][/b]. It&#039;s 3 pages of printed materials with some minor cutting required, and you&#039;ll need some extra euro cubes and d6&#039;s. The central concept is dice allocation: you roll a pair of dice and decide which to allocate to your defensive barrier, which gets tested every 6 rounds, and which to allocate to your action points for picking up and rescuing refugees. I&#039;d be really keen to hear how it feels to others.

On the subject of waiting, guess what FINALLY arrived late last week? I&#039;ll be anxiously waiting for the days when I have the free time to really dig into it.

[imageid=2650539 medium]</body>

	<item id="4112570" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="142084" 			
			objectname="Kings of Israel"
			username="Malaiser" 
			postdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 05:38:25 +0000" 
			editdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 05:38:25 +0000"
			thumbs="32"
						imageid="1719406">
	<body>I played my first game of this today.  I was relatively easy to learn and the game flows rather smoothly.  I&#039;ve heard this compared to Pandemic and it was hard to break out of the Pandemic mindset at first.  When I started the rules and saw that there were altars, I figured they worked like research stations.  Nope, they did something completely different.  I would say that this game plays similarly to Pandemic but it is definitely not a re-skinned version of the game.

Here&#039;s how the game works.  Because the Israelites fail to follow God, sin creeps up and threatens to overwhelm Israel.  You play prophets through the generations to preach God&#039;s word and try to help keep Israel on the right path.  You win if you are able to build enough altars but lose if all the sin cubes run out, the idols are all placed on the board, or you reach the end of the time track and haven&#039;t won.

Kings of Israel is based on Israel&#039;s early history.  The time track on the side works it&#039;s way through Israel&#039;s Kings.  It starts with Saul and ends with Hoshea.  He was Israel&#039;s last king and the ruler when Assyria conquered Israel and the Israelites were exiled.  It&#039;s very interesting to see Old Testament history laid out like this.  I also found it very fun to see where all these cities were, on a map. When I read through the Old Testament last year, it was pretty tough to visualize where everything was.

I really enjoyed this game.  I won pretty easily, but I think that is for two reasons.  I made a few rules mistakes, and I was playing the normal game.  There is an expert game in the rules, and I&#039;m pretty sure that is how the game is meant to be played.  I was pretty cool because at the beginning of the game, it felt like I was going to win easily, but as the game went on and things got harder, it stopped feeling like victory was eminent.

Here is the board at the end of my game.

[center][ImageID=2650203medium][/center] 

There are a couple of really cool things that happen with the king&#039;s track on the side of the board.  At the end of every round, you move the tracker down to the next king.  If it&#039;s a good king you get to draw a blessing card, basically a good event.  However, if it&#039;s an evil king, you draw a sin and punishment card, basically a bad event.  There are also some kings who had very short reigns, and they basically give you two bad events in a row.

I liked the game on my first play, and I look forward the next plays.  I&#039;ll be curious to see if this and Pandemic both belong in the same collection, but they feel different enough, at first glance, that they just might.

Here&#039;s a cool thing.  The card art for the location cards comes straight from the map.  I was able to lay the card on the board and the artwork matches up perfectly.  I always think that kind of thing is fun!

[center][ImageID=2650205medium][/center]</body>

	<item id="4112624" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="125046" 			
			objectname="Fantastiqa"
			username="EndersGame" 
			postdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 06:54:19 +0000" 
			editdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 06:57:19 +0000"
			thumbs="38"
						imageid="1321261">
	<body>I&#039;ll bashfully admit that I&#039;m not normally one to play games solitaire.  But I enjoy Fantastiqa a great deal, so when I came across a solo variant recently, I just had to give it a shot. Short version: I loved it, and have played it almost ten times already in the last few weeks!

For those not familiar with Fantastiqa, it&#039;s a game by Alf Seegert, whose design credits include Road to Canterbury and Musee.  While the game is often described a deckbuilder with a whimsical theme, the real gameplay happens as you move your adventurer on a board, subduing creatures, which then get added to your deck. You can also purchase artifacts and beasts to make your deck more powerful. Points are earned by going on quests. It has a whimsical theme, but definitely captures the feel of adventuring around, and feels much more like an adventure game than a deckbuilder.  I&#039;ve seen it described as a kind of Mage Knight lite, so maybe that gives you an idea of what to expect.  Alf is an English professor, and has drawn extensively on various literary influences in the game, which gives more to appreciate about it.  To find out more, check out my [thread=989982]pictorial review[/thread].

[imageid=2618619 medium inline]

Now on to the solo variant. It&#039;s the one posted by Sky Zero here:

[b][thread=1096944]&quot;Uriel&#039;s Robe&quot; Fantastiqa Solo Player Variant[/thread][/b]

I&#039;ve tried several variants for the game so far, and this is easily the best.  In some respects it is even more fun than a standard multi-player game, because you really need to make skilful tactical use of cards with special abilities like the key icon to access statues, and the magic carpet icon to travel, and cycle through your deck to find the cards you need.  And when using the Creature deck as an end-of-game timer as I do, you really get to have fun with the deck you&#039;ve crafted.

The variant isn&#039;t perfect and still needs some minor polishing.  I&#039;ve come up with my improved version [url=https://www.boardgamegeek.com/article/20124954#20124954]here[/url], and no doubt it can benefit from ongoing tinkering.  But it&#039;s a fantastic way to enjoy the game, and I look forward to playing it more often.  Highly recommended!

[imageid=2621039 medium inline]</body>

<comment username="EndersGame" date="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 14:11:55 +0000" postdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 14:11:55 +0000" editdate="Wed, 02 Sep 2015 14:11:55 +0000" thumbs="9">
[q=&quot;davekuhns&quot;]Ender, would you recommend getting this game if it was almost exclusively for solo? [/q]
[floatright][imageid=2617270 inline][/floatright]Good question.  Even though it still needs a little more polishing perhaps, the Uriel&#039;s Robe variant is really fun.  I&#039;ve played it more than half a dozen times already, and had enormous enjoyment out of it.  Several other gamers have found the same. In fact, most times I&#039;ve played it I just wanted to keep on playing!   

Fantastiqa is more of an adventuring game than a deck-building game, so it really lends itself to solitaire play like this. I&#039;m not that familiar with Mage Knight, but I gather that it plays quite well solo, and I&#039;ve seen Fantastiqa described more often as a whimsical and lite Mage Knight.  

The game itself doesn&#039;t come with an official solitaire variant.  It should also be noted that original form of the Uriel&#039;s Robe variant did need some tweaking.  But several suggestions have since been made for refining and polishing it, and the person who came up with the variant plans to play-test some of the ideas I&#039;ve suggested and develop it further.  Even in its current form it works quite well.  One advantage of the Uriel&#039;s Robe variant is that it doesn&#039;t change the game rules much.  

My only concern would be whether replayability would be an issue if only playing Fantastiqa solitaire.  Then again, I&#039;ve played the solo variant about 7 or 8 times already, and I&#039;m long not sick of it. For most people, even that many plays (about an hour each time) might be considered worthwhile.  One additional consideration is that in some respects the solitaire form of the game is almost more fun than a multiplayer game.  It offers an excellent challenge that requires clever skilful and tactical play in ways that a 2-4 player game doesn&#039;t offer, and that makes it very rewarding.  

So I could imagine some people being quite happy with a Fantastiqa purchase simply for solo play only.
</comment>
