	<body>I&#039;ve just got back from a long weekend over the Bank Holiday in the UK. We went up to our cottage in the Lake District. As the name might suggest it can sometimes rain a lot so I took along Space Infantry in case the weather was particularly inclement. I figured I&#039;d easily get a campaign done as the missions are so quick. In the end the weather conspired against me and was absolutely glorious so I only got two missions done. :)

The first mission was a disaster. The squad needed to find 4 missing scientists in some caves and had been given the Pilum ATV to assist getting around the surface of the planet. What they hadn&#039;t been told was that the pilot had only recently passed his driving test, and that he&#039;d learned in a milk float and this was his first time driving an ATV. Basically, I failed so many Pilot tests that progress was painfully slow! Tactically I should have aborted the mission to avoid the -1 VP for failure, but after so many poor chit pulls for Pilot checks I kept on convincing myself that the next pull had to be a good one!

The second mission was much more successful. It was a reconnaissance hive mission exploring a Beastmaster lair. I took along a Scout and lots of Intelligence resources and medkits. I like to try and keep moving in hive missions. I got very lucky with an early Intel cache and was able to whiz through the tunnels with minimal resistance. I did have an extremely tough fight on the final Resource Node, which saw everyone getting injured and the hapless Scout being killed, but it wasn&#039;t enough to stop the rest of the squad surviving the successful mission. After the first mission fiasco I was finally able to grant some of the squad Veteran status.

I&#039;ll try and finish the campaign before I get back into Empire of the Sun.

I took a panoramic photo in a spot that is about 5 minutes from our house. Hopefully it conveys why even I didn&#039;t really want to be inside playing games...

[ImageID=2650695 large]</body>

	<item id="4112844"

			objectname="Field Commander: Rommel"
			username="de_la_poer"

						imageid="1096391">
	<body>I played 2 games today. North Africa again, both times. The biggest problem here (I think) is that the longer the game runs, the tougher it gets to take over that egyptian area. So I tried to take my two Pz units and run for egypt. The other units have to take the fortress asap so that new units can come into play from there.

First game was chaos. Turn 3, both Pz units destroyed and tons of allied units on the map. Let&#039;s start all over again.

[ImageID=2650697 large]

Second game was better. My two Pz units were the killing machines again that I am used to. I decided to take my supplies for battle plans instead for movement. Mistake! I could not reach the fortress this way and rolled the worst thing in the allied round. Add units to fortress tobruk. Two times!

[ImageID=2650698 large]

Anyway, do you see what I saw? Yep. My two Pz units were in reach for the two units in egypt. And those were the last units in the egyptian area. I decided to head for them instead of the fortress, take the egyptian objectives AND defend them. Haha...

[ImageID=2650699 large]

Crazy thing happened. The 1st Arm was a laugh but the 5th Ind got another unit for help AND even pushed me back to where I came from.

The fortress tobruk allies were about to attack and even kicked me out of that area. Exploited after that but I stopped them the next round. Wounded.

New reinforcements in all areas. The fortress units were hunting my units in the west and the new guys in the east were out for blood and destroyed me right there.

[ImageID=2650700 large]
[ImageID=2650701 large]

This mission is hard! D-Day is even harder you say? :arrrh:</body>

<comment username="HamsterOfFury" date="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 10:11:43 +0000" postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 10:11:43 +0000" editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 10:11:43 +0000" thumbs="5">
[q=&quot;fortheloveofdice&quot;]How long does this game take to play?[/q]

I find that a &quot;week&quot; of play takes maybe 10-20 minutes. I tend to play a few weeks in a go but I find that the game rolls along quite nicely and suddenly I realise I&#039;ve been playing for 2 hours.

You can take a break whenever you want, but the end of each week is quite a natural pause. It&#039;s like the Football Manager computer game - play for as long or short a time in one sitting as you want.
</comment>
<comment username="masil" date="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 10:50:48 +0000" postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 10:50:48 +0000" editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 10:50:48 +0000" thumbs="7">

I started my first season a couple of days ago, so I&#039;m a beginner. I tend to be interrupted in my gaming quite a bit (by various members of the family) so I find it difficult to give a time-frame as to how long a week takes to play. However, in terms of the rules and procedures, it&#039;s not a complex, laborious process to get through a week, so I think the designer&#039;s 10 to 20 mins sounds about right even for a beginner.

Furthermore, the amount of stuff to do and think about changes every week so the time you consume changes accordingly.

Also, as Al notes above, this really is an easy game to get on the table ---print out a good chunk of paper, get a d6 and a pen is all that&#039;s needed, no cutting out cards etc whatsoever--- so you don&#039;t lose much time or effort by giving it a try.

On the other hand, it seems to me that you&#039;ll get progressively more and more depth out of the gaming experience the further you progress in the season or as your team gets promoted (or not!) to higher divisions. So in that sense you&#039;ll be investing time into the game, although at that point you&#039;ll probably be wanting to make that investment anyway.

I&#039;m loving the game and plan to write a SGOYT entry at some point this month.

</comment>
<comment username="Al_Shrew" date="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 13:21:02 +0000" postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 13:21:02 +0000" editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 13:21:02 +0000" thumbs="2">
Hey Masil, Glad to see you took the plunge and gave it a try. First impressions do you like it as much as TOS?
</comment>
<comment username="masil" date="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 18:29:30 +0000" postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 18:29:30 +0000" editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 18:29:30 +0000" thumbs="4">
[q=&quot;Al_Shrew&quot;]Hey Masil, Glad to see you took the plunge and gave it a try. First impressions do you like it as much as TOS?[/q]

Well, Al, that&#039;s a very interesting question. One thing is certain: in no way is FM inferior to TOS. Sure, ToS looks great but they are both well oiled games.

There are a couple of things that stand out in FM for me. To me it feels like an epic game in which you develop your team from ground up and follow its journey from the humble beginnings to glory. In theory, I guess you could play the game forever. You&#039;re more involved and developing the players through the kind of training you expose them to, I like that a lot. Also, I quite like the ability to adjust tactics mid-game so a match is not just about to tossing the dice. There&#039;s [i]a lot[/i] of tossing the dice in FM, although its mostly minor tweaks to the overall machine so no particular roll feels big in itself.

</comment>

	<body>I played 2 games of this after work. I&#039;d only played [thing=37380][/thing] previously and I think I prefer this to that game. The build in solo rules are basically play 8 rounds and try to beat 100 points or your previous highest score.

[b]Game 1[/b]
I wasn&#039;t really sure of what I should be trying to get first (extra dice/goods/food) or what to build. I ended up with a mixture of everything.

Completed:
4 monuments for 25 points
5 developments for 16 points
no bonuses or wealth
19 tribute
5 disasters

Total: 55 points

Not bad for my first attempt but well off the target.

[b]Game 2[/b]
The second time I realised that I would need as many dice as I could get to build monument and developments. unfortunately the dice do not always roll the way we want them to and in getting extra dice I was not using workers for monuments. I also played 2 rounds with 1 fewer dice than I should have had but I couldn&#039;t remember what I had done in those 2 rounds to undo the actions so I just took the hit of not using that dice for those rounds.

Completed:
2 monuments for 19 points
6 developments for 31 points
no bonuses
22 tribute
7 disaster

Total: 65 points.

:thumbsup: - Quick dice game.
:thumbsup: - Fun to play.
:thumbsup: - Solo plays the same as multiplayer (with one or two minor exceptions).
:thumbsdown: - Box doesn&#039;t include a pencil/marker yet it is required to play the game.
:thumbsdown: - I don&#039;t like games that include sheets you need to write on as I always worry that I will run out of them at some point. I know you can print your own sheets but I needed a second :thumbsdown:</body>

[b]Game:[/b] 1/3
[b]Difficulty: [/b]1 Drone per objective
I&#039;m on a roll with this game having won 3 in a row.  This movie is definitely tougher than the first.  The aliens advance quickly.  At one point in the game both avatars were a bad strike draw away from death.  Once I got the sentry guns setup it was smooth sailing from there.  The Queen appeared pretty quickly and I was prepared.
[IMG]https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/NRr3L0gkk_HSdG9P61xoEYkp9KUHJsJvCIPNXiO-LXM=s400[/IMG]

:star: This game really shines at telling a story and creating a tense atmosphere.  No other card game I have played come close in that aspect.

[b]Game:[/b] 2/3
[b]Difficulty: [/b] 0 Drone
4th win in a row.  I&#039;m starting to wonder if I&#039;m cheating :)  I played as the Medic and Commander.  The Commander&#039;s ability to gain a cost 3 card came in very handy early on.  I was able to gain a lot of Critical Analysis cards.  Discard a card from your hand and draw 2.  I had three in one hand at one point.  Very powerful when you can string them together.  I really like the cards from this movie.  Out of the first three movies this is my favorite to play.  My end two turns alowed me to draw a lot of cards when ended up giving me a MAJOR victory.  Well, that&#039;s what I&#039;m calling it any way.  27 combat to kill the Queen.
[IMG]https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/XV7aRl54j6vESXjpDaAlinn2auFITMmkxY5_IBfxsKY=s800[/IMG]

[b]Game:[/b] 3/3
[b]Difficulty: [/b] 0 Drone and 1 Hive card in the complex
There are some games, like my 2nd play of this movie, where everything works out perfectly.  The cards you want are in the HQ and you always have enough recruit points to gain them.  You always seem to have enough attack to scan and keep the aliens at bay.  Class/crew abilities are constantly activated for bonuses.  The events and hazards appear at the least impactful moments.  This was NOT that game...
[IMG]https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/MGrTZTBJkkNsWFGKzCXnWhDC-TRMfOT5MflMtaiNgQY=s800[/IMG]

I was able to hold off the queen for three rounds in the combat zone.  Body armor helped.  But it didn&#039;t matter how much attack I could generate anyway.  I could not get enough recruit to rescue the character which had to be done before attacking the queen.  I can attribute my loss to 3 things:
1 - gaining attack cards early rather than recruit.
2 - lack of cohersion in my decks.  I rarely had any combos
3 - due to 1 &amp; 2 I was unable to gain the cards that I really needed.  Which leads to the real reason for my loss...
[size=18]weak hands[/size]
[IMG]https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/FHUd5vzQM_q7B3wwWsJXZUi_587WMCpOYndEIB7Nvdg=s800[/IMG]

:star: I should really just add Mage Knight to my Hall of Fame list and call this my #1.</body>

I can see why people would not like this game but, for me, it&#039;s a perfect morning game. Plays in an hour, lots of stuff happening, good decisions with pushing your luck. The extra rules regarding fireproof doors and bulkheads were cool too (although I only had 1 fireproof door activate; and it worked!)

Glad to own this :)</body>

	<body>Ok I played the game that got me introduced to Victory Point Games. 
Played 3 games of this so far today. This is the second edition. 

The first two games were without any of the optional cards. 

I got my highest so far with just the regular cards in my first game as I scored 45 points. Things were pretty dicey most of the game but I held off until the end to score a minor victory.

The second game lasted only 5 turns as I pretty much got bum rushed by the Zulus and was unable to hold them off. Did score 20 points though as I did take some of them out.

For my 3rd game I added all the optional cards which can help you score more points but you have to subtract 1 point for each card you add so you start with -19 in the hole adding all 19 cards. Playing this way it seems like a victory just to survive to the nighttime. I did survive until the night but was overran soon after. Scored 18 points but after subtracting my 19 points I ended up with -1.
I think the most I ever scored playing this way was like 7 or 8 points and I don&#039;t think I ever made it to the end.

<comment username="reverendunclebastard" date="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 04:50:33 +0000" postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 04:50:33 +0000" editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 04:50:33 +0000" thumbs="1">
[q=&quot;Al_Shrew&quot;]I bought these in bulk [imageid=2657056] as I had a few games to sleeve at the same time.

It&#039;s acceptable, but I do plan on upgrading to a premium, thicker sleeve. When this geek list stops making my buy games.

[imageid=2657057]

I use those sleeves too (for LE: Alien/Predator, D-Day at Tarawa and Star Trek: Five Year Mission). They are not perfect but I paid $0.79/100 sleeves. This meant I could sleeve, for example, Predator (700 cards) for less than $6. With fancier sleeves (that run around $4/50 sleeves) that would have cost me $56! I would rather deal with less than perfect sleeves for $6 than spend enough money to buy another game to get perfect ones.
</comment>

						imageid="992459">
	<body>Tonight I played the Cold Front scenario (#5) as the Germans against the Russians.  Immediately I knew that the placement of trenches was critical in order to deal with the massive number of Russian Elite troops that were going to storm my way.  I positioned a few trenches near the only bridge crossing the river, and with the snow on the map, each &quot;clear&quot; hex had an additional 1/2MP cost, so I figured I&#039;d be able to take some liberties with clearing them out.  I split my troops through with a few positioned towards the mid/high part of the map in case they tried to come around and flank or exit my side of the map.  Sounds like I had a plan... and then all hell broke loose.

I was able to take pot shots at the Russians, taking out troop after troop as they approached the bridge, but towards the bottom of the map, they made their way out of LOS so I couldn&#039;t get a bead on them.  Meanwhile the Russians towards the top &quot;camped&quot; out in the warmth of the buildings and repositioning for an assault.  

Unfortunately you can&#039;t use OPfire against the Advance cards, and the Russians were able to advance a troop into the trench where I was and killed my rile team in melee combat, taking over a critical position on the map.  From there it just got worse and worse.  My other team was too far out of position to help, and the reinforcements from the Russians started to push on the top of the map, crossing the frozen stream and heading for me.  Eventually the Germans surrendered after receiving too many casualties. </body>

			objectname="VivaJava: The Coffee Game: The Dice Game"
			username="Malaiser" 
			postdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 03:46:55 +0000"

			thumbs="17"
						imageid="2089536">
	<body>I played this the other day, and since I was learning the rules, I played a two-player game. I simply played both sides. I really enjoyed it because there was a lot of decisions to be made regarding research. When to spend your dice to create a blend (which gives you points) and when to spend your dice on research (which improves your dice rolling).  

Tonight I played the solo game. It seemed like it would be pretty cool. The two solo opponents have different abilities which is a nice touch, and I went up against Sacchar, Inc. I also thought I would just start out on normal. I got creamed. I lost 21-14. The AI was a points machine. 

Maybe I should have started on easy, so I played again. I got just as thoroughly ground into dirt. I lost again 21-14. 

Now that might not seem like such a terrible defeat, but the AI was always in the lead and there was never any doubt he wouldn&#039;t win. 

I feel like I&#039;m doing something wrong. There wasn&#039;t really any of the decisions about research or blends that I liked so much in the two-player game. It was a simple go as fast as you can to keep the AI from scoring all those points. 

Does anyone, who&#039;s played this, have any advice? I&#039;m pretty sure I played the rules correctly. Maybe there is a common mistake I didn&#039;t realize I made. 

[b]Edit 1[/b]
I played three more times this morning.

[u]Play 1[/u]: This was a much more fun play of this game.  I played against OMNIBlend Transglobal, and won!  It was really close, I won 21 - 19, and eeked out the win on the last turn. I completed the yellow research (Flip Bean) which pushed me to 21. Yes!  Gary was right, OMNIBlend is a much easier opponent.

[u]Play 2[/u]: I went for it again, and won again.  This time it was even closer.  I won 21-20.  I was able to snatch the Featured Blend out from under Topps at the last minute and take the victory.

[u]Play 3[/u]: Because this game is so quick, it went for another round.  This time I wanted to try out something strange.  I only focused on completing research.  I grabbed the Rainbow Blend at that beginning but after that, I only used my dice for research.  I was curious if I could complete them all and, combined with the Rainbow Blend points, win the game.  Nope.  That was a very dumb strategy.  I lost 21-13.  Haha.  It was worth a shot and since the game plays so quickly, it was no big deal.

These games were a lot more fun.  In both the games I won, I completed on research.  I would not have won without it.  My biggest worry was that the tension of using dice for points or for research was lost in the solo game.  I was wrong.  Research is still a necessity.  I am very pleased how these games went, and I feel like I actually beat the AI instead of got lucky with the dice.  My feelings are coming back around, which I&#039;m very glad about.  Next up, is Nick&#039;s solo variant.</body>

	<item id="4114109" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="124622" 			
			objectname="In Magnificent Style"
			username="reverendunclebastard" 
			postdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 04:36:28 +0000" 
			editdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 04:36:28 +0000"
			thumbs="25"
						imageid="1685861">
	<body>Another fun play of this thematic dice-chucker.

The game has two ways to score, a VP-based historical comparison and a basic &quot;how many positions did you capture&quot; number.

[imageid=2651778 large]

This game was a disaster. With several brigades wiped out entirely I ended up with a historical &quot;Severe Defeat&quot; and a &quot;Poor&quot; result of two Union positions captured.

This game is very luck based, with lots of dice rolling and chit pulling. However, this is a great way to represent a historical battle where the player&#039;s side faced a terrible defeat against bad odds. In spite of the randomness, there are a lot of interesting decision points:

1 - How and when to use the General&#039;s abilities for each division
2 - If and when to use the Longstreet and Lee bonuses (which provide great benefits but a chance of a serious reduction in VPs at the end)
3 - Which order to activate your divisions (keep in cover longer, push over the wall to make an adjacent divisions job easier, risk moving further into heavy fire to reveal more &quot;fire&quot; markers at the end of your turn etc.)
4 - Keep rolling to push over an obstacle to move out of a high-risk artillery zones vs. risking being pushed back to your rally point

I thoroughly enjoy my plays of this game so far, it is very exciting every time you roll the dice.
</body>

	<item id="4114148" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="68820" 			
			objectname="Enemy Action: Ardennes"
			username="Dancing Frog" 
			postdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 05:17:58 +0000" 
			editdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 07:12:57 +0000"
			thumbs="35"
						imageid="1197092">
	<body>I am waiting to win. I played the German Solo last month in which I lasted through December 25, 1944. For me, the result was the same as Ardennes &#039;44. Bastogne was captured with the 2nd Panzer and Panzer Lehr on December 19, 1944, but I was unable to get the 1SS and 12SS Panzer past the wooded regions in front of Verviers before the clock ran out. Also, the 7th Armee never even got to Ettlebruck.

So, I decided to play the Allied Solo this month to try to learn what I keep doing wrong with the Battle of the Bulge games as the Germans. I am still not dead after 4 days. I have learned four things. First, I am way too concerned with flank protection, so much so that I dilute the point of the spear too much. Second, I keep getting 116th Panzer stuck behind St. Vith. Third, I didn&#039;t understand what Von Heydte&#039;s paradrop actual purpose could be. Its actual purpose is to disrupt the placement of allied reserves. Fourth, the Allied Solo AI cheats. 

O.K., so the Allied Solo AI cheats. So what? You have to give the German player some advantage as it can&#039;t really anticipate what the Allied Player is going to do. For the most part, I think the AI is quite brilliant, especially the detachment and reserve system which ensures protection of the flanks of the panzer spearheads, advances hidden forces, and augments significant attacks. It allows masses of panzers to grind forward single-minded toward their objectives. I am all for that, I just think that are two areas where the Germans give themselves an unprecedented advantage. 

The first area is the initial setup which is handled by cards that simulates the results of the first German attacks. When compared with the German Solo system, the results that come out of that are pretty unlikely in German Solo system, unless the German player is very lucky with the chit draws. Or, the Allied player is a complete buffoon who decided to stand and fight rather than retreat and then quit after seeing how bad he did leaving you to clean up his mess. I think though on some level one can argue that this represents the total confusion of the first day.

The second area as I see it is that the German player can infiltrate through any line that&#039;s not wall to wall which is something he can&#039;t do in the German solo. That really makes it really easy to breach most lines at relatively low odds and push allied units in directions that they don&#039;t want to go opening holes that aren&#039;t available in the German solo.

So, with all that in mind, back to the game in progress. The following photographs document the situation of at the dawn of December 20 after 4 hard days of fighting.
[IMG]https://cf.geekdo-images.com/images/pic2650555_lg.jpg[/IMG]
In the 6th SS Panzer Armee sector, the Germans did their typical attacks for an Ardennes game with the 3rd Fallschirmer and the 1st SS Panzer destroying the 14th Cav in the Losheim gap. They then proceeded to capture Bulligen which put pressure on Elsenborn from the south while the 12th SS Panzer pushed around Rocherath-Krinkelt to the north helping the LXVII corp capture Monschau, putting pressure on Elsenborn, and surrounding  Rocherath-Krinkelt - the 2nd ID is a much stronger formation in Ardennes &#039;44. Then, Pieper infiltrated around to the back of Elsenborn on the the 17th surrounding it. Elsenborn was reduced on the 17th, and Rotherath-Krinkelt held until the 19th.

Meanwhile, the LXVII corp after taking Monschau moved south and relieved some of the units of the 1st SS Panzer from their duties besieging Rocherath-Krinkelt. Those elements with the all of the 12th SS Panzer oozed around the 7th Armor CCA on the 18th which had dug in in the woods along the Malmedy-Eupen road and destroyed it relieving Von Heydte&#039;s paratroops which had been messing with the deployment of the 30th ID and the 1st ID. 150th did it&#039;s driving through the ZOC thing and wound up north of Verviers revealing the final 6th Armee objective to be Liege and getting trapped by the 30th ID. The following day, the 19th, the same battle group slightly reinforced oozed around a regiment of the big red one, captured Spa, and pushed it aside to the northwest. That forced one regiment to pull back from Malmedy to Stavelot to protect the approaches to Trois Pontes.

In the process of all this, the German 1st SS and 12th SS panzer were heavily attrited. They also don&#039;t control any of the main roads, so their supply lines are tenuous to advance further unless they take Stavelot. I can&#039;t call them contained, but they are seriously hurt. Luckily, the 2nd SS Panzer Corps and 3rd Panzer didn&#039;t show up take part in the fight on the 19th. With the 3rd AD moving into the area on the 20th, it&#039;s possible that the worst is over in this sector.

[IMG]https://cf.geekdo-images.com/images/pic2650556_lg.jpg[/IMG]

In the 5th armee sector, things were probably the worst. The dummkopf that was playing the Allied side got the regiment of the 28th ID in front of Clervaux killed which left the road to Bastogne wide open. St Vith was also wide open and the 116th Panzer got across the Our causing enough losses to the regiment of 28th ID that was defending it that it rendered it ineffective as a blocking unit. The 106th also got hit hard by the LXVI Corps with two regiments surrounded and one reduced. I cobbled all the survivors into a defense of St. Vith and Vielsam and reinforced St Vith with 7th Armor CCB. 

Meanwhile, 9th Armor CCB and the engineers played cat and mouse along the road to Bastogne with the 2nd Panzer and Panzer Lehr whose objective was Houffalize. That only postponed the inevitable for about a day and Bastogne was captured on the 18th before the 101st could arrive. The 101st arrived later on the 18th where they tried to establish a line along the Ourthe, but only got as far as establishing a line from St. Hubert to La Roche before the Panzer crossed the bridges. There they were able to coral the Panzers into attacking from single hexes at the rivers edge. That caused the Panzers enough losses that they actually dispersed during the first attack of the day, but the 101st got pushed back across the river from La Roche with enough losses that they had to be replaced with the 9th Armor CCB which had survived its encounter and had to abandon it&#039;s defense of Houffalize to come help. The survivors from La Roche went to Manhay to recover. That pretty much arrested the panzers advance for the rest of the day which allowed two Combat Commands of 10th Armor to backstop them later in the day.

Back in the LXVI Corps area, elements of the 116th Panzer, LXVI corp besieged St. Vith while the rest of LXVI corps, the 116th Panzer, and the 560 reduced the two surrounded 106th Infantry regiments.

On the 19th, the 2nd Panzer and Panzer Lehr with the Fuhrer Begleit brigade tried to resume their advance to their next objective, Rochfort, but only managed to advance slightly with significant losses against dug in defenders of the 101st and 10th AD CCB in the forests in front of Marche. During that day, three regiments of the 82nd which had been delayed by the indecisiveness of Eisenhower moved into the area to further backstop the 101st. The other regiment of the 82nd with the 17th airborne was left back in the north at Werbomont to defend it from the 1SS and 12th SS should they past the big red one.

While that was a relatively major accomplishment, the LXVI and LVII corps were still able to capture St. Vith freeing them up to besiege Vielsalm the next day.

[IMG]https://cf.geekdo-images.com/images/pic2650557_lg.jpg[/IMG]
The 7th Armee sector was also pretty bad. Yet another regiment of the 28th at Vlanden also got flipped which left Diekirche and Ettlebruck wide open. It had to beat a hasty retreat to Diekirche where it was forced back across the bridges to Ettlebruck which the Germans managed to capture on December 17. Luckily, the Germans were focused on Mersch which allowed 4th ID to establish and dig into a defensive line in front of Arlon by the 18th while the 9th AD delayed the boys in pink in front of Mersch and then slipped across the river Alzette to safety. That move abandoned the remaining unit of 4th which had retreated from Echternach to Consdorf to the LXXX corps.

Even though these forces are relatively weak, I think they&#039;ll be able to hold out until 3rd Corps arrives.

So, I think we are doing OK. I expect to lose Vielsalm to the 116th Panzer today, but I may be able to hold up both the big spearheads. The 6th Panzer Armee sector really depends on how 2nd SS Panzer Corps shows up. If it comes into the fight today, it looks like it will probably spend the whole day attacking units blocking the supply line which means I don&#039;t think Verviers or Liege are in danger today. I expect Stavelot will be the target. In the 5th Panzer Armee sector, I am pretty sure we will be pushed back close enough to Rochfort that I will see where 5th Panzer Armee intends to cross the Rhine, but I don&#039;t think they&#039;ll break through. If they manage to make it to Rochfort, it looks like they&#039;ll have lost quite a bit of their punch just because they have to drop off units to protect their flanks until the 116th is able to catch up. Finally, I think the 4th will hold in the 7th Armee sector. 
 </body>

	<body>[size=9]Only a little while ago, I decided to take the plunge - playing a number of my co-operative games alone, and looked into a few variants of games I love, like Star Realms. I enjoyed playing these games so much, actively preferring a number of the solo gameplay experiences to their multiplayer counterparts; so I decided to invest a little more time and money into solo-gaming and pick up a game or two designed, specifically, for solitaire play.

After drooling over some games, like [thing=142854]Infection: Humanity&#039;s Last Gasp[/thing], and reflecting on budgets etc. it seemed that Friday was the perfect place to take the &quot;next step&quot; - and, wow, what a game! Despite assiduously and comprehensively defeating me, I have thoroughly enjoyed the game so far, and look forward to finally defeating the pirates before moving on to level two.

Now, I just need to wait &#039;til I can afford the likes of Infection...[/size]    [size=7]and maybe Mage Knight...    [/size]   [size=5]maybe even Darkest Knight...[/size]</body>

	<body>[center][imageid=2652224medium][/center]

Talk about [b]waiting[/b]...

I wouldn&#039;t normally do this but considering the theme of the month and how near I am to getting back to gaming I couldn&#039;t hold back.  I&#039;m actually posting about a game that I haven&#039;t quite played yet. :blush:

The kids had been off school for 10 weeks, no fuss, no bother, but not a lot of gaming either.  They started back Monday just gone and hence a few games of Mistfall amongst other things.  Today I had planned my first ever play of this (one of too many not yet played games in my collection) - it arrived during the school holidays (quite early on IIRC) and I&#039;ve been [b]waiting, waiting, waiting[/b] to get it to the table.  Whilst I [b]waited [/b]I read and re-read the rulebook, after [b]waiting [/b]some more I watched Ricky&#039;s vid again, followed by some more [b]waiting[/b].

Today was the day, except, the boy after 2 days back in school gets a chest infection and needs the rest of the week off.  So while he dozed and I [b]waited [/b]to do the Flo Nightingale bit this morning I opened the box anyway, threw out the insert, sorted bits and pieces into a handy plano (one of my favourite activities for any new game), set up and ran through the first Cycle.

The rulebook seems comprehensive (I only had 1 question unanswered) but is a bit all over the place with trying to ease players into it and layering things on - why isn&#039;t there a good overarching round summary?  Play tripped along nicely once I understood the flow and it seems like a game to get stuck into.

Sadly I still can&#039;t tick this one of as having been played so I must [b]wait [/b]a little longer.

[center][imageid=2652226medium][/center]

:thumbsup: Nice enough components, colourful map
:thumbsdown: Rubbish insert

[b]EDIT 11/9/15:[/b]
Well the boy went back to school but then the wife went off sick so I am only today able to get a play in.  Scored 36 medals (50 is required for a Baronial victory).  Good game, tough decisions and annoying insurgents but I can see ways to improve my gameplay (I think!).</body>

<comment username="Moe45673" date="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 15:19:28 +0000" postdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 15:19:28 +0000" editdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 15:19:28 +0000" thumbs="1">
Oooh, one more thing. This is an absolute must in the market games I love: can the commodities be used by yourself instead of sold?

<comment username="Ibbo" date="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 15:23:04 +0000" postdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 15:23:04 +0000" editdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 15:24:05 +0000" thumbs="1">
[q=&quot;Moe45673&quot;]I&#039;ve wanted to try a game like this, solitaire. Love me games with a good market. Does it feel natural in the 1P game how the prices rise and fall? Ideally, an AI market would work like a COIN flowchart or the new Conflict of Heroes system. [/q]

Someone with more experience of the game should really answer you but from my initial feel I would say no.  The (single) die roll at the start of each turn increases all 4 commodities one two or three levels.  The Government (auto play) decreases two of them by 1 each or does nothing, the Government when in[i](the pocket of)[/i]fluenced by your Industrial Baron can increase or decrease 1 commodity.  Pretty simple stuff really - but I could be selling it short.

EDIT: No commodities are only sold - either International Market (high &amp; low prices) or Local Market (low prices).
</comment>

Damn. I love the [thing=74720][/thing]-style thing where you produce stuff that you can either sell or invest back into your production line to produce more in the future.

	<body>

Gave this another play this morning and put in 5 black/debt. I quickly took on more Red/Crime cubes, which did not help the situation. I got close to losing (Public Safety was at 1) but used some money to get rid of some reds and then finished the black.

It&#039;s a fun little engine to try to beat. The default is a bit easy ... I may add another black and a couple of red cubes next time. Has anyone tried the advanced cards?

If you are scared of ever doing a print-and-play, it doesn&#039;t get easier than this. Print out the sheet, grab a bag and borrow some cubes from other games and give it a go. I laminated my sheet and use a dry-erase marker to keep track of the offices instead of more cubes. But you don&#039;t have to get that fancy.



</body>

<comment username="fractaloon" date="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 15:45:08 +0000" postdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 15:45:08 +0000" editdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 15:45:08 +0000" thumbs="4">
I can imagine.  Binders would be huge.  I use dividers to organize the game.  I keep the adventures in the original box and the player cards in an expansion box for Thunderstone.  That combination seems to be just the right size for me.

I was very very overwhelmed until I printed out the dividers by Ryno80 and started using them.  I used to use GeckoTHs&#039; divicers before but for some reason didn&#039;t find them very usable even though they look fantastic. Maybe because I printed them out on cardstock and the new ones are mounted on matte board.
</comment>
<comment username="modernlife" date="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 16:33:25 +0000" postdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 16:33:25 +0000" editdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 16:33:25 +0000" thumbs="5">
Take a look at the Ultra Pro binders if you haven&#039;t already. They come in different colours so you can match the spheres. I use a blue, red, green and purple binder for all the player cards by sphere, sorted by allies/events/attachments in release order. And then a white binder for all the heroes and neutral cards. 

Not exactly a cheap option but I find it great for looking through the cards to build decks. Although because the cards are in binders I only sleeve the deck(s) I&#039;m using now so there&#039;s all the money saved from not sleeving every card!
</comment>

	<item id="4114723" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="102652" 			
			objectname="Sentinels of the Multiverse"
			username="garyrbrooks" 
			postdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 15:04:59 +0000" 
			editdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 15:04:59 +0000"
			thumbs="30"
						imageid="1296144">
	<body>My 8th play of this recently reacquired game.

The randomiser app picked Absolute Zero, Bunker and the Visionary to take on Baron Blade in Insula Primalis.  I love that about this game - tons of replayability and no need for scenarios to create that.

This was a medium difficulty selection - that&#039;s what I&#039;ve decided to play until I feel totally comfortable with everything.  Also, I tried 3 games at hard difficulty and got my hat handed to me.

Managed to squeak a win by the skin of my teeth.  All 3 of my heroes had 1 HP remaining when Bunker finally finished off the Baron.

This game boggles my mind.  It captures the theme but also delivers a real mental challenge too.  Working out combos (e.g. using a Visionary card to change Baron Blade&#039;s attack to fire so Absolute Zero could do damage or heal himself) and keeping track of everything keeps my brain ticking.

One of the reasons I initially got rid of it (the bookkeeping) is now one of the reasons I want it to stay.  I&#039;ve also chilled out a lot and I&#039;m ok with missing the odd modifier - most can be applied later anyway and if not, over the length of game it usually doesn&#039;t affect the result significantly.

This wasn&#039;t in my [geeklist=189816]Top 20[/geeklist] last year but will almost certainly be this year.  It might even crack my top 10.

It might even beat [thing=129437][/thing] as my favourite super hero game.

I&#039;m now eyeing the expansions for this.... how long can I resist?

:thumbsup: It&#039;s super heroes. 

:thumbsdown: The bookkeeping won&#039;t be for everyone.

:thumbsup::thumbsdown: The art.  All by the same artist but some of the cards look great and some look amateurish.</body>

	<body>The first of my Out of Dust Games this month.  Last played in Jan, so used No Income Bacterial this time... [i]I will escalate to (Overtime Without Pay) Viral soon.[/i]

Won a couple, lost a few.  The worst play was up against it from the start; ended up lasting only 12 rounds.  Checking the cards, they ordered 11 molecules to be added to the C-Ring, throw in few negative dice modifiers and it got to the point where only a natural 6 would prevent the spread of infection.  An unlucky shuffle which could only have been countered with great dice rolls.

Disaster/Threat Management games have come to be a firm favourite of mine, and this has the common elements of one; variable powers (equipment &amp; staff), action points (drawing proteins, with cash restrictions), &#039;bad stuff&#039; (card effect on board and dice) and a timer (infection track) - all with a nice puzzley twist.  However for some reason I am not getting swept up in this game.  

[i]As I like to keep my collection small, more plays are planned, but this game&#039;s place in my collection is under review.[/i]

:thumbsup: Disaster Management-esque in a small footprint.
:thumbsdown: No Meeples</body>

	<item id="4115380" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="149079" 			
			objectname="Everything vs. Everything"
			username="radchad" 
			postdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 21:23:22 +0000" 
			editdate="Thu, 03 Sep 2015 21:23:22 +0000"
			thumbs="28"
						imageid="1844074">
	<body>And I figure the first game that I really want to post about was of course my game: Everything vs. Everything. Haven&#039;t played it in about a month or so but it still remains exactly the game that I want it to be. I personally always play with the difficulty at its highest, but instead of 4 cards in each drafting deck, I use 6 cards. The game is at its best with all of its crazy combos and 6 cards gives you the best options.

-------------------------------------------------------
I wanted to play a more traditional game so I chose to play against an Attack/Boost Director. I did of course choose my characters accordingly. 

My characters were The Joker, Macross, The Zerg, Optimus Prime, Kirby, and the Alien Queen as my spare. Since the Director is going to come out swinging, my strategy was to use the Directors tactics against him. Having Macross deflect damage back and swapping the Joker to steal an opposing character that was getting to powerful was the key. The Zerg&#039;s rush tactic that just attacks each turn helps, and Optimus Prime is great at boosting. Plus Kirby is just plain flexible.

Key problem with my strategy is picking the Energy Cards. I wasn&#039;t sure what my proper proportions were, so I went with 7 hearts, 7 clubs, and 6 spades.

Other weaknesses include no card changers, healers, draw extra cards, or spades in my deck (so Macross can&#039;t even attack normal). 

The Director started with Boba Fett, Swiper the Fox, The EMH Doctor from Star Trek Voyager, The Borg, and Danger Mouse. Yep, this game is always interesting.

[imageid=2652777 large]

First Turn: I get lucky with the directors first card as it cannot actually do anything to me! Yay. Of course, my first draw is just as spectacular. I do actually use the Joker&#039;s first attack ability against Boba Fett even though it is expensive so that the EMH director doesn&#039;t get a chance to fully heal him to 18 health.

Second turn: The Zerg continues to whittle away at both himself and the EMH doctor. Boba Fett deals a devastating blow to the Joker. I should probably get rid of him before he gets completely wiped out. SO I do. I grab the Borg and the Director gets my Joker. Can`t actually attack with the Joker, so he is now a meat shield.

Third Turn: The EMH Doctor gets a bazooka&#039;s worth of damage in boost tokens. I think that Macross needs to go against him. Yep, I do. So I do. 

Turn Four: First elimination: The Zerg takes out the Joker. Yep, his ability does feel like a true Zerg rush. Of course, he is going to kill himself as the game goes on, but it is still pretty cool to see it played out. Swiper continues to suck as a character. And the first new director character: Aerith Gainsborough from Final Fantasy 7. Still no Uber Director cards yet. 

Turn Five: Swiper gets some useless boost tokens, Aerith gets some useful boost tokens. I do a little damage to Swiper. Still waiting for the big attack!

[imageid=2652780 large]

Turn 6: In one of those weird timing effects of cards, The EMH doctor attacks Macross, but the Macross redirects the damage to Boba Fett, killing him. But this works right before the EMH Doctor can fully heal Boba Fett. This works because you enact each action on the card before moving on the the next action on the card. Oddly enough, this leave me without that much to do on my turn because my best attacking character, Kirby, gets stuck with a non attacking ability if he attacks something that cannot attack back. In other words, Swiper continues to swipe. And attacking Aerith is tricky to because her ability helps the director way more than it helps me.

Turn 7: Gypsy Danger gets pulled into the fold! He is one heavy hitter. Yikes! I use Optimus prime to Move things around a bit because Aerith Gainsborough does some major healing if she dies. So instead, the Zerg can take out Swiper. (I wonder if they would turn him into thier Zerg Queen? Owww man.)

Turn 8: Swiper dies. Aerith attacks. Macross redirects damage to EMH director. Then Optimus Prime attacks the EMH Doctor, killing him. Good thing too, he had 12 boost tokens. At the end of my turn, I sub in the Alien Queen for about to die Zerg. May as well use them if I can.

Turn 9: First Uber card. Was wondering where they were. And it is the major attack card. Gipsy Danger does major damage to my Borg. The Terminator comes into the game. Aerith Gainsborough&#039;s damage is redircted to Gipsy Danger, and Danger Mouse continues to do nothing because his attack is so wierd. I cannot respond due to not having enough clubs in my hand so I cannot do anything.

Turn 10: Another attack by the Director. He does a lot of damage, but it isn&#039;t enough.

[imageid=2652781 large]

End game score:

Director: 33
Me: 62

Knowing what you are going up against is a huge advantage in this game. Every strategy has a counter strategy. By design. But if you like to play a game that lets you do something clever, this is your game!
</body>

I am not speaking about the 2 well known German website shops, but all the rest is simply 2-3 months late on the matter.

It is ridiculous but even Wing Leader that was shipped in early July is still not available in shops that work with the official channels.

Chances are that the moment Churchill will be &quot;distributed&quot; to the normal EU shops, in 2/3 copies, GMT will run out and you have exactly a few days window before it is no longer available. It happened to Unconditional Surrender and lots of other games (Coin series etc...).

All that talk are simply excuses for not following the GMT or wargaming market closely. Period. These excuses are lame and is simply a direct result of sloppiness and non interest in supporting wargames. They sell a million XWing, so they are not even aware of &quot;another Wing&quot; game.

Individual shops can often import these things MONTHS before the distributor does, so it is quite clear where the hic up up is made.

	<body>I broke out Castaways today. I was really exited to play this because I&#039;ve enjoyed it so much in the past. I set it up and reread the rules. I probably could have legged it out without reading the rules, but I&#039;m really glad I did because I had played it solo before. This time, however, I decided to play with three characters, instead of one, and the rules are slightly different when playing with multiple characters. 

I won! So that was really satisfying because the game is crushingly hard with only one character. In fact, I found the game really easy this time around. I won with five rounds left in the game. Only one of my castaways had a trauma and only one of them had any injuries. In the solo game, my characters had died from too many traumas. It felt like an easy stroll across the island while I waited to be rescued. 

Despite the ease of the victory, the game took me three hours to play. It was so long! The time at least doubled with the two extra characters. I found that to be quite a disappointment. This game is relatively easy and a lot of it is like a choose your adventure book. So, the difficulty to length ratio seemed to be off by quite a bit. That&#039;s something I&#039;m starting to pay attention to. Games that are long should be more complicated, in my opinion. You know, [thing=96848]Mage Knight[/thing] takes 3 hours, but the depth and complexity make the time feel well spent. However, I wouldn&#039;t want to spend 3 hours playing a single game of [thing=142854]Infection[/thing]. Castaways feels like it should be an hour-and-a-half kind of game.

But I won, and that was really satisfying. I made a couple of mistakes but that&#039;s because I find it easy to mix up the [i]supply[/i] and the [i] storage[/i]. Here&#039;s my guys at the end. They&#039;re hungry and tired, but little worse for wear. 

[center][ImageID=2651842medium][/center]

[b]Edit:[/b]
I played two more games of this today.  I played one with two players and the other with three players.  Like Kevin said below, the game is crushingly hard with only one player.  I might even say unbeatable.  With two, it feels like a desperate attempt at survival. With three, things run along really smoothly and I find it pretty easy to stay alive.  With four, I would imagine that you will have more people than you know what to do with.  

I lost both games.  In the first game, I had the necessary requirements to flag a passing ship but I couldn&#039;t make it to the top of the mountain.  In the second game, I never really got the things I needed to signal the ship.  However, we had a bunch of wood and food, a goat, and we had built a house back in camp. So, the three of us would happily spend our days, in relative safety an comfort on the island.

[center][ImageID=2654113medium][/center]

This is a good game, and I quite enjoyed it.  However, I think my time with this game is done.  I am working really hard to [b][geeklist=194076]explore my collection[/geeklist][/b], and I am finding that means I need to get rid of games.  So, Castaways is off to the trading post.</body>

<comment username="Malaiser" date="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 15:46:47 +0000" postdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 15:46:47 +0000" editdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 15:46:47 +0000" thumbs="5">
Hi Al, I&#039;m not sure I can make the best comparison.  I&#039;ve only played one game of RC and it was a bunch of months ago.  I never really got a feel for the game in my one learning play.  However, I will do my best to compare the too.

Castaways is a medium-weight game, maybe along the lines of Ticket to Ride: Marklin (it&#039;s the most complicated of the TTRs).  RC is a much heavier game.  They both are worker placement games.  And, of course, they are both about being stranded on a island.  In both games you are trying to survive, you need to find food, build shelter, and explore. However, I would say they are accomplished in different ways.

Castaways only has one scenario, so to speak, where RC has a bunch of different scenarios.  Castaways has a choose-your-own-adventure type card deck which creates variability, but every game is the same basic structure.  In RC, it&#039;s my understanding that each scenario gives the player a different way to play.

In Castaways, there are two parts of the game.  First is the worker placement half.  In this, you are gathering wood, finding food, building shelter, keeping your fire lit, finding wreckage from your ship, building a &quot;help&quot; sign in the sand, that kind of thing.  It&#039;s the survival half of the game.  The second half is the exploration of the island phase.  

In the exploration portion, you leave the worker placement board and go off into the island and explore. There are three decks of cards, one for the coast, inland, and heart of the island.  As you explore, you draw cards from these decks.  It will often give you options and prompt you to get certain cards from the choose-your-own-adventure-style deck.  These new cards can be anything.  New events, new challenges, new equipment, a dog.  Here&#039;s an example.  There is a card that says you find a native woman running through the jungle trying to escape from the savages.  You can help her, help the savages, or ignore her.  This takes place during the inland portion of your exploration, and depending on what you do, you will take a card and shuffle it into the heart of the island deck.  I chose to help her, and because I did, I discovered they were cannibals later on in the game.  If I would have fought them, I&#039;m sure I would have learned something different.  

So, there is a very big story element to this game that isn&#039;t in RC.  However, I still think RC creates a strong story as well, it&#039;s just doesn&#039;t have an entire portion of the game dedicated to the story.  In Castaways, you stop the worker placement part of the game and start the exploration phase.  It&#039;s almost like it&#039;s two games in one.  With that said, however, the two halves flow together seamlessly.

I hope this helps.
</comment>

<comment username="camidon" date="Sun, 06 Sep 2015 02:53:57 +0000" postdate="Sun, 06 Sep 2015 02:53:57 +0000" editdate="Sun, 06 Sep 2015 02:53:57 +0000" thumbs="3">
Castaways is no longer in my collection.  RC is, and is never leaving. 

The concept of Castaways was good--I liked the exploration.  A lot. There was so much that could be done with the story cards.  But it didn&#039;t come together for me.  The game took far too long to play both solo and multiplayer.  What should have played in 90 minutes often took twice that time.  In addition, you&#039;re doing all the same actions every game for the same reasons, and it felt repetitive.  In RC, though the actions stay the same, the reasons for doing them differ quite a lot, which to me, make the game great.

I also found you had to play with more than 1 character to have any chance of winning.
</comment>

			thumbs="35"
						imageid="738119">
	<body>Let&#039;s just get this out there.  [b]I love this game.[/b]

I have to thank [b][user=woelf]Kyle[/user] [/b]for bringing it to my attention.  A non solo game that he has created a super simple solo variant for that works brilliantly.

I have only played it 6 times but each one of those games has been excellent.  Each game has been different and it truly captures the theme. 

In this play I was Captain Bruce Nicholson (of no fixed abode) and his stats made a pirate strategy the obvious choice.

This worked really well and I even got a Glory card that allowed me to remove all my bounties (5 at that time) by paying gold so I could start from scratch again.  I completed a mission, 3 rumours and upgraded my ship to a Frigate so I reached 10 Glory points with 2 turns left (the solo variant has 15 turns) and was victorious.

[ImageID=2653617 medium]Crikey! That&#039;s a lot of boats.

Or so I thought.  I then realised I hadn&#039;t made an influence roll for 2 of my rumours. :shake:  My brain must have been thinking about something else (West Ham winning at Anfield in the league for the first time since 1963 possibly - the year before my parents met!).

Anyway, I did the two influence rolls and only succeeded at one so I took off a Glory point and discarded a Glory card.

I now had 2 turns to get 1 point.  I tried twice to take down a pirate Sloop but failed.  I damaged it badly but it successfully fled both times.

My last chance was to try and take down a merchant and get 12 gold from the raid.  I was able to add a fourth cargo card to the haul and this gave me 14 gold and a Glory point. VICTORY (for real this time).

Anyway, this will definitely make my [geeklist=189816]Top 20[/geeklist] when the People&#039;s Choice Top 100 rolls around.  I have a feeling it may even be in my Top 5.

It may also have made [b][thing=95103][/thing][/b] redundant.  This is easier to set up, the rules are much simpler and it delivers an experience just as thematic.  I will have to play that again to compare properly but right now I know which one I would choose to take to a desert island.

:thumbsup: Theme, components, ruleset, challenge.  All of these are spot on.

:thumbsdown: The luck of the dice and movement of the NPCs can sometimes destroy you.</body>

	<body>[center][imageid=2653644medium][/center]

The telephone rang.  Super Dad and Sick Boy ran to answer.

&quot;Super Dad, Sick Boy!  We&#039;ve just had reports that Dr Doom and his Doombot Legion have stolen Mole Man&#039;s Massive Earthquake Generator and has set it up in Donegal.  He&#039;s trying to get it on-line right now.  You know what to do. And be quick about it!&quot;

&quot;We&#039;re on it, Chief.&quot;

SB &amp; SD gathered the most trustworthy SHIELD agents they could.  &quot;Okay people, we need heroes and we need them now.  You!  See who&#039;s available.  You!  There are some shenanigans going down on Front Street, see what&#039;s occuring.&quot;

Reports soon filtered back that the Sinister Six and Maximum Carnage were creating havoc to divert attention from the Generator.  Fortunately Iron Man, Spider-Man, Thing, Thor and Captain America had answered the call.

Despite losing a few good agents to some early earthquake fissures and some very scary Maximum Carnage feasting the dream team were starting to fire on all cylinders.  With some cool moves and great planning Doombots were sent flying in a hail of electric sparks, Shriek was silenced, Sandman was blasted and Vulture&#039;s were plucked out of the sky.

Spider-Man turned Kraven the Hunter into the hunted and Thing, Thor and Captain America pulled off the final attack that captured Dr D and pulled the plug on the generator.

Super Dad and Sick Boy thanked everyone and sat down with a nice biscuit and a cup of tea.

The Hills of Donegal were safe once again.

<comment username="Ibbo" date="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 18:19:25 +0000" postdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 18:19:25 +0000" editdate="Fri, 04 Sep 2015 18:19:25 +0000" thumbs="3">
[q=&quot;sixthecat&quot;]Great write-up!
Great song! Nice toe-tapper. :thumbsup::thumbsup:[/q]

Thanks, glad you liked it.  Local band but a national hit, it&#039;s a real party song and was modern about 20 years ago!  The philosophy behind the song comes from the fact Donegal was, in the bad old days, very cut off from the rest of the country being almost surrounded by the North.  Things were very different here compared to the other 25 counties - almost neither one side of the border nor the other.  So why not play on that &#039;otherness&#039; and create your own wonderland?  And like you say, it&#039;s a jaunty tune.
</comment>

	<body>[IMG]https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/HjWZv4t8JryNUxHOy2gK5zOowHyE4F5kiyWZXZ5u10NCoEKhfdBnyGpxnNabjsl4QNjTFZPzFNafprGmWfS2wgx2LQq4jlrH-QwyFOmG7yuK4M6OsQ6RJrllPVTdIwhN4Ua7eBVaJt23WsE92xSJ_WrTDjgcX8NW8LUUIN_MW5vKIdQMpGKxGStsvGWSHAN9aH_JoVgdnAired1U4tLeFUJ907_qfu3E6dwUxaET4hf1aQzzEhPLkqaCAbIkJrdicB9rVEa5IXYjvgxospBJ6kPDapL6m8D4LRFJtrr1_1yMbGnqnXsCixw_BEUVMPWVX7Wi05WNfHBqRjhd9DaePbF25hEUyaOTvDiH5IfLVQvJci5RQ87UpXdP0WqNOFsqRIJ6GKzDPmmUoOlL8Djzgf3R4O-Dht7uSjILMoSGa9CrgjPvDL6f2YL376ii7G5Ya3PFbKcCK2SxmH-g4bX1gyc2YA3wVhHCXlzX8K9bL-B8b3l0TBoHjiq654NgLOo9ZNq1rTelxn4XjMyNV7Tdm38=w212-h54-no[/IMG]

[b]Game:[/b] 1/3
[b]Difficulty: [/b]1 Drone in objective 2, 2 drones in objective 3.
[b]Tow Handed[/b]
Two losses in a row.  This one felt like a straight up beat-down.  After playing this movie again I am happy I watched it too.  It helps with the theme of this deck which is about brotherhood and sacrifice.  If the CGI of that move wasn&#039;t done so poorly it might have been an OK movie.  I cringed every time I saw the alien.

I think this might be the 3rd time playing this movie.  And it shows.  I&#039;m not quite sure the best ways to construct and use this deck.  But that&#039;s part of the fun of course.  This was a tense game.  By the middle of the second objective, I would have at least one alien in the combat zone.  What made it worse is the facehuggers inserted into the barracks.  When those appear they get the most focus.  So instead of taking out aliens in the combat zone I had to kill the facehuggers and then start drawing strikes.  Early on in the third objective the Beast (final enemy) appeared in the combat zone.  It was soon followed by Michael Weyland who instead of making you draw a strike, he puts a chestburster into you discard pile.  When you get around to drawing this card you are dead.  He was in the combat zone and I needed 7 attack to kill him.  I had 6 :(  Basically my turns were now numbered.  A few turns later I had a gaming moment I&#039;ll remember for a while.  I drew and played &quot;Internal Exam&quot; card and was able to discard the chestbuster.  Yes, I was punching air...
[IMG]https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/FNYkokgQPdQE256j1JKt6rV_LGGOoiNCbWKowd88spM1bDoidwQpII3_EjpRKTqOKL-NEg2Vz3gAy1us1P7OPJnz2M8NM0_Gqe5Ue_uDZsKlvk4-UWPploiIWa-xD3lCtxrTt79QLw9_EsPfJIgOxPJ1hHwqjCiToryqQ3fbmTU4Ig63L5Hf3l-2-oI14hbD7ZArHxrxyj23g7ZMQuoqBcf9gSRQmZhdaEjsdfRGaG06FawuqBvw9vrUxcEwxV4EHWtu-Ou4HgKf-MacHQmvUdtpNDUPiamyuYhh6eZ_kDlzGD1mFj4PTQBmWVdCV2EMoZsmJzEuZW9ehgIOX7hQBvfN8iwoNORCYrILD14egNLODtIukKggitrZoAU_odLS6ipaUaSpBacY9eI-krHp_rqF-qgjm1qyXsGLKoN30xu8cc6p4RT3uIbZIel-4G-d6B3N_st0njsS2MD6QzkdnhTydCxWqCUhfJleCEd6FKEWYV9E_0vbJOEsNi0O_9WV8D7kZVxHXogWUw1ZkKDzX3I=s800[/IMG]

Well, it didn&#039;t really matter anyway.  I was able to hold off for a few more rounds but ultimately the aliens had their way.  I&#039;m sure both characters are now either ripped apart or are now hosts to a baby alien.

:star: This game is just so tense.  It is not a way for me to sit down and relax :)  The only other game that has this affect on me is [thing=144568][/thing]

[b]Game:[/b] 2/3
[b]Difficulty: [/b]1 Drone in objective 2, 2 drones in objective 3.
[b]Two Handed[/b]
Now this was a fun session!  I focused primarily on picking up cards that could kill other cards (deck thinning).  It worked out very well.  There were times where situations were a little uncomfortable.  But that didn&#039;t deter my strategy.  At the end of the game one hand had 11 cards and the other 16.  I had no issue generating the attack I needed throughout the third objective.  I got you this time Beast!!!
[IMG]https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/fw4YO3gCBbbR0CaDgonnZqghvJT2Pk9hGIIUwZGVg51vHfwJZljz9Vb7ZxgmKnUpi-U0Q0iNeaw94bXPSksWrTafCT4-HAECnblyfQyEph9kDFTifW4TgGE5yfcy5jwMPfpLBOa0uB0xszBa_5GGpAIzZI6NecYSd8wTeZ_qNZioGwa4873DnmciYs9fh-5KNiUR5NZbSFxsTQMolVYOGgxv9_NWkXEbtrwcakE4mqaH7h8aILfD5t31adN1SEW6-2Y_zEwWfURrBnzoZQB0Q4EZKTabs8u3lBm1qIq0H7Pe2Jv7AoPhriWcRMfgqkvFptbjs7OGEIi6HMqpV1rKhZKM8oMkzSIQ3g_aC_EUlzLzw3hw58CBDi24IMfdw6zlaQ-RDD2sfBF6vkODliaSVxoX88eaW3GKSEeAWu3dH5m0DJ7ka8bRaBtuXT-1-Y6ptaCrfs-IStQj_mv1Q3StQGbVbslHU4nKjCYfXoL9yJLpqo_v5hfnCq3z8Mqyo9bQlqUiAWP1DEDCRKSiEqyL7Sc=s800[/IMG]

[b]Game:[/b] 3/3
[b]Difficulty: [/b]0 Drones
[b]Two Handed[/b]
Got my groove back with my 2nd win in a row.  I played with 0 drones this time to amp up the difficulty.  No problem, I was able to continue my previous strategies of thinning my decks early.  The HQ stayed full of great cards and I had no issue taking out the Beast.

	<body>Sologameapalooza has begun!  And what a way to start....

I did it!  I finally beat the Watcher in the Water!  Epic details here: [listitem=4114069][/listitem]

Last night, I took the time to organize all my card and put together sideboards for each of my decks.  This is essential, I think, if you want to use a thematic deck (dwarves, elves, etc) for multiple quests.  I find that I&#039;m much more successful when I deckbuild specifically for a quest, but I don&#039;t always find that enjoyable - meaning, I would rather be playing a thematic deck with my favorite characters than just play to win.  With a sideboard, I can have it both ways.  I have a core set of cards to each thematic deck that are always in that deck.  Then I can swap out the less-thematically-important-to-me cards with cards in the sideboard that are still thematically relevant, but can give the deck what it needs for a certain quest.  So, I have my dwarf deck, and then this huge stack of &quot;dwarf&quot; trait (or somehow dwarf related) cards.  My allies and weapons are almost always the same, but the event cards are what I most often switch up depending on the quest.  </body>

	<body>5 more plays today - which completes 1 of my planned 3x10 Out of Dust for this month.

Today was more Disaster than Management; whilst it was &#039;No Income Bacterial&#039; again it was with Variant: Tightening the Belt, so only $10 to start.

[i]Disaster[/i] - apart from the 5/5 losses; in the first game; the homogenizer (1 protein covers 2 spaces on the same molecule) was the first purchase after an early destruction of a matching pair of molecules.  However after it&#039;s purchase it failed to work every turn until an event card removed it from the game. :devil:
[i]Management[/i] - meant often buying only the cheap proteins, and needing to destroy a molecule (or two) before being able to buy cards.

[q=Gedin]How much tension do you experience while playing the game. Do your victories feel earned? When you lose, does it feel like a nail-biter finale where you felt if you had just one more turn you could have won? I know that many of my games felt like they came down to cliff hanger.[/q]
3 of the games were nail-biter end-games; plenty of molecules were solved as the &#039;Add to X&#039; rarely swapped out the partial builds. However in each the Containment Phase ran out before I could assemble the last solution.  Yet I was not feeling the tension, just &#039;Dice Hate Me&#039; as rolls would be fails beyond the help of Plus 1 modifiers.

Part of the problem with these recent plays (I now realise) is a missed rule; I have not discarded a Lab card during clean-up if nothing was bought, so have been stuck with a bad selection - and with limited funds saw no way to get better cards.

[i]I have plans for yet more plays before year end, and for 50 plays before a decision is made - so time enough to play correctly.[/i]</body>

	<item id="4118091"

	<body>Now, I definitely wouldn&#039;t consider myself a wargamer, but there are certainly some &quot;war&quot; games that I enjoy.  With that in mind, I recently acquired [thing=28829][/thing] in the latest Canadian Math Trade and had a chance to peruse the rulebook during some downtime at work today.  With the house to myself tonight, I figured it would be a good chance to break this one open and give it a shot.

I decided to try out the shorter Ghost Division campaign.  Setup was a breeze and I was up and playing in just minutes.  I quickly rushed forward, moving the troops into Dinant and then Reims, in hopes of putting a dent in the Allied forces, but they quickly bounced back with more reinforcements popping up in Paris.  Unable to manage his supplies, Rommel was quickly vanquished by the first week of June as the Allies held strong in Cambrai.

Overall, though I suffered a ridiculously quick defeat, this game seems quite fun.  It plays quick (at least when you lose as quick as I do) and setup/take-down is quite minimal, so I can see it getting to the table a lot in the next coming weeks.  I can&#039;t wait to give this one another shot.


:thumbsup: The rulebook was quite simple to follow and nicely laid out for quick referencing.  It didn&#039;t take long to get a good feel for the flow of the game.

:thumbsup: The chit-pull mechanism is great and gives you lots to think about when launching an attack.

:thumbsup: I only have a few games with counters and hell will freeze over before you ever see me clipping, but these counters seemed to be very high quality (and pre-clipped? or is that just my used copy?)

:thumbsdown: The paper maps, though durable for &quot;paper&quot;, are still paper.  I really would have liked to see a mounted maps, but I wouldn&#039;t have shelled out for the deluxe version... oh well.  A big positive is that they are very nicely laid out and all the charts/boxes for each campaign are right there for reference on the map.

Possible :thumbsdown:? Only 3 maps with no variable setup makes me wonder what the replay value actually is.  On the plus side, this game seems punishingly difficult (so that will certainly get me playing over and over).</body>

	<body>[imageid=2654506]

I played a randomized game of Legendary with the Golden Solo Ruleset. I thought I would try out my new challenge cards to increase the challenge a bit and pulled the &quot;Hell on Earth&quot; Challenge, requiring to play two villains at once. I&#039;ve played a few games using the golden solo ruleset but turns out i was supposed to be pulling 2 villain cards all along according to the ruleset. 

Here is the randomized scenario I played:

Mastermind: Carnage
Scheme: Master of Tyrants (with doom, sinister, zombie green goblin added to the villain deck)

Villain Deck:
Streets of New York
Maximum Carnage
Doombot Henchmen

Hero Deck:
Apocalyptic Kitty Pryde
Rogue
Old Man Logan
Ghost Rider
Colossus

Results: Heroes won (72 points)

I had a hard time getting started. The lose condition of the scheme was 5 masterminds escaping. I had 4 Masterminds in the escaped pile. One more and I lose. I couldn&#039;t keep any good cards in my deck as Maximum Carnage and Doombots kept feasting/KOing them. I thought I was surely doomed but at the last ditch effort I was able to get some breathing room. I  set up a good combo with Ghost rider, and Rogue&#039;s strength cards and scrounged up enough damage to knock out 2 slots in the city. This bought me some breathing room and i was able to start punching Carnage. I finally won in the knick of time as the Zombie Green Goblin, the 5th mastermind card, was about to escape.

[imageid=2654518]

Between Feast and Doombots I only had 13 cards in my deck at the end of the game. I had KOed 22 cards from my hero deck and 4 from my victory pile to feed Ghost Rider&#039;s Blazing Hellfire.

Kitty Pryde and Old Man Logan didn&#039;t do much for this set up. No other heroes had tech cards to combo with kitty. Old Man Logan relied on other players. Both also relied heavily on KOing heroes which I really couldn&#039;t afford.

This was probably the hardest game I&#039;ve played of legendary yet. I&#039;ll still have to wait and try my challenge cards again soon for an extra boost of difficulty.</body>

	<item id="4118260" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="103885" 			
			objectname="Star Wars: X-Wing Miniatures Game"
			username="reverendunclebastard" 
			postdate="Sat, 05 Sep 2015 05:54:06 +0000" 
			editdate="Sat, 05 Sep 2015 06:06:57 +0000"
			thumbs="37"
						imageid="1603292">
	<body>So it has been a while since I last played this amazing game. Tonight I was inspired by the recent release of a user-made cooperative campaign! Amazing stuff. Five story arcs that mix together as you fight off the empire in a remote section of the galaxy. Pilots that level up! 

Instead of using the standard squad building, you start with a newbie pilot and, through successful missions, gain experience which allows you to buy upgrades and skills. The campaign rules really open up the experience, slowly letting you accumulate upgrades and multiple elite pilot skills and modifications (in the regular game you can have only one elite pilot skill and one modification). You start in an x or y-wing but can spend experience to upgrade to a b-wing, a-wing or Hawk.

It also has new terrain (Ion clouds, minefields, SPACE STATIONS!), and an AI system for the empire&#039;s ships that is based on the web app that so many of us use ([url]http://xwing.runbam.com.s3-website-us-east-1.amazonaws.com/[/url]) but has been tweeked to allow for formation flying and swerving around obstacles. The AI charts are printed on cards and enemy movement is resolved with a d6.

Amazing work, and beautifully designed too. You can find it here:

[url]http://dockingbay416.com/campaign/[/url]

The only downside is that to run a full campaign you will need a lot of ships (especially Tie Fighters!). Luckily I have a bit of an obscene collection.

Played the introductory mission tonight (no new terrain needed so I just used the pdf on my computer to display the AI charts). My two pilots had to survive ten rounds, distracting the empire while the rest of the rebels jumped into hyperspace to reach our secret base.

My two pilots were Kelarin Undea in an x-wing with an R7T1 droid (which gives you an action to target lock and boost if you end up in an enemy firing arc) and Sha Senn in an x-wing with an R5P9 droid (let&#039;s you spend a focus token at the end of combat to regain a lost shield).

Names generated by the Star Wars Random Name Generator, found here:

[url]http://www.dimfuture.net/starwars/random/generate.php[/url]

As Kelarin (#1) and Sha (#2) head into the asteroid field, they spot three tie fighters approaching.

[imageid=2654533 large]

Turn 1:

The two rookie pilots squeeze through the asteroids and prepare to engage the enemy.

[imageid=2654537 large]

Turn 2:

While Kelarin shoots past the pair of ties to the left, hoping she can turn in behind them, Sha fires at the third tie but misses.

[imageid=2654555 large]

Turn 3:

Sha flies past the lone tie and engages the pair of ties as they curve around the asteroid, damaging the lead ship. Kelarin turns and takes a long-distance shot at the lone tie and scores a hit!

[imageid=2654538 large]

Turn 4:

As the two x-wings turn to reposition themselves, a tie interceptor joins the battle!

[imageid=2654539 large]

Turn 5:

Kelarin turns in behind the interceptor and manages to blast one of the ties out of the sky. The destroyed tie&#039;s partner manages to seriously damage Kelarin&#039;s ship. 

[imageid=2654540 large]

Turn 6:

As Kelarin finds herself with an interceptor close on her tail, Sha swings back towards the centre of the asteroid field, hoping she can take out the damaged tie and start to even the odds.

[imageid=2654546 large]

Turn 7:

Kelarin pulls a k-turn and ends up face to face with the interceptor, too close for either one of them to shoot. Unfortunately another tie fighter has entered the asteroid field and it scores a hit. Things are critical! Meanwhile Sha manages to further damage one of the other ties, but it barrel rolls to get her in its sights and fires! A hit!

[imageid=2654550 large]

Turn 8:

Kelarin flies at top speed towards the tie that is closing on Sha, hoping to take it out before it can cause more damage. Unfortunately the nimble interceptor makes a sharp turn and boosts in behind her to take a fatal shot. Kelarin is lost!

[imageid=2654551 large]

Turn 9:

Sha only needs to survive this turn and the next to allow the Rebel Transport to launch into hyperspace. She k-turns in behind a tie, but the deadly interceptor gets her in his arc. Game over, the rebels have lost this sector!

[imageid=2654557 large]

After playing the intro scenario, I am definitely printing this whole thing out tomorrow. Can&#039;t wait to dive in! I have flown as the empire in most of my games, so it is exciting to me to be playing the rebels for once. 

By the way, the asteroids in the pictures were made from BBQ lava rocks (you can get a bag of 100s for $7-8 at a hardware store). Primed, painted, drybrushed and a small hole drilled in them to insert the pegs. The acrylic tokens are from Litko (love them), you can find them here:

[url]http://www.litko.net/categories/Supported-Board-Games/Star-Wars-X-Wing/[/url]

:star: Cooperative campaign!
:star: Minor tweaks to the existing AI charts make a huge difference to the deadliness of the empire&#039;s ships
:star: A ton of gameplay from a free download
:star: Missions all scale to the number of rebel ships in play
:star: I know the guy that created this and he has playtested it for close to a year at a bunch of different player/rebel-ship counts
:nostar: Need to print and cut out a bunch of cards and terrain
:nostar: You need a lot of ships to play the full campaign (however, if your collection is limited, playing with a single rebel ship reduces the number of enemy ships necessary. You can also substitute ships that you do have for ships that you don&#039;t).</body>

<comment username="Gaius" date="Sat, 05 Sep 2015 17:12:56 +0000" postdate="Sat, 05 Sep 2015 17:12:56 +0000" editdate="Sat, 05 Sep 2015 17:12:56 +0000" thumbs="4">
Awesome session report byReverend.  This game has been collecting dust in my collection for two years now and I came close to selling it a number of times.  Thanks for the inspiration.  This new coop variant might be what it takes to get this game back on the table.

I&#039;ve skimmed through the this homebrew campaign book, and it wasn&#039;t immediately apparent what the minimum number of ships by size I would need for a campaign without an unreasonable amount of proxing.  Has any one done the math for, say, a 2-player coop campaign? (I&#039;m thinking a solo experience with 2 rebel ships would be more fulfilling.)  Thanks.

<comment username="reverendunclebastard" date="Sat, 05 Sep 2015 17:25:47 +0000" postdate="Sat, 05 Sep 2015 17:25:47 +0000" editdate="Sat, 05 Sep 2015 17:27:22 +0000" thumbs="5">
[q=&quot;Gaius&quot;]Awesome session report byReverend.  This game has been collecting dust in my collection for two years now and I came close to selling it a number of times.  Thanks for the inspiration.  This new coop variant might be what it takes to get this game back on the table.

I&#039;ve skimmed through the this homebrew campaign book, and it wasn&#039;t immediately apparent what the minimum number of ships by size I would need for a campaign without an unreasonable amount of proxing.  Has any one done the math for, say, a 2-player coop campaign? (I&#039;m thinking a solo experience with 2 rebel ships would be more fulfilling.)  Thanks.[/q]

My rough estimate if playing with two rebel ships:

Rebel:

2 xwing, 1 hawk, 1 falcon, 1 Rebel Transport and if you want to upgrade your player ships then also 1-2 ywing, 1-2 awing, 1-2 bwing 

Empire:

5-6 ties, 3 tie interceptors, 2-3 tie bombers, 1 tie advanced, 1 shuttle, 1 decimator, 2 phantoms, 2 defenders

There is one mission that uses a second shuttle, but as an obstacle only, I plan on using a firespray for that.
</comment>

	<body>My first divergence from my month with Awakening the Bear. I wanted to get in a quick play of something before my daughter woke up from her nap.

It&#039;s probably common sense, but poor shuffles can go both ways in this game. I thought I did a pretty good shuffle after my last game, but even though I tried to mix things up as I was setting up, I still ended up with a lot of cards right in a row as I needed them. I cleared all the face down starting cards before I even got to the 3rd page I believe. It was an easy win that I didn&#039;t bother to score.

I think this will be one that requires a shuffle both before and after each play to ensure randomness. I still had fun this play, but it wasn&#039;t really a challenge.

[b]Update:[/b] Well no dang wonder I&#039;m thinking this game is so easy. I thought that when you set up the passenger&#039;s rescue, you could play as many cards as you can from what you draw. Turns out you can only play ONE. That makes things way more restricting. Without even playing another game I can see why the &quot;victory&quot; condition is set at 19.

The Great Rules Bungler strikes again!

[b]Update:[/b] Just played a game using the crew member that lets you play all the cards you draw, but doesn&#039;t let you draw new action cards, meaning you get 2 for the entire game.

I scored a 12. That&#039;s more like it.</body>
