	<body>The fight back starts now.

After banging on about how good Sentinels of the Multiverse is it was time for my historically favourite super hero game to put its underpants on over its tights and go to work.

Inspired by the great post by [b][user=ibbo][/user] [/b] and because this is sitting in the incorrect spot in my current [geeklist=189816]Top 20[/geeklist] I decided to try and play this 5 times today.

I played using the set up for the Week 7 Challenge - they stopped creating them after about 30+ challenges but plenty to try and someone else has started a new set of challenges.  Here&#039;s the link to the original challenges thread: [thread=1008529][/thread]

Turned out to be easy to achieve those 5 plays.  The first 3 games were over very quickly. The first game after just 3 turns, the third game after 4.  That was a reminder of how frustrating this game can be when the decks have clumps of cards together.

The fourth game went much better and I was doing ok and took down Loki for a third time with this combo:

[ImageID=2654711 medium]
Only for this to be the tactics card:

[ImageID=2654712 medium]
Those two KO&#039;d bystanders brought the total to 4 KO&#039;d and that meant the end.

I decided to play a fifth game but decided to try Weekly Challenge #8. This was a much more straight forward challenge.  This was a lot of fun and I got to about two turns from the end and managed to take down Magneto for the final time.

These last two games reminded me how fun this can be when you get a good deck together and get some great combos.

Anyway, this will definitely be moving up my top 20 (currently at 20) after these plays but I&#039;m also reminded why it probably won&#039;t crack the top 10.  The way the hive deck is constructed in Legendary Encounters stops that game being over too quick and that&#039;s why that game will probably end up higher than this in my list and my favourite deck builder overall.

:thumbsup: Theme and mechanics - I love super heroes and deck builders.

:thumbsdown: The decks can sometimes conspire against you and end games very quickly.</body>

<comment username="draines" date="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 21:10:25 +0000" postdate="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 21:10:25 +0000" editdate="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 21:10:25 +0000" thumbs="3">
[q=&quot;garyrbrooks&quot;] The way the hive deck is constructed in Legendary Encounters stops that game being over too quick and that&#039;s why that game will probably end up higher than this in my list and my favourite deck builder overall.[/q]

So I have been house-ruling Legendary for awhile now to stop this problem. I look at the particular plot I am playing and see if there is a &quot;you lose when the last scheme card appears&quot; type of condition. If so, then I take one of the scheme/bystander/whatever cards and put it aside. I shuffle the rest of the bad-guy deck. Then I pull 4 cards, add the held card, and shuffle those together. This small packet goes to the bottom of the deck. This keeps the game from being over before it even starts.

Cheating? Possibly. Less frustrating? Definitely.

Give it a try. You will probably feel that the game plays better for that type of scenario.
</comment>

<comment username="Kyuss" date="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 09:16:27 +0000" postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 09:16:27 +0000" editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 09:16:55 +0000" thumbs="0">
I also recently picked this up and played through a couple of games. It is a fabulous game but you definitely want to take it slow and steady!

To echo what Peter said, I&#039;d recommend playing the Allies and using the Japanese bot for your first game. I found the Allied bot a bit trickier to implement at the start of the game. I also found it a little easier to win against the Allied bot because of the way it handles the Progress of War rules. Next time I play as the Japanese I&#039;m going to do a bit more of playing both sides during the Allied mid game and not religiously follow the Allied bot instructions.

	<body>This one has been languishing at the bottom of the pile for a while.  It needs playing more often. :)

I was very lucky with the opening draw, with a high proportion of strength 3 cards.  This meant I could snaffle a couple early on relatively cheaply.  This meant (unusually) I &#039;boosted&#039; a card using an Indian only once in the entire game.

This fine team powered me across the continent, leaving MacKenzie gasping in my wake.  A slight exaggeration maybe...  He started 2 spaces in front of me and ended 3 spaces behind as I powered far into the pacific.

My brain is too often frazzled at the end of the day and a thinky optimisation puzzle isn&#039;t often top of the list.  However, when I am in the right mood, this is fantastically rewarding.

	<body>My other play this evening was this altogether different game.  Thematic as ever, this game sucks you in despite its small(ish) footprint and simple (but high quality) components.

This time it was the turn of Book, Flamer, and Claws teams to try their luck.

Unfortunately Mr Flamer was an early casualty in the first location.  Despite being on the back foot so early, the team pressed on.  A lot of luck (!) kept the Claws and Book teams going until the last location.  The loss of the entire Flamer team hampered the action selection.

Then it all went wrong.

They started dropping like flies.  Judicious use of the Power Field kept some glimmer of hope, and both blip piles were slowly emptied - sadly at the expense of a million &#039;stealers in play.

The star Book team marine (Mr &#039;Chain Attack&#039;) was the last one standing.  No &#039;curse of the zero&#039; for him.  Standing alone, a Gun Jam event proved too much to overcome and he was swamped on both sides.

I love this game :devil:</body>

	<item id="4119817" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="178613" 			
			objectname="Star Trek: Five-Year Mission"
			username="suzyvitale" 
			postdate="Sun, 06 Sep 2015 05:26:56 +0000" 
			editdate="Sun, 06 Sep 2015 05:26:56 +0000"
			thumbs="22"
						imageid="2560621">
	<body>I liked this so much more than I thought I would.  I played the first game solo with two characters, Kirk and Spock.  Per the rulebook, if you play with 2 players, then you use characters numbered 1-2.  Which are Kirk and Spock.  But then it says that someone has to play Bones (for healing) otherwise the game is hard.  I opted to play Kirk and Spock, and it was game over pretty quick.  Healing is important in this game.  There are cards that can provide minimal healing, but there aren&#039;t many and they only heal one injury.  

My husband was interested, so we played the second game together using Kirk and Bones.  It was really hard, even with healing.  We just never had enough dice it seemed.  We lost by failing too many missions.

We played a third time, this time each controlling two characters.  He had Kirk and Scotty, and I had Spock and Bones.  This was a much better game.  It was still pretty close there at the end, but we won at the Ensign (easiest) level.  

I noticed on the box that it says it&#039;s a cooperative game for 3-7 players.  I think that you would need to be playing at least 3 characters for this game to be winnable.  And it&#039;s a lot more fun the more characters you have out.  When we play again, we&#039;ll definitely control two characters each. 

:thumbsup: As a lover of Star Trek: TOS, this game is a thematic win on so many levels.  Plus, they nailed all the graphic design.  Really well done.

:thumbsup: A unique addition to my collection.  Mechanics are creative.

:thumbsdown: I can&#039;t see myself playing this solo very often.  You really need at minimum three characters for this game to be winnable, and playing &quot;three-handed&quot; seems like a lot to manage.  (This is coming from the person who thinks it&#039;s too much to play LOTR:LCG two-handed, so take this for what it&#039;s worth.) Maybe someone creative will think of a good way to scale this down so it plays well solo?

:thumbsdown::thumbsup: Components have gotten a bit of a bad rap around here.  The cards could be better, they are on par with Onirim 2.0, but since you don&#039;t shuffle these cards very often (once per game), it&#039;s not the end of the world.  If you&#039;re worried, you can sleeve.  The rest of the components are great.  Nice heavy cardboard for the character mats and Enterprise mat.  The printing is done very well.  Nice quality dice too.

:thumbsup: It&#039;s just plain fun.  Sometimes you have to drop everything to resolve an urgent mission, sometimes you can&#039;t talk to your fellow players, sometimes the dice love you (or hate you)...it has a feel of Escape: The Curse of the Temple meets Pandemic.  It really is a lot of fun.
</body>

	<item id="4120553" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="59946" 			
			objectname="Dungeons &amp; Dragons: Castle Ravenloft Board Game"
			username="Jokemeister" 
			postdate="Sun, 06 Sep 2015 13:12:27 +0000" 
			editdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 04:45:12 +0000"
			thumbs="38"
						imageid="660244">
	<body>Felt like a dungeon crawl so I pulled this out for a quick run.  This time around, the Cleric, Ranger and Wizard wandered into Castle Ravenloft to deal with Count Strahd&#039;s new monster - a Flesh Golem!!!

[ImageID=2656095 medium]

Things did not get off to a good start as I first came up against a Wraith.

[ImageID=2656097 medium]

Followed by a Gargoyle!

[ImageID=2656098 medium]

After defeating that first Wraith, I drew another one.  Good thing as having 2 wraiths activating at the same time could have resulted in a premature end to my quest.

[ImageID=2656099 medium]

The MVP in this game was, by far, the Cleric.  The Cleric was constantly in the thick of battle and his Flame Strike allowed me to clear rooms ...

[ImageID=2656100 medium]

Shortly after, he managed to level up which gave him an additional daily power.  Useful as he ended the game with all of his Daily and Utility powers used.

[ImageID=2656101 medium]

The Cleric even managed to find the Workshop which resulted in the villain reveal!  Which means its time for - Dramatic Dungeon Lighting!

[ImageID=2656102 medium]

This resulted in a running battle as the Flesh Golem made for the dungeon entrance while we chased after it, trying to calm it down.

The Ranger got knocked down by the Golem and we had no healing surges left.  By this time, we had managed to find 2 calm tokens for the Golem and there were 2 tokens left to choose from (the other 2 having been spied as being enrage tokens).  I had one last chance for the Cleric to act to try and win the game.  

If I guess correctly and showed the correct item, I would calm down the Golem and win the game.  If I showed the wrong item, the Ranger would act next and without a healing surge, the game would end with a loss.

[ImageID=2656103 medium]

I chose - well!!  I managed to calm the golem and win in the final act of the game!  Woot!

[b]Final thoughts[/b]
This is one of my favourite quests in the game for 2 reasons.  Firstly, the Flesh Golem mini is a great mini and looks awesome on the board.  As a general rule, I love quests which result in a final battle against a massive monster - what better way to end the quest!  Secondly, I love how the quest climaxes in a running battle through the dungeon as you try and keep up with the Golem as it heads for the entrance, only pausing occasionally to knock you back into the dungeon.  

Plus, I have this fantastic image in my head of the Dwarven Cleric running on stubby legs to keep up with the long strides of the Golem while frantically searching his backpack for various items which might calm the Golem down!

Edit: Thx to Suzy, I now know how to make these images [size=18]bigger[/size]! :cool:</body>

	<item id="4120768" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="175334" 			
			objectname="The Undercity: An Iron Kingdoms Adventure Board Game"
			username="Zouave" 
			postdate="Sun, 06 Sep 2015 15:46:44 +0000" 
			editdate="Sun, 06 Sep 2015 15:53:12 +0000"
			thumbs="33"
						imageid="2514461">
	<body>Hey, there&#039;s a new game out with really cool minis.  Thanks, but I already have enough.

It&#039;s fully co-op.  Hmmm.

With a persistent campaign, including branching side quests.  Oh....

And it has a steampunk theme.  Sold!
 
So it was, after watching Doug Herring&#039;s play through video series, that I purchased [thing=175334][/thing].  So far I&#039;ve finished the first mission and I like what I see so far.  The combat is several notches below what I like in game such as [thing=140519][/thing], but there are still enough choices each turn, and enough differentiating between the four characters, to keep it interesting.  The AI is also pretty good.

Kurt B. has already written up a very good summary of the game, so for that I direct you here:

https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/1429282/my-new-favorite-co-op-time-being

I&#039;ll provide some pics below of my mission.

Here is that board that comes with the game.

[imageid=2656179 large]

Here is what it looks like after you set up the mission.

[imageid=2656187 large]

You can see some villain spawning areas to the west and northeast, as well as a possible side quest to pick up in the east.

The mission involves making your way to the dead body surrounded by four thugs in the north, and searching it while there are no villains in the space.  Once done, one of two possible bosses will appear for the final fight.

I&#039;m doing something with this campaign I rarely do: playing all four characters.  It&#039;s partly for the novelty, partly because each is so interesting I found it hard to leave any out, and partly because the ergonomics of the game allow it.  The playing area footprint is manageable.

I should highlight one character in particular, because it is in fact two: Pog and Doorstop.      

[imageid=2656230 large]

Doorstop is a huge Steamjack with a fearsome melee attack.  On his own, though, he can do no more than stand still or move one space.  Pog, however, can use one of his action to order Doorstop to do other things, such as charge.

All character have innate abilities they can use each turn, as well as Feat cards they can use to get additional bonuses or actions.  It allows for lot of choices to be made each turn.  The other three characters are a range attack specialist (Canice the Gun Mage Duelist), an alchemist with good AOE attacks (Milo the Cutthroat Alchemist) and a tanky type (Gardek the Trollkin Warrior).  In this first mission, we are up against crossbowmen and sword thugs, until the boss appears.

[imageid=2656233 large]

The characters activate in initiative order, and a turn consists spawning a villain, taking actions, and then drawing a Villain Action card to see what they will do.  Each round begins with an Event, which might introduce things such as Fog, that makes ranged attacks more difficult.

Canice began by using a Feat to advance two spaces and shoot at the thugs near the body.  She took out only one, and then two thugs charged her, but missed in their attacks.

[imageid=2656238 large]

Milo advanced next, joining Canice and tossing a bomb into the body space, killing a thug.

[imageid=2656247 large]

Pog then ordered Doorstop to charge, and he pulverized the two swordsman with his mace and shield.  Pog held back, as he planned to race to the east to pick up the side quest.  During this turns, the enemy was mainly activating crossbowmen and peppering my heroes with crossbolts.

[imageid=2656249 large]

Finally Gardek advanced two spaces, and when a sword thug activated to charge him he used a counter-charge Feat to intercept and kill the thug.

[imageid=2656275 large]

The Event deck serves as a timer, and we were about 2/3 of the way through it when Gardek finally managed to search the body with no villains present.  At that point, an Epic Ogrun (aka orc) Boss appeared, accompanied by two crossbowmen and two sword thug.

[imageid=2656276 large]

By this time, every crossbowman in the mission was on the board, and we were being continually bombarded by a grand battery of bolts.  We finally put together some well-orchestrated uses of Feats and abilities to take down the boss, capped off by a boosted acid flask attack from Milo, and the boss went down.

[imageid=2656278 large]

My heroes will actually carry some of their wounds over to the next mission, as you heal only three hits between them.  I can see already that the next mission will play out completely differently, giving me high hopes for the rest of the campaign.  I also get to use the XPs gained during the mission to buy Feat and ability upgrades.

I initially overlooked this game because it is listed as 2-4 players.  In fact, it is perfectly solo-able, and I am liking it so far.
</body>

<comment username="Zouave" date="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 13:12:47 +0000" postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 13:12:47 +0000" editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 13:13:59 +0000" thumbs="2">
My watching of game play videos of Super Dungeon Explore also turned me off it.

After thinking about Undercity for a bit, I realized the game it most resembles is [thing=138431][/thing].  It&#039;s got a scripted campaign, heroes that level up their abilities and AI actions that are determined by drawing cards.  Sometimes a villain right next to you won&#039;t activate because of the card draw, something I recall happening in GD.

Then there was this sword thug, who evidently graduated from the Imperial Stormtrooper School of Accuracy and Aiming.  He was in the same space as Canice the Gun Mage Duelist for almost half the mission, and never was able to land a blow.

[imageid=2657675 large]

Another minor thing to note: some of the board is interactable (sp?).

This poor crossbow thug was standing in a passage with loose rocks.  Milo tosses a bomb into the space.

[imageid=2657682 large]

Not only is the crossbowman gone, but the bomb also managed to hit the rocks, thereby turning them into rubble.  Rough terrain uses all movement points to enter.  I did this to slow down any boss who might enter from the connected spawn point.  In fact, none did.  But, as Big Jim McBob and Billy Sol Hurok used to say, the passageway blowed up real good!

[imageid=2657687 large]
</comment>

	<item id="4121166"

			objectname="Unpublished Prototype"

I hope things go better me on the next game.

This mat is used to place all cards drawn during the coarse of your game, so you don&#039;t really need, it but it&#039;s very thematic and puts your mind into the story. The solo game turned out to be a significant little game in itself that we will make it available to order on the website later this year. It won&#039;t be retail however...[/q]

	<body>I really enjoyed this solo variant.  Has a great flow and is very intuitive.  

Details here:  [listitem=4114077][/listitem]

:thumbsup: D&amp;D Dice Masters is a great addition to the Dice Masters family.  It&#039;s nice to have an alternative theme to comics (and I&#039;m really not interested in Yu-Gi-Oh).  The art is well done and the thematic abilities are great.  Dragons are especially fun.

:thumbsup: Solid solo variant that&#039;s easy to learn, easy to memorize and replicates an opponent very well.  

:thumbsup: Fun to set up, picking characters is one of my favorite parts, and looking at the all pretty dice on the table

:thumbsup: Quick and satisfying game play.  

:thumbsdown: I might have spent a crazy amount of money on this because I&#039;m a bit of a collector with some things (ahem, Dice Masters and LOTR:LCG...).  You can definitely get a ton a great play out of just a base game and a few booster packs, but oh my I have no discipline when it comes to &quot;just say no to the gravity feed&quot;

:thumbsup: Opening gravity feeds is one of the most fun things ever!

:thumbsdown: Booster pack cards are often bent up a bit.  Card quality isn&#039;t stellar.  

:thumbsup: Did I mention all the pretty dice?  :D

	<item id="4121437" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="140620" 			
			objectname="Lewis &amp; Clark"
			username="Moe45673" 
			postdate="Sun, 06 Sep 2015 23:38:12 +0000" 
			editdate="Sun, 06 Sep 2015 23:39:15 +0000"
			thumbs="32"
						imageid="1902092">
	<body>Just a quick report. Was at my parents over the weekend and my sister was in town with her husband and  two little ones. I broke this out to play alone and my 3 year old nephew, who&#039;s pretty rambunctious and loves attention, asked if he could play. I said sure and he climbed on my lap. 

We were obviously playing two different games. I was playing Lewis &amp; Clark while he would cheer when I filled up my boats with resources (which is actually not a good thing :D ) saying &quot;yay, you filled up the last spaces!&quot;. Or, when I&#039;d say something like &quot;I need a canoe&quot; he&#039;d point at the plano and go &quot;they&#039;re in there!&quot;

I played on the easiest level and won. As I saw the game was coming to a close, I threw out a strength 3 scout-movement card and played the 3 canoes I had in stock, jumping me forward 12 spaces from the mountains, then 7 spaces back for time spent. Ending just ahead of Fort Clatsop, I beat Mackenzie by 1. 

Since I was a little distracted this game and I couldn&#039;t find any privacy to play, I wasn&#039;t totally into this session. That&#039;s not a statement about the game, rather the session. It&#039;s awesome picking out cards and figuring out the best way to combine them. Almost, dare I say it, Mage Knight-esque.

My nephew is adorable. At one point, he looks up at me from the game with his big blue eyes and goes &quot;I love you&quot;. So yeah, I got to play a game and, aside from the distraction of a little boy on my lap commenting throughout the game (which negatively affected the engrossment/immersion that us sologamers find so addictive), it was time well spent. 

This post is actually the kind that I would hate to read as I love to learn real thoughts about various games and this one has almost nil. However, I know some of you love emotional &quot;Awwww&quot; stories so here you go, one from me :)

:thumbsdown: In the solo game, it&#039;s really hard to keep track of moving Mackenzie!

Next game, Mackenzie is starting one space up from me!</body>

	<item id="4121816" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="79131" 			
			objectname="Star Trek: Expeditions"
			username="BitJam" 
			postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 04:22:13 +0000" 
			editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 04:22:13 +0000"
			thumbs="17"
						imageid="1021598">
	<body>While I am [b]waiting[/b] for [url=https://boardgamegeek.com/boardgame/172737/high-frontier-3rd-edition]High Frontier (3rd Edition)[/url] to arrive I&#039;ve been playing light to midweight space-based games.   I have limited energy so my brain gets foggy after about 45 minutes or an hour.   My will power probably goes down as well so it is hard to drag myself away from games even when I realize I&#039;m becoming incapacitated.

[i]Star Trek: Expeditions[/i] has gotten mixed reviews.  Radho liked it and several people have said it was similar to [i]Pandemic[/i] which I quite enjoy.  After playing ST:E I would say it is more like a very light version of [i]Eldritch Horror[/i] because you move around and buff up characters while you try to accomplish several simultaneous goals by passing tests that involve buffs and dice.  I quite enjoyed it and I look forward to playing it some more.

After reading up on BGG I decided to play with [i]Uhura[/i] and [i]Kirk[/i] on the medium difficulty setting.   I would have Uhura mostly stay on the ship and scrye the energize deck (she can give cards to other players much like Charlie &quot;Citizen&quot; Kane in EH) while Kirk has his usual adventures on the ground.  I also planned to buff up the Enterprise as early as I could.  There are two timers in this game.  One of them is the Star Date which simply counts down.  The other is a space battle between a beefy Klingon Bird of Prey and a rather wimpy Enterprise.    If the Enterprise gets kicked around too much then lots of bad things happen.

Well, my battle plan did not survive the opening teaser of this episode.   It started out with Kirk beaming down to pick up a Klingon Frequency Pad to boost the shields of the Enterprise.  But it was a trap and Kirk is immediately kidnapped by the rebels!  This is bad because while he is trapped the Star Date keeps ticking down.  Uhura must beam down to rescue him as soon as possible or else this is going to be a very short episode.  

Unfortunately the transporter is on the blink so she is stuck on the Enterprise and has to [b]wait[/b] until her next turn to beam down.  The transporters were flaky throughout the episode and this really hurt the team in the early going.   There was still no way for Kirk to free himself so all he could do was get Energize cards and [b]wait[/b] for rescue.

I tried to apply a rule of thumb I learned from [url=https://boardgamegeek.com/boardgame/37046/ghost-stories]Ghost Stories[/url]: don&#039;t roll the dice unless you don&#039;t need them or almost don&#039;t need them.   In GS, if you fail, you just lose an action but in ST:E you lose an action [i]and[/i] a health when you fail.    So Uhura beams down to get some Rebel Artifacts that should help her free Kirk.  Unfortunately, right after she leaves the ship the Klingons get their disrupter working so the Enterprise Shields are useless!    This is bad ...

[url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hdjL8WXjlGI]ROLL OPENING SEQUENCE[/url]:
[IMG]http://images.mentalfloss.com/sites/default/files/styles/article_640x430/public/TOSopeninglogo_5.png[/IMG]

Notice that every part of my initial strategy failed early on.  The Enterprise had become a sitting duck and Kirk was trapped and useless.  Uhura had to first free Kirk and then beam back up to the ship to find the correct shield frequencies to prevent an early demise of the Enterprise and the episode.    She had already assembled a team that was good at Operations to rescue Kirk and this same team would help her fix the shields to defeat the disrupter and save the Enterprise.

It was only after Uhura had put out all of these fires that the team could start to work on solving the 9 missions needed to win the game.  Unfortunately the episode was already halfway over.  Since many of the missions have a clock associated with them (they need to be completed before certain Star Dates) we solved almost every mission poorly which resulted in very few victory points.   After some missteps and other adventures, we were finally able to beef up the Enterprise and it could hold its ground against the Bird of Prey.  This was fortunate because we did so poorly on all the missions that if the Enterprise had been beaten back then the game would have been lost.   We were able to eek out a Pyrrhic victory: Nibia joined the Klingon Empire; civil war erupted with the rebels controlling central parts of the planet; and there were many deaths due to permanent damage to the ecosystem.

As I said, I really enjoyed it and I look forward to playing again.  I liked it much better than [url=https://boardgamegeek.com/geeklist/194479/item/4100357#item4100357]solo Alien Frontiers[/url].

:thumbsup: It is relatively inexpensive now
:thumbsdown: This is partly due to the fact that it is unlikely there will ever be a &quot;real&quot; (mission) expansion for it.  Think of a very light [i]Eldritch Horror[/i] with no expansions.

:thumbsup: It has some very high quality components
:thumbsdown: The location cards are large and don&#039;t match a standard sleeve size.  I may  end up laminating them like the location tiles for [url=https://boardgamegeek.com/boardgame/79127/star-trek-fleet-captains]Star Trek: Fleet Captains[/url].

:thumbsup: It&#039;s Star Trek!
:thumbsdown: ... The 2009 reboot that is.  I enjoy Trek but I am not a big fan so I don&#039;t really differentiate between the original and the reboot.  For me, the game played like an episode of TOS and didn&#039;t really correspond to the reboot.   If this matters to you then just don&#039;t look real closely at the images on the role cards.  Or use the fan-made [url=https://boardgamegeek.com/filepage/107139/tos-cards-clix-values]TOS role cards[/url].

:thumbsdown: IMO Clix sucks.  I would much prefer clear bases.
:thumbsup: There are fan-made cards that have the Clix values so you don&#039;t need to use the adult-proof Clix bases.

[b]Notes:[/b]
Here is a [url=http://redlettermedia.com/plinkett/star-trek/star-trek-09/]very long review[/url] comparing the reboot with the original.  It can be vulgar and offensive as well as insightful.   You might also want to look at the comparison in [url=https://www.claremont.org/article/the-politics-of-star-trek/]the Politics of Star Trek[/url].</body>

<comment username="reverendunclebastard" date="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 17:13:28 +0000" postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 17:13:28 +0000" editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 17:48:56 +0000" thumbs="2">
[q=&quot;Lumpy75&quot;]I&#039;ve very keen to get this printed and onto the table.  Is there a summary of which ships are needed (and how many) somewhere?[/q]

Basically you need the following:

1 x Lambda Shuttle, Decimator, Tie Interceptor, Rebel Transport, 1 Hawk, 1 Millennium Falcon

Plus the following:

2 x tie fighters for each rebel ship (i.e. 2 for a 1 rebel ship playthrough, 4 for 2 rebel ships, etc.)
1 x tie bomber, tie defender, tie phantom, tie interceptor for each rebel ship

Keep in mind that in each mission some ships enter during later turns, so you will probably have killed Tie Fighter models that can be returned to the field.

The designer suggests that you can proxy for ships you don&#039;t have, or replace them with a ship you do, although that may affect the difficulty.

It is also possible to print out the AI cards and the Pilot cards and just use them to fight standard dogfights.

I am running a two rebel ship campaign. I am lucky that I have mostly collected Imperial ships as that is what I fly FtF. I think I have enough ships currently to run a three-person campaign.
</comment>

	<body>Mission 2: After a few weeks of sitting on my table, I finally had a chance to replay it using the same 3 heroes.

[q][b]Thoughts after 5 plays:[/b] I&#039;m wrong. This is a top 20 game. I expect it to hang on in there and just about make my top 20. Box could be smaller though.[/q]

:thumbsdown: A high score game so that won&#039;t be for everyone - it shouldn&#039;t be for me!

:thumbsdown: It&#039;s a smallish box but it could still be much smaller, say the size of the Harbour box.</body>

	<body>[b]Print On Demand #1: The Massing at Osgiliath[/b]

Deck 1: Eowyn, Dunhere, Prince Imrahil
Deck 2: Beravor, Gimli, Legolas

Well this was one hell of a quest to start back on after a few months away! I heard that this was hard and it didn&#039;t disappoint with six enemies in the staging area before the quest had even started.

The first few rounds were very shaky. A lack of allies meant that by the time the initial onslaught of enemies had been dealt with the heroes were all injured and down to 1 or 2 hit points left. Progress was slow in attempting to cross the Anduin.

Suddenly the tide turned when Legolas gained the Steward of Gondor and Beravor a Song of Battle resulting in a plethora of eagle allies and support cards joining the fight.

Having not read the quest cards the requirement to discard a hero or ranger to be able to quest came as a bit of a shock. Thankfully one of the rangers had already joined out party and the other made an appearance straight after starting to cross the Anduin. However, both were on the more combat  orientated player deck. With no enemies in sight the heroes successfully crossed the river... only to face the Witch-king.

This turned out to not be a problem as by now Gimli was a defending monster! Two Unexpected Courage, Support Of The Eagles (which allowed him to add +4 to defense or attack) and a Citadel Plate meant that he was able to deal with anything thrown at him and it wasn&#039;t long before the heroes were in the safety of Minas Tirith.

Result: [b][COLOR=#00CC00]Success![/COLOR][/b]
Final Score: [b]174[/b]

Thoroughly enjoyed playing this quest and it certainly got the pulse racing a few times when defeat looked inevitable. Would have been nice to defeat the Witch-king. I had the attack to do it but the requirement to raise the defending players threat by 3 to keep them engaged would have knocked them out. But now, onward to Moria...</body>

<comment username="reverendunclebastard" date="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 17:16:21 +0000" postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 17:16:21 +0000" editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 17:16:21 +0000" thumbs="3">
[q=&quot;philmcd&quot;]I have played about 20 games on yucata.de so far, 2/3/4 players and so far my scores have ranged between 18 and 36 (you don&#039;t get ranked other than yucata&#039;s system).

There is a fair amount of luck both in what tiles are available on your turn and what you roll on your dice, but it is good lite fun.[/q]

I can get a gauge of how &quot;luck based&quot; a game is when I play against my girlfriend. She tends to beat me most of the time when we play. A game like Run, Fight or Die is clearly luck based because we each win about half the time. Nations: The Dice Game, however, she beats me a good 70% of the time, so while luck is involved, strategy is clearly important!
</comment>

	<item id="4122648" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="142854" 			
			objectname="Infection: Humanity&#039;s Last Gasp"
			username="garyrbrooks" 
			postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 15:49:24 +0000" 
			editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 15:49:24 +0000"
			thumbs="21"
						imageid="1666140">
	<body>I played my first two games of this since May.

My first game was a quick victory on Bacterial level just to remind me of the rules/gameplay.  I managed to win after just 9 rounds (as quick as I ever have) mainly due to the extra funding on this level and the mutations going in my favour too.

Time to step it up to Viral level.

This time it wasn&#039;t over quickly and it was epic.

The game lasted 21 rounds (my longest ever) and I came so close to winning and completing all the molecules (never done that before).

In round 20 I had to roll a 6 on the containment check to give me a chance of getting the 2 proteins I needed next round. I did it! Yay!

When refreshing the protein pool though I drew neither of the proteins I needed.  I then bought a lab equipment card card that allowed me to change all the proteins if I rolled a 4-6.  Rolled a 3.  Then I needed to roll a 6 to have yet another round.

[ImageID=2657830 medium]I didn&#039;t roll a 6.

Two vastly different games with different feels.  The first was a quick luck driven game and the second was very tactical with me adapting to what was happening as the game went on and on.  

Luck played a part in the second game too (I set a record for rolling 6&#039;s on containment rolls) but it was how I used that extra time and how I ordered all my actions to maximise my turns that really had me enjoying the experience.  I felt like I was in a lab under growing pressure to get things done as the world slowly succumbed to the virus. 

I&#039;d forgotten how entertaining this could be and how thematic.

:thumbsup: Thematic and when it&#039;s not over too quickly it can be a pressure cooker of an experience (in a good way).

:thumbsdown: It uses dice rolls for certain checks and they can sometimes be a little swingy. 

:thumbsdown: The cards need sleeving.</body>

  - Mission 2, Alarm 35
  - Mission 3, Alarm 36.</body>

	<item id="4122755" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="101785" 			
			objectname="D-Day Dice"
			username="schiavonir" 
			postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 17:06:39 +0000" 
			editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 17:06:39 +0000"
			thumbs="20"
						imageid="1206256">
	<body>I listen to a lot of audiobooks in the car, and for the past several months, I&#039;ve been listening to &quot;The Rise and the Fall of the Third Reich&quot; (Amazon link: http://goo.gl/MvUH7q) so needless to say I&#039;ve been pretty engrossed in WWII history.  And then reading about so many wargames on this list, and elsewhere, has me longing to add my first wargame to my collection.  

There are a number of popular wargames played were, and it seems like most of them are out of print and/or very expensive.  I don&#039;t normally like dice games, but I am warming up to them (and my son likes to chuck dice, so that helps warm me as well) and as long as there&#039;s luck-mitigation and choices, dice are okay.

So put all those ingredients into the pot and stir it up and what do you get?  I started looking for D-Day Dice.  I found it in good condition for under $30 shipped on http://boardgameco.com/ for under $30, but didn&#039;t jump on it fast enough and then next available copies shot up to $45 shipped.  A day before I had seen a deal on eBay for both the base game and the Atlantik Wall expansion, so without hesitation after losing the first deal, I jumped on it.

I played a number of training missions, losing time and time again, finally figured out that I needed to take it slowly and build up as many men as possible before advancing too far.  Finally played the full-on Exercise Tiger scenario and won!  

Bunker: 20
First in bunker: 20
Last Sector: 10*10=100
Soldiers: 13
Courage: 0
Specialists: 2*3=6
Awards: 1*10=10
Total: 169

The first 140 points is a gimme in the solo game, so I guess the 29 points I scored after that is what really matters.

I&#039;m excited the flip the map over and lose repeatedly on the second mission before finally defeating that bunker!

I do still think there&#039;s a WWII-themed hex-and-counter solo wargame in my future, but for now I will stick with the dice.




</body>

	<body>While in San Francisco last week for a conference, I was able to get over to Gamescape, a game store on Divisadero St. Very cool store!

They had a copy of Baseball Highlights: 2045 Deluxe Edition in stock, so I picked it up.

I didn&#039;t really get a chance to play it until last night after getting back home on Saturday. Man, how cool is this game?!?

I played 2 Series, once as NY and once as SF with 2 buy rounds in each. I won the first Series (NY) 4-2; lost the second Series (SF) 4-1. Started to setup another series when I glanced at the clock and saw 2:57 am. :surprise:

There is so much more to this game than meets the eye, IMHO. It looks simple and it is in the sense that it is easy to learn, but there is depth in the decisions to be made, both during play and during the buy rounds.

I have high expectations for playing against a real person as well!

SO GLAD I picked this up.

[b]Update:[/b] Got two more series in today, both with Boston. Lost both, neither closer than 4-2. I need to get better at watching what the AI has and thinking ahead as to what is coming between shuffles...</body>

	<body>This was one of the first kickstarters I backed, and it&#039;s been sitting on a shelf unpunched since I received long ago. So I decided to unpunch it and give it a try this long holiday weekend.

It looks good, and has lots of cards and other components. The rule book is clearer than some. But once I got into the game I found myself looking for answers to questions and not finding them or maybe just not knowing where to look.

As a solo game I found it a bit dull. It&#039;s technically a co-op game, with opportunity for backstabbing and other player interaction. It might be more fun with multiple players.

I don&#039;t think I will hang onto it. For me, Castle Panic scratches a similar itch, albeit from the other side, but seems more fun as a solo game (and also a game I can get non-gamers to play on the rare occasion I have a chance).

Storm the Castle isn&#039;t a bad game. It just doesn&#039;t do it for me personally.</body>

	<item id="4123342" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="145493" 			
			objectname="The King&#039;s Armory"
			username="gentle" 
			postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 20:17:24 +0000" 
			editdate="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 18:09:51 +0000"
			thumbs="27"
						imageid="2582948">
	<body>I got this last week and I already played it 6 or 7 times.
When I first got the game, the box looked smaller than expected. Then, after setting my first game up, I was surprised by the amount of space needed on the table.

[imageid=2658169medium]

I also cut the top of the 3D towers off, the board is huge and you can&#039;t see anything behind them and can&#039;t move anything. Even in a 4 player game the others had to read everything out loud again and again until we just moved the towers out of the way when we had to move/attack with monsters at that tower.

Anyway. After a couple of tries, solo and with friends now and having lost every single time, I decided to set it up again tonight for a three character game.

[imageid=2658177medium]

[i]Valcor,[/i] the fighter! Ready to slay his enemies and protect his allys by tanking everything that came his way, self-sacrificing and probably not too smart.
[i]Ember[/i], the archer! Quick to draw and quick to fire. Raining arrows down on enemies till they resemble a pincushion. From the safety of the tower, she&#039;s brave and safe.
And then we had [i]Boleslaw[/i]. The weird, strange kid who nobody wanted to be friends with and was always up to no good. He lurked in the tower, never leaving them, making flying monsters drop from the sky or slowing them down for Valcor to kill them.

The archer&#039;s really good on one tower, basically killing everything coming her way in wave 1 and 2 without any problems. Valcor tanks and kills everything coming his way and healing up between waves without any problems (at least in the frist few waves).
I&#039;ve never played Boleslaw before which is the main reason why I decided to pick him. He can never leave the tower but can teleport to another tower and has some nice surprises for the monsters and can help a lot. I hope.

The first wave of monster appears:
[imageid=2658192medium]

The heroes looked at the goblins and orc and laughed. That was hardly worth their time! Valcor just let the goblin walk up to him and held his sword ready. The poor creature practically skewered and killed itself! The archer was having a great time doing target practice. And just like that, it was over. Easy. Way too easy!
But who cares, we got the gold! Showing foresight, which does not happen too often, a cleric was drafted and joined our ranks. A healer! There were more monsters coming and sooner or later we were bound to receive some wounds.

Then the next wave of monsters appeared:
[imageid=2658202medium]

A siege engine! That stirred everyone up for a second but it moved so slowly, every monster who tried to hurry it along was quickly killed that it didn&#039;t prove to be a threat at all!
Quickly, every foe was vanguished and the heroes looked at each other, underwhelmed. That was an easy job they were hired for apparently. Which was alright for them!

The cleric got some experience from the fight and was better able to wield his abilites and Valcor bought a net to catch flying monsters. 

So far things were looking good, but the heroes could already hear another batch of monsters assembling in the forest, making their way to the dwarven gate.


[size=18][b]update: wave 3![/b][/size]

8 foes appeared. Two siege engines again! And one flying monster. I had Valcor, the fighter and tank positioned to the east with the cleric, the other three were all on the western tower or in front of it.
Only two monsters decided to go for Valcor. A measly goblin (Level 1) and a flying monster. But Valcor had his net ready, catching it and dragging it to the ground!
The others tanked two monsters, the siege engines were really slow and only came towards the end, the last monster was ignored. It tried to attack my hired swordsman but missed.
Valcor quickyl dispatched of his foes (with a critical hit and never missing one of his other rolls) and was ready to rush to the aid of the others.
All things considered that was one of the easiest Level 3 Waves I&#039;ve ever had! And all thanks to Boleslaw!
His ability to make primary attacks supernatural damage was key to it! Valcor destroyed one siege engine alone in just one round! He hit critically, which meant 10 damage to it. The rest was easy!

With the rewards, I bought a third tower, a reinforcement card that, when used, gives all my allies 2 extra actions this turn and decided to keep the rest of the gold for a future round, maybe buying an armory card after next wave.

Really great to see how all the different abiliies work together! Buffing Valcors damage to 5 and making it supernatural made Boleslaw the hero of this wave!


So far, I really really like that game! A few years ago, I played a lot of tower defence games on my computer, this game does a wonderfull job in bringing that to the table!

There&#039;s 7 heroes which all play very differently. Archer, sorcerer, cleric, tank, fighter, summoner, supporter... everything&#039;s here. And, depending on what you decide to play, you can later on hire allies to fullfill roles you didn&#039;t pick. Which is a great idea. They begin at level 1 and can go up to level 3, getting more actions and better spells/attacks.
What nearly made me back this (which I now regrett not having done) was the adjustable player count on top of all this. You start playing, a friend comes over and wants to join? No problem, just adjust the number of monsters for the next wave and the rewards. Someone has to leave? No problem, same applies. This is really neat.
If I keep playing this game that much, I&#039;ll have to try and get the kickstarter items from somewhere! It only left my table once during this week, when we played it at a friends place. Set it up again the very next day.

You can also make different maps for the monsters to take. A single path map usually is easier, make it a winding path and you make it very easy on yourself. Or make it harder, let them go in two directions and lead them straight to the castle doors.
A lot of thought has gone into this game. It really shows.

I&#039;m not too keen on some of the rules, like the starting equipment cards. Every hero gets two of them, but they are locked. You have to unlock them first, because those are only the two items the dwarves are willing to sell to you at the moment. After that, you can draw from the deck. But I have to admit, at least you know what you&#039;ll get for the first two cards and you can choose if it&#039;s worth it to you or not.

And then there&#039;s the thematic rules, which, admittedly, I still tend to forget sometimes. They are just there so you won&#039;t break the game in some situations. For instance, you only have one enemy left and don&#039;t kill him until the healer has healed everybody back to full health.
You were hired to protect the castle and its your job to kill the monsters. So you have to attack at least once or move closer to them to try and attack or prepare an attack.
For me, it wasn&#039;t a problem yet, I don&#039;t think I did anything wrong this last time.

The game itself is not that hard, the rules aren&#039;t that difficult usually, but there&#039;s always that one exception for me that I forget. But nothing mayor and not to my advantage. I think.


:thumbsup: Adjustable player count! Awesome! Lets others join or leave with clear rules so the game&#039;s still balanced!
:thumbsup: Great replayability!
:thumbsup: Without good strategy, you&#039;ll loose. Guaranteed.

:thumbsdown: Still, rolling a die. So there&#039;s quite some luck involved, too, of course
:thumbsdown: The 3D towers. They block the view. I cut 2 towers down and thats an improvement. But they still look really cheap. I&#039;d have loved some thick cardboard like in Legends of Andor.
</body>
	
			<comment username="gentle" date="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 18:16:24 +0000" postdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 18:16:24 +0000" editdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 19:03:58 +0000" thumbs="0">
[b]Wave 4 + 5:[/b]

[b]Wave 4[/b] went relativley easy. Boleslows ability to make someone else do supernatural damage and increasing it by +1 really made a difference. The archer was able to fire supernatural arrows and killed a lot of monsters.
Valcor hacked his way through his foes. The cleric was busy healing the foot soldier who nearly got killed but made it through the wave!

I decided to buy 2 more reinforcement cards, giving me three of them now in total,  since I didn&#039;t need another ally and couldn&#039;t afford the armory card anyway. Which turned out great for me!

[b]Wave 5:[/b]
Wave 5 is then the boss monsters appears, too. But in the first turn, only the monsters appear and attack. 12 monsters... the hired foot soldier was close to death after they all appeared. Playing one of my reinforcement cards that gave everyone 2 extra actions this turn proved to be a livesafer.
Valcor killed two foes, the hired footsoldier wounded one, Ember, my archer, killed one foe instantly and took another down with him. The cleric used the extra actions to heal that unlucky footsoldier up.
Then the monster moved again. After that second movement, the boss appeared. The Boss appeared in form of a giant rolling boulder!
It was pushed by an Ettin and would smash right through the doors of the castle!
In the first round though, it smashed right through my unlucky footsoldier, flattening him and crushing his bones beneath it!
Full of wrath, Valcor and Ember slew the Ettin pushing the boulder, the cleric was intelligent enough to move out of the way and tanking another foe instead.

But two runners made it to the gate, I decided to let them go. They tried to blow it up but I played another reinforcement card that allowed me to heal the gate for 7 HP. So that was alright!

I finally managed to kill every other foe and soon only the giant boulder was left. I chipped away at it (again, Boleslaws ability was amazing, because the boulder would have been immun to Embers arrows otherwise) and soon had it reduced to rubble!

Victory was mine!


First game I won and I was lucky with some of my rolls. Ember headshotting two foes, instantly killing them was great. That was fun!

</comment>

	<item id="4123365" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="168274" 			
			objectname="Mistfall"
			username="hervuli" 
			postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 20:25:16 +0000" 
			editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 20:25:16 +0000"
			thumbs="28"
						imageid="2410035">
	<body>This has been on the table a lot lately - I&#039;m up to 7-8 full plays, mostly with two characters and once with three. I&#039;ve played The Abomination and Tangled Paths scenarios and have used each character at least once.

[ImageID=2640035 medium]

I&#039;m really, really liking this game. The variety in characters is nice - there are definitely a couple that I have yet to figure out how to use to their full abilities, like Hareag - and I&#039;ve figured out the strategy well enough that I can reliably win on the basic difficulty level. The rules have become second nature; I don&#039;t think I needed to look at the rulebook more than a couple times during my most recent playthrough. The errata is still a bit of a bother, but most every game has errata and this certainly isn&#039;t any worse than, say, the first iteration of the PACG series ([thing=133038]Rise of the Runelords[/thing] had a ton of errata and that didn&#039;t stop me from enjoying it).

[ImageID=2657908 medium]

I really liked my 3-handed play of Tangled Paths - I played with Ardenai, Fengray and Hareag. The variety of abilities made for some fun strategies and combos, particularly with Fengray pulling as many enemies into his area as possible and Ardenai picking them off at range. I&#039;ve seen some criticisms that the card combos are a bit too obvious and get repetitive, but I haven&#039;t experienced that yet (maybe I&#039;m just not smart enough to figure them out that quickly).

[ImageID=2657909 medium]

I would definitely like to see more quests - I&#039;ll probably start replaying some of these at higher difficulty levels but I&#039;m not sure how long that will hold my interest. So I guess what I&#039;m really saying is, if and when there are expansions published, they&#039;ll be auto-buys for me :)

[ImageID=2654566 medium]

Long story short, if you don&#039;t mind purely deterministic combat, i.e. you like Mage Knight-style puzzles instead of (or along with) PACG-style dicefests, this is probably a game that will work for you.</body>

<comment username="hervuli" date="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 21:33:13 +0000" postdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 21:33:13 +0000" editdate="Mon, 07 Sep 2015 21:33:13 +0000" thumbs="0">
[q=&quot;gentle&quot;]I watched a few runthroughs, the theme seemed right up my alley but they all made it look so boring.[/q]

Out of curiosity - what made it look boring to you? I could see some being turned off by the deterministic combat, but I&#039;m assuming that if the Mage Knight comparisons are a draw for you, that&#039;s not the problem.

To be fair, Mistfall zooms in on only one part of Mage Knight - the combat. The exploration and all the different things you can do in MK (recruit, pillage, attack different kinds of fortifications, etc) aren&#039;t there in Mistfall. But the combat is a lot more detailed as a result.

	<item id="4124105" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="146574" 			
			objectname="The Lord of the Rings: The Card Game â€“ The Voice of Isengard"
			username="hervuli" 
			postdate="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 04:15:23 +0000"

	<body>After playing a ton of [thing=142875]The Black Riders[/thing] recently, I got back into the regular adventure cycles for the LotR LCG, continuing my chronological play-through with The Voice of Isengard. I got trounced by the first scenario, The Fords of Isen, with a pre-constructed hobbit deck that was totally unprepared for the new mechanics that punish you for having lots of cards in your hand. In response I crafted the below Spirit/Lore dual-sphere deck, which is optimized to have as few cards in hand as possible.

It&#039;s built around Elrond/Vilya (which can put cards into play directly from the deck, without them being in hand), Eowyn (whose ability can discard cards from the hand to add to her willpower), and Spirit Glorfindel (who is, well, Spirit Glorfindel). It has basically no events - the rationale being that events tend to stick around in hand until the moment they&#039;re needed, which is Bad News for this quest. The only event here is Elrond&#039;s Counsel, a zero-cost card that can be beneficially played at almost any time.

Spirit and Lore don&#039;t have much in the way of combat abilities, so I splashed in a few Tactics allies who can be paid for by Elrond or simply put into play with Vilya. Most cards in the deck are low-cost so I can put them into play ASAP. The high-cost allies (Beorn, Gildor Inglorion, Northern Tracker, Gandalf) can be either played via Vilya or discarded via Eowyn if I can&#039;t afford to pay for them.

Results? Beat all three Voice of Isengard scenarios with this one, including an utter demolition of Into Fangorn, which I managed to win in four turns. To Catch an Orc was a bit trickier with this deck, because the optimization is all wrong (the &quot;hand hate&quot; mechanic isn&#039;t present and more card draw would be helpful), but I still won 1 out of 2 tries.

Here&#039;s the deck...

	<body>After that crushing defeat with [thing=42776][/thing], I might as well try something a little lighter to help build my confidence.  Of course, instead I pulled out [thing=28829][/thing].  Being only my second time playing, I thought I would try out the Ghost Division campaign again.  Now that I&#039;m comfortable with the rules and the counters, I&#039;m not referencing the rulebook as often and the game plays even quicker... especially when I get demolished.

By the end of the 4th round or so, I was starting to feel pretty good about myself.  I had managed to move forces steadily to the west, quickly taking and holding Paris and then even Cambrai, followed by Arras!  Woohoo, 2/3rds of the way there, right?  Well the reinforcements out of Calais changed that almost immediately and overwhelmed my puny 25th Pz and 78th Art rather quickly.

This game is such a blast.  I love the tension every turn, but wow, is it tough.  Seeing that Allied Operations box fill up with forces and then burst open with a &quot;Go!&quot; chit is brutal.  I honestly don&#039;t see even a hint of victory anywhere in sight, but that won&#039;t stop me from playing it.  It sets up quick and I can bang out a game (...er, defeat) in about an hour.  I can&#039;t wait to try it again.</body>

	<item id="4124149" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="182250" 			
			objectname="Pocket Adventure"
			username="radchad" 
			postdate="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 05:00:02 +0000" 
			editdate="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 05:00:02 +0000"
			thumbs="19"
						imageid="1657689">
	<body>My path takes me deep through the woodlands of Gorand&#039;s pass. There are plentiful goblins and  wolves in these parts and although I have some skill with an Iron Hatchet,  I have lost some of my resolve for the path of adventure. I am still hopeful.  A cold wind blows through the air and it chills me to the bones.

Soon into my path a wolf attacks. I make a reckless attack, but it succeeds in killing the wolf before it can attack back. I receive a fur tunic for my troubles. Then an orc soldier attacks further  down the road. I attack recklessly again and fell the cruel beast before it can attack.  I now claim an giant&#039;s tooth as my reward.

As I travel further, a storm blows in, threatening my resolve even more. I question why I make these travels. I am not sure of the gain. 

A swarm of goblins attack. I make a more cautious attack against both of them. I take a single wound for my troubles, but they are quickly dispatched. I then rest a bit, healing my wounds. Ironically, I find a priest down the road offering to heal my wounds.  I turn him down as I am healthy. He does tell me that the wolves have been behaving more aggressively as of late. There is likely a Black Fur that has moved in lately and established itself as alpha.  It looks as though I have purpose in this valley as of yet.  I continue my journey.

The storm blows harder. My resolve fades more. I doubt that my bones can take this horrible weather much longer. I feel tired.  I dispatch a wolf and a goblin with relative ease.  Another goblin is felled without any fuss. But the storm continues to blow harder and harder. I am exhausted. I cannot go on for much longer.

The vile Black Fur appears and I make a desperate attack against it. He is one vicious beast and tears into my thick leather armor leaving me in a state of hurt. But my desperate attack takes the beast down.  I am hurt. I am exhausted. But I am victorious.

I decide to make my way back to town. There are rumors of thieves about, but no matter. I must take a rest. I am ambushed by goblins in my journey back. I fight both cautious and defensively. I have nothing to prove, and these simple beasts are more or less, just in the way. Then another goblin falls.  I finally roll into a small village and rest at the inn. I regain some of my resolve, but I am still very tired.  The rest is healing and I am healthy again.

But the storm blows still and I feel exhausted again.  Still no sign of the thieves anywhere. I don&#039;t think I can manage much longer.  A begger appears. I give him something of value and he can feed himself for a month with the trading value.  My heart stirs with hope. Maybe this is not all for not.

An encounter with a Dire Wolf leaves me wounded. Time feels like it is against me.  But there is hope. The storm finally blows  over, and heavy rain falls. Hard fighting conditions, but I can manage. The rain then stops, but dark skies remain.  Stopping to rest, the skies clear up for what seems like the first time in weeks. 

I am in a cheery though exhausted disposition when I encounter my first thief.  He falls without much effort. I hope to find one more soon.  I do not succeed and retire unfulfilled in my adventures for I am too exhausted to continue.

----------------------------------------------------------------
This game is from the current Solitaire Print and Play contest. If you want to try it, then look below!

[imageid=2657966 large]

[url=https://drive.google.com/file/d/0B0WBVnUE4NbHYXNIc0FBc0F6Tmc/view?usp=sharing]Vassal Module for Pocket Adventures[/url]</body>

	<item id="4124586" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="71074" 			
			objectname="Expedition: Northwest Passage"
			username="davekuhns" 
			postdate="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 11:25:41 +0000" 
			editdate="Fri, 11 Sep 2015 01:29:37 +0000"
			thumbs="20"
						imageid="1681453">
	<body>New entry since I&#039;m finally playing this correctly! 

If it weren&#039;t for my Canadian 1 Player guild friends I&#039;d be lost. 
[user=reverendunclebastard][/user]
set me straight on this one

and [user=Moe45673][/user] set me straight on Loyang!

You guys are the best. Perhaps I should move to Canada to gain a better understanding of gaming?

Anyhow, this game, set in Canada really, is very fun and challenging. I have set myself a solo &quot;win&quot; condition. You have to get all 5 discovery tokens (1 of each) to have a &quot;win&quot;. As well as be positive in your score. Most likely if you&#039;re able to do the one the other will follow because of the little bonus you get. It&#039;s tough though!  I think the tiles do need to come out in a favorable way in order to be able to mostly use the special solo game tile drawing rule. 

I especially enjoy that this game sets up and re-sets up quickly thanks to my little Plano organizer.

Game 1 saw me get to the Passage relatively late. I had a big island in the way (which never got completed unfortunately). I saw I had a chance to get 2 sets of the discovery tokens and went for it. Apparently that particular expedition was never heard from again. All hands lost. -33. :shake:

Game 2 was a quick re-set (yay!), and I was at it again, this time vowing to be a little more conservative. I made it to the Passage in time to get the 10 points again. I worked my way back, but it was a trade off between losing the ship and all hands again or picking up some Franklin wreckage. Needless to say I made a bee-line for Groenland. I had 4/5 tokens and a final score of 0 thanks to lots of islands discovered. I benefited a lot from islands that bordered the edge of the map. That was about half of them!

:thumbsup:&#039;s and :thumbsdown:&#039;s: I&#039;m really enjoying the exploration mechanism in this game, and find the discovery tokens very thematic, except for one: the straits. Why don&#039;t I score them just for sailing through them? That seems to be how they would be &quot;discovered!&quot;  Still, quite a fun thematic package here. 


Update 9/9/15:
I got in 2 games last night. I love that about this game. Quick set up and play yet plenty of brain burn with tile selection, placement and timing. Actually 2.5 games because I had to abort one due to having placed a tile illegally and it was too late to fix.

Anyhow. Game 1 I accomplished all my goals! Except one. I got to the Passage and scored 10 pts. I got a full set of Discovery tokens and found some islands! The one thing I missed? I didn&#039;t make it back to Groenland. All hands lost. I would think that the Groenlanders would have been able to see their ship founder it was that close. Final score was -1. I think I got too greedy.

Game 2 went better. It almost went exceptionally well. I was one crew member short of getting 2 sets of Discovery tokens! I was more efficient and I didn&#039;t let my sled wander off as far as I have in the past, and was able to scoop them up and head for Groenland. I finished with a final score of 8! 
Game 2 final image: 
[ImageID=2663445large]
</body>

	<body>Played yet another game of this! This time I decided to go with 1 hero just to see if it worked as well as the marketing says it does.

Want to find out? Read on!

Just kidding, I hate when people do that. It totally worked! I played with the optional solitaire rules regarding equipment, reinforcements, and starting cash.

Wave 1:

[IMG]http://i.imgur.com/yf4rN06.jpg[/IMG]

Sorry for the bad pic quality. Done with my phone and it took me awhile to actually properly figure out how to get good pics. Anyhow, I used Ember the archer and hired a foot soldier with the starting cash. S&#039;long, baddies!

Wave 2:
[IMG]http://i.imgur.com/NZHZuuK.jpg[/IMG]

Ah yes. Notice the slight improvement in sharp edges and color. Almost like, dare I say it, I knew what I was doing. Regarding gameplay, Quinten was a beast. Using him to tank remote baddies almost made me feel bad for them. Wow, Psionics are pretty kickass! This mental clickage unlocked a whole new set of strategies for me, a way where I can finally see something approaching a session that doesn&#039;t involve me being swamped in the final wave.

Wave 3:

[IMG]http://i.imgur.com/nB7hLj2.jpg[/IMG]

Now is that a picture or what? 

&quot;Yeah, Moe, congratulations. You&#039;ve made it to the 20th century with your photography skills&quot;.

Boy, that Daniel. Jumps right into the thick of things, not noticing how low his health gets. Wait, don&#039;t say it. Don&#039;t say it!

[IMG]http://static2.fjcdn.com/comments/If+_aa9c817f242953f328bb7e7c48024574.jpg[/IMG]

Bastards.

Wave 4:

[IMG]http://i.imgur.com/sEBmxrX.jpg[/IMG]

I have taken my picture skills to &quot;Common Instagram User&quot;. I am awarded 3 XP and a crushing inferiority complex.

So I had to get Nancy (level 2 cleric). Thanks a lot, Daniel, way to make me throw money to keep your dumb ass alive. 

Wave 5:

[IMG]*placeholder*[/IMG]

Yeah, I forgot to take a pic of the start of the wave. 

&quot;We&#039;re already aware of your mental deficiencies regarding the visual arts. No need to say anything!&quot;

Shut up, Internet! I did take some more pics. Here&#039;s one of me throwing a rain of arrows on some tough baddies!

[IMG]http://i.imgur.com/FHmflNX.jpg[/IMG]

And, haha, here&#039;s one of my crushing defeat!

[IMG]http://i.imgur.com/MphKd4D.jpg[/IMG]

Wait......

So yeah, the game plays exceptionally well with 1 hero. In future, I am going to try..... four. I predict quite a bit of table space but less money going towards hireables and more towards equipment, as well as saving up for the armory card. 

Love that Quinten. What a beast. </body>

<comment username="Moe45673" date="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 17:07:31 +0000" postdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 17:07:31 +0000" editdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 17:58:10 +0000" thumbs="2">
My one negative about the game. It takes about 3 hours...... but part of that is rule referencing and stuff (what actually takes a long time is, not necessarily finding the rule, but rather interpreting rules and wondering if you even need to do a rule lookup at times). I&#039;ve also tended to stack the &quot;1&quot; hitpoints under characters and the time doing that adds up. I think using the &quot;5&quot; and &quot;10&quot; hitpoint tokens, while less visually cool, should speed that up.  I&#039;m guessing it takes the designer 135 minutes to play a 5 Wave campaign. 

Part of me thinks &quot;I could be playing Mage Knight during this time&quot; but the other part of me is happy to play a game with lots of hacking and slashing and minimal brainburn. I can leave the game and come back to it later and not be all &quot;ok, what the heck was my plan again???&quot;. 

The good news is, more people shouldn&#039;t lengthen the time it takes to play. When the fiddlier bits can be divvied up amongst multiple people, that should speed things up!

I do think this would be a lot of fun co-op. I love games where you can support your teammates well (one reason I really enjoy XCOM). 
</comment>

You&#039;d think so........ But they&#039;re really straightforward. They mean (top to bottom, left to right)

Range
Number to add to attack roll
Damage dealt
Health
Movement
Defense
Melee resistance
Ranged resistance
Supernatural resistance

<comment username="airjudden" date="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 16:50:29 +0000" postdate="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 16:50:29 +0000" editdate="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 16:50:29 +0000" thumbs="6">
[q=&quot;Longbombed&quot;]What did you think of it as a solo game?[/q]

I like it.  The game is basically [thing=99698][/thing] with a LOT more cards for added variability.  The game has multi-player rules, but it&#039;s basically multi-player solitaire.

However, a couple of days ago, I was hanging out with the designer, who showed me a 2-4 player variant that he and a buddy was making.  It turned this game from a Euro solitaire to a multi-player 4X wargame, and let me tell you...THAT was awesome.  Stay tuned for his release of the rules.

Keep in mind I&#039;m a wargamer through and through, so anything that lets me bash my opponents and conquer his systems is always going to score a lot of points with me.

<comment username="LaggingEdge" date="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 00:09:58 +0000" postdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 00:09:58 +0000" editdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 00:09:58 +0000" thumbs="6">
I&#039;ve had good results battling musty/smokey smells in old games by following this recipe:

- Get a wide, shallow plastic bin with a lid.
- Line the bottom with charcoal briquettes.
- Spread a few layers of newspaper on top. 
- Spread the game components out on top of the newspaper and sprinkle liberally with baking soda. 
- Snap on the lid and let sit 2-3 days. 
- Brush off the components and then air them out in the open on top of some fresh newspaper for a couple more days. 
- Add salt and pepper to taste. Enjoy. (oh, wrong recipe...)
</comment>

<comment username="Gizensha" date="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 19:45:16 +0000" postdate="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 19:45:16 +0000" editdate="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 19:47:12 +0000" thumbs="1">
[q=&quot;Cardboard Conundrum&quot;]I only picked up Onirim quite recently, but have had my eye on this one too. Are the games similar at all - bar their artwork? [/q]

They&#039;re similarly light, at least before you pull in any of the expansion modules (Of which Onirim has significantly more), though mechanically very different.

Mechanically I think I&#039;d probably compare Sylvion to the video game Plants vs Zombies - This is a lane based tower defense game. A weirdly surreal one, where you&#039;re fighting fire elementals with fountains, growing trees to replenish your base at the end of the game, and moving the fire elementals into different lanes by having whales carry them in their mouths, but a lane based tower defense game at it&#039;s core.

For me, at least, the theme comes across a lot stronger in Sylvion than Onirim, incidentally, though I haven&#039;t started mixing expansions in to either yet.
</comment>

It does play well solo.  I really enjoy this as a solo game.  I like that the characters can be either male or female.  I like the story aspect of it.  I like the artwork.  I like that I only need to manage a single character.  I think it is a fun game.

After I had made the purchase, I found this thread ([url]https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/1417597/alive-amazon-shadows-brimstone-both-city-ancients/page/1[/url]), showing the experiences others had had with this listing. So I hoped for the best as I [b]waited[/b] for my games to arrive from the UK, and at last a giant box arrived! My wife sent me a message at work that said â€œSwamps of Death?â€

Me: â€œJust one game?â€

Wife: â€œYes. Man, this is nerdy looking.â€

Disappointing, but their customer service was very quick to respond. Iâ€™ll be getting a full refund, and keeping Swamps of Death. I do feel bad for this company in a way; the amazon listing clearly is aware of two different games existing. The box it arrived in was even large enough that it could have fit both games :/ So I donâ€™t know where the disconnect is, but several people have had this same experience, and it has to be costing them a good deal of money.

Financial concerns aside, I am now the proud owner of this giant box and all of its contents. I spent the long weekend gluing and punching, leaving me with two sliced fingers and some reasonably well-assembled minis. This was my first experience with assembling miniatures for a game, and I think it went well.

(For more on the topic of waiting, see my latest blog post! [url]https://boardgamegeek.com/blogpost/45616/patience-gaming[/url])

			username="garyrbrooks"

			thumbs="17"
						imageid="2089536">
	<body>After I couldn&#039;t take getting beaten by Gears of war any more I turned to this lighter game.

Turned out to be only marginally friendlier.

Managed 3 games before I had to pick up the girls from school.

Started with a win against the Omniblend AI on easy. 21-15.

Then took it on at standard difficulty and lost 17-22.

Finally I tried the Sacchar AI on easy and lost 19-22.

I love this as a quick dice game with an opponent. The 2 AI&#039;s work pretty well, are different from each other and put you under pressure from the get go. You are constantly forced to choose between blending, research and sticking with your blend or abandoning it.

I wanted to get in another couple of games, including one against both AI&#039;s at the same time but ran out of time.

:thumbsup: The AI opponents work well to make this &#039;filler&#039; game a decent solo experience.

:thumbsdown: It&#039;s a dice game so if they don&#039;t work for you then this probably won&#039;t do anything to change that.

:thumbsdown: Some of the components (e.g research abilities) aren&#039;t used in the solo game.</body>

	<item id="4125507" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="119432" 			
			objectname="Snowdonia"
			username="schiavonir" 
			postdate="Tue, 08 Sep 2015 18:31:56 +0000" 
			editdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 16:08:03 +0000"
			thumbs="21"
						imageid="1430858">
	<body>Well, hopefully, the third time&#039;s the charm.

I played Snowdonia on TTS and reported on it for the August SGOYT.  I have since determined that I was playing incorrectly.  I saw no need/benefit from buying the engine so I never did.  I later came to find out that one of the major benefits of having the engine was to employ that third laborer (at the cost of one coal) - something I had been doing the whole game anyway.  So that basically invalidated my two solo plays thus far.

I liked the game so much that I bought a copy of it, and set it up last night for my first solo using the physical game.  I was nearly done when I drew a contract card that lets me take the &quot;First Player Marker&quot;. Of course, I don&#039;t care about this for a solo game, but it got me thinking - once you get this card in a multi-player game, how would anyone else ever get to go first?  So I went through the rules and BGG trying to answer this question, and discovered that you only get to use the special effects of the contract cards ONCE!  I had been using those abilities repeatedly in all my plays!  So I immediately tore down that game and set it up for another play, hopefully tonight.

One thing I noticed in this game was that if you use less than 6 resources each turn, as I often did, the bag will empty out quickly, leaving only event cubes which get played over and over, hastening the end of the game.  So that is something that I really need to manage in future games.

I did have one question - suppose there are 3 cubes left in the bag when it is time to stock the yard.  I pull an iron ore, a coal, and an event cube.  I place the event cube and resolve the event, which causes 3 more white cubes to go back into the bag.  Am I done with this phase, or do I need to draw those other 3 white cubes out to make 6 cubes total?  (I don&#039;t think you do because the book talks about if the bag doesn&#039;t have enough cubes, you just draw what you can.)

--Edit--
Third time WAS the charm.  What a challenging game when you actually play it by the rules.  I think I did pretty well, and now I&#039;m wondering how the heck I&#039;m going to beat this score 6 more times.  During this game, I didn&#039;t really keep a running score.  In future games, I will probably need to do that so I can keep an eye my target.  Maybe I should have sandbagged this one?

Full Game, Engine #1:
Completed sites: 3+7+7+9+9+14=49
Completed track: 2+2+2+5+3+3+4=21
Contract cards: 31+16+17+11=75
Surveyor: 11
Total: 49+21+75+11=156
[imageid=2661361]</body>

[b]Tow Handed[/b]
This is my first game playing this movie but it might be my favorite.  I really like the character deck and the end challenge of having two tough final enemies.  The Monster&#039;s Mother card is pretty awesome too.  Very very powerful if you get it early like I did.  This card allows you to gain a dead alien.  you get the benefit of the aliens attack value which even the weakest aliens are generally more powerful then your best character card.  Example of how powerful this card can be below.  I used this card when killing the newborn.  The Newborn is dead and now I use the Monster&#039;s Mother ability and gain the 13 attack newborn to my deck :)
[ImageID=2659924 large]
While I had the Newborn in my deck I never got a change to draw it.  Really, I didn&#039;t even need it.  With the help of two other aliens I killed the Queen.
[ImageID=2659929 large]

[b]Game:[/b] 2/3
[b]Difficulty: [/b]0 Drones, 1 hive in complex
[b]Tow Handed[/b]
Well, I got a little too brave with ramping up the difficulty.  The first hive card reveled in the complex was a Xenomorph Runner.  It made it&#039;s way to the combat zone quickly and it stayed there for a long time.  By the time I could generate a measly 4 attack, I had to use it on the facehugger drawn from the stike deck.  When I finally was able to kill the Xenomorph, two more were in the combat zone.  I never stood a chance this game.  In my final turn I drew 4 strike cards with only 4 health to spare.  First character died early in the 2nd objective.  When that happens I just call it game over.  No point trudging through the rest of the game with the other hand.

[b]Game:[/b] 3/3
[b]Difficulty: [/b]0 Drones
[b]Tow Handed[/b]
Crushed again... The first hazard card came out early and I could not get rid of it.  Another Xenomorph Runner made it into the combat zone early again and was causing the normal amount of trouble for me.  The killer was the 2nd objective event cards with 3 clones on the table.  I&#039;m not done with this movie yet...</body>
