	<body>Reported this session on the Undercity game page, but I&#039;ll add it here to the SGOYT.

After watching the videos and reading the rules, I finally found the time to set this up in my home office and started playing it.

I really like this game, even though I&#039;ve played the first scenario a few times due to mistakes that I made.  I still have some questions about ranged characters activating and I keep forgetting to use both of a character&#039;s weapons (looking at you Milo with your throwing dagger and your explosions!), but I really hope that they make more scenarios, campaigns and characters for this.  If this was a FFG game, I wouldn&#039;t be worried (except for worrying about too *many* expansions), but I hope Privateer Press can keep the momentum on this.  I actually feel that they need to make expansions to bring more people on board.

Thoughts on the game itself: The &quot;drab&quot; board isn&#039;t as bad as people are making it out to be. I do wish that the tiles clicked together like Descent&#039;s tiles as I kept knocking them, but that was a small thing. The Villain activation was easy to figure out and worked quite well. The Crossbow thugs stayed at range and fired away while the Sword thugs swarmed their target. 

My scenario ended with Canice having sprinted to get the loot, each character got 5XP, and a few wounds on some of the characters.  I&#039;ll probably play this scenario one more time and hope to get every rule right before moving on to the next scenario.</body>

			<comment username="hervuli" date="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 00:52:42 +0000" postdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 00:52:42 +0000" editdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 00:52:42 +0000" thumbs="2">
I think the key to success (in my limited experience at least) is trying to resolve encounters as quickly as possible, ideally in one turn - even if it means driving your focus way up. That way you don&#039;t have to deal with reinforcements (so high focus doesn&#039;t matter) and, as long as you&#039;ve also prioritized taking out Relentless enemies, you can rest for free. It&#039;s easier said than done but in my successful play-throughs I&#039;d say I&#039;ve finished 80% of my encounters in one turn. Sometimes by killing all the enemies, but just as many times by fulfilling whatever the other end condition is on the encounter card - don&#039;t overlook those!

In any case, this makes fast and reflex actions that deal damage a real priority to get and use.

I&#039;m still trying to figure out optimal strategies but this has been what&#039;s worked for me so far...
</comment>
<comment username="camidon" date="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 14:28:32 +0000" postdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 14:28:32 +0000" editdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 14:28:32 +0000" thumbs="1">
I definitely realized my error with the relentless enemies. After two plays, I have a decent understanding how it all works. The resting after finishing an encounter is critical.
</comment>

	<body>Lately, Iâ€™ve been playtesting â€œA Glorious Chanceâ€, a solitaire wargame that simulates the struggle for Lake Ontario between the American and British navies in the War of 1812. 

[ImageID=2659052 large]

The player commands the American forces seeking to wrest control of the Lake â€“ dominated by the British at the beginning of the game â€“ from the AI. The player sends his fleet on different types of missions in order to score VPâ€™s by controlling Lake areas, invading/raiding enemy strongholds, and sinking major enemy ships. The AI (inspired by John Butterfieldâ€™s [thing=3202]RAF[/thing]) will respond to American incursions to varying degrees depending on its current strategic priorities â€“ or it may seek to exploit holes in the playerâ€™s strategy to score extra VPâ€™s.  

The scale is operational, with each turn representing two weeks. Counters representing individual ships (two types of schooners, brigs, and corvettes). The situation is asymmetrical: the player has far more ships -- but, in the main, they are also far less capable then those of their adversary; the British start with a small but powerful fleet hampered by a lack of long gunsâ€¦initially, at least. Other features include random events, tactics chits, leadership effects, weapon differences, ship repair and construction, and more â€“ leading to surprising granularity in a semi-abstract game in addition to a rich narrative.  

This is an impressive effort from first-time designer, 

[user=broadsword56][/user]

She plans to merge this operationalâ€“level game with a â€œManeuver Levelâ€ system featuring tactical combat; alternately she also has designed the game to be compatible with other Age of Sail tactical systems such as [thing=8730]Flying Colors[/thing]. 

â€œA Glorious Chanceâ€ is in active playtesting. I encourage you to try it out and lend a hand by geekmailing the designer.  

For a taste of how the game plays (but NOT how to play it well!), hereâ€™s [thread=1432071]an AAR of a recent game.[/thread]

I also kept in as many of the other cards as possible, which thanks to recent revisions is now possible for almost all of them - only three have to get pulled, instead of half a dozen previously.

I managed to win this one with a little bit of cushion, and had three tiles left in the draw pile when I began my final turn.   Those all would have gone down at the end of the turn, and then the collapse would have begun on the following turn.  The way the tiles were set up the whole thing would have come down within (at most) 2 turns.

When it ended my final health was at 2, mostly from ambush damage.   Some events hurt too, although a helpful beam of light kept me going when I needed it.   The Potion Kit was never found.

A little more testing is still needed too see if anything else needs to be adjusted yet, but balance-wise this feels really close to right.</body>

	<body>Well it took me forever, but I finished my second play through of Fire in the Lake.  

Oh the AI...I&#039;m actually feeling pretty comfortable that I am doing things correctly, but it is taking me F-O-R-E-V-E-R to do every card (there is a lot of thinking, then checking, and then rechecking going on).  I cringe every time I work down the flow charts and end up at Sweep (with Air Lift), Assault (with Air Lift) or, God forbid, a free March.  Yes, I love that there IS an answer.  And I love that you can credibly play such a deep game solitaire.  And I really, really appreciate that skill in which the AI was designed (brilliant how every scenario I&#039;ve come across has been contemplated...well actually I did run into the &quot;I&#039;ve already executed a Raid so I need to pay for a ARVN Patrol without moving any pieces&quot; in the errata, but still)...but I&#039;m not sure I have it in me to keep learning it so that I can complete a single card in less than 45 minutes!  The last card before the final Coup, the last Coup round, and final scoring took me just shy of two hours last night!  YIKES!

As for my actual game play, I set up Westy&#039;s War (1965-1967, the short scenario) with Period Events.  I played as the VC against the 3 non-player bots.  I started out slow, but was able to do some real damage to ARVN patronage through events.  I was slowly losing bases via US Sweep and Air Strikes, but then the NVA ended up in a relatively tight time frame with two events that gave them free Marches (the Trail was stuck at 0-1 the whole game, so that was huge for them).  They quickly drew the attention of the US, who had lost two bases, and gave me some more room to operate.  The first coup card had come out right in the middle of the first set, but the second came out on the first card possible, which gave me comfort that I would have time to see my plans develop.  A series of AI instructions had left Saigon lightly defended, so I was able to March a bunch of my gathered guerrillas into Saigon.  This was a risky move, as they had all been activated, but they never ended up being targeted as there was always some NVA-controlled population that was a higher priority.  An event had knocked down Saigon support to Passive, and without COIN control, the end of game Support Phase was key for me as I was able to get Saigon to Passive Opposition through Agitation for end of game scoring.  Final score: VC: 0, NVA: -11, ARVN: -9, US: -25.  National Liberation!

Here was my board at the end of the game:
[ImageID=2660943 original]</body>

	<item id="4127645" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="42673" 			
			objectname="Field Commander: Napoleon"
			username="garyrbrooks" 
			postdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 14:30:57 +0000" 
			editdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 14:30:57 +0000"
			thumbs="27"
						imageid="1063957">
	<body>Played the third campaign - 1800 (second Italian campaign)

This is a really short campaign. Win it in 3 turns to match Napoleon.

Realising time was of the essence I attacked Milan straight away with all of Napoleon&#039;s forces that had started in Lonato.

A well fought battle there led to a rout of the enemy forces and the city was captured.  The sweep and engineer insights working well again.

I had 2 resupply points so I had the choice. Sit and regroup or force march a couple of my forces and attack the weak forces in Marengo.  I attacked.

A good fog of war roll allowed me to bring an extra mobile force in to the battle.  This would prove decisive as it allowed me to win the envelope check, totally destroying the forces there.

At the end of my first turn I had 4 of the 5 objectives needed to win.  I bought 2 cannons (the one thing I lacked) and some more cavalry.

The enemy&#039;s first turn also went in my favour.  1 force attacked my forces in Marengo and lost an envelope check again, another attacked my forces in Genoa.

The battle in Genoa was aided when my fog of war roll allowed Napoleon to move to the battle.  My cannons won this battle.

Then it was my next turn.  The forces in Savona were vast.  Total strength was 29.  I would be able to muster forces of strength 30.  Waiting another turn wasn&#039;t going to help much (and would probably spread my forces too much) so I attacked.

Another good fog of war roll allowed me to bring another infantry unit to the battle boosting my strength to 36.  I then successfully activated my sweep and engineer insights which reduced the enemy&#039;s strength to 19 and removed a couple of their units.

After that though I wasn&#039;t able to put enough hits on the enemy as my cannon missed a couple of times and their strongest units kept getting battle plans that kept them out of range of my infantry.  Time was running out.

On the final turn I lost a unit (poor Suchet) but had them down to a garrison unit and a strong cavalry unit.  Total strength 10.  My strength was 24.  If I could hit the garrison with my cannon then they would only be at 7 and I would win a rout check.

I need a 6 or less as I was using the Grapeshot battle plan.  I rolled a 7.

This meant the battle ended and I had to roll for withdrawal. There&#039;s always a 30% chance of a French Retreat at this point which would have been meant another turn would be needed.

I looked at the die.  Don&#039;t roll a 6-8 to I said. 

[ImageID=2661057 medium]
Phew! That&#039;s an enemy retreat.

I now held all 5 objectives. Victory.

[ImageID=2661059 medium] 
Apparently, that makes me a better military leader than Napoleon. :shake:

:thumbsup: The sweeping epic feel you get from this game.

:thumbsup: Forces you into some tough decisions.

:thumbsup: You have to blend strategy, bravery and luck to win.

:thumbsdown: I think it was [user=kerskine][/user] who said this game felt too easy.  I&#039;m not at that point yet but 3 wins in 4 plays (including the notoriously hard 1798 campaign) may mean he is on to something.

:thumbsdown: That combined with the very specific campaigns is starting me thinking that this will be a once through the campaigns type game like PACG: Rise of the Runelords. 

This now might not end up as high on my [geeklist=189816]Top 20[/geeklist] as originally thought because of those two reasons but just like PACG I will enjoy it whilst it&#039;s here.</body>

	<item id="4128270" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="146021" 			
			objectname="Eldritch Horror"
			username="ian_07720169619" 
			postdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 18:50:33 +0000" 
			editdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 18:25:46 +0000"
			thumbs="35"
						imageid="1872452">
	<body>I&#039;ve been playing far too much [thing=90215]Skyrim[/thing] recently so I decided to set myself a goal. I am going to play 1 game of Eldritch Horror against each of the Ancient Ones in the base game before I play any more computer games. The number works out nicely to complete that game in my 10x10 challenge.

[b]Game 1 - Azathoth[/b]
I played using Norman Withers and Leo Anderson using a mix of all the Mythos cards. I ended up facing 5 tentacle cards and 2 Elder Sign cards plus 5 normal cards. As I&#039;m sure you can tell, it was quite difficult. I managed to defeat Azathoth with my 2 investigators intact but had I of needed 1 more round then the world would have been devoured.

The first mystery - Omen of Devastation - was probably the hardest one to complete (it certainly took the longest to complete). I don&#039;t generally close gates or attack monsters unless I absolutely have to. The starting gate and the second one drawn were both red Omens so I planned on attacking them early on once the Omen marker reached that Omen (as that is a requirement of the mystery). Unfortunately, the first investigator became delayed and was unable to reach the gate in time and the second investigator failed the test so could not close the door but did get rid of the monster. With the Omen marker advancing there was little point in closing the gate until it came back around so the investigator remained in that area trying to gain clues while the other investigator carried on moving around the board to advance their skills. Once the omen marker moved back round The gate was closed and the mystery solved.

The second mystery - Seed of the Daemon Sultan - only took 2 turns to complete. The first turn involved one of the investigators getting 1 space away and the second turn he moved to the space and succeeded with the test. While this was going on, the second investigator closed 2 empty gates that were close together.

The third mystery - The True Name - took 3 further turns but that was just how long it took to get to the location. The investigator that hadn&#039;t solved a mystery but had several clues arrived first and spent the clues to complete the mystery. The final Mythos card was tough but didn&#039;t advance the Doom marker so all was good.

At the end of the game the Doom marker was on 2 and both investigators were fairly healthy. From about the 5th turn on Star Spawn and Dark Young were both in play and one of the investigators had a Dark Pact so every time I had to roll the dice during the Mythos phase I was worried about seeing those low numbers. The last turn in particular would have been the worst one. The monsters could have taken the Doom marker down to 0 and the Dark Pact could also have killed off an investigator.

RESULT = WIN

:thumbsup: - The game felt challenging but never impossible.
:thumbsdown: - Some of the &quot;easy&quot; Mythos cards are tougher than the &quot;hard&quot; Mythos cards.
:thumbsdown: - The positioning of objectives can have a huge impact into the difficulty of completing a Mystery.

[b]Game 2 - Yog Sothoth[/b]
This time I used Mark Harrigan and Lola Hayes. The Mythos cards were not as bad but the dice were far worse. I completed all 3 mysteries but not before Yog Sothoth awoke. One of the investigators was then devoured leading to the investigators losing the game.

The first mystery - Spawn of Yog Sothoth - was fairly easy but, due to the positioning of the investigators and the first Mythos card drawn (an ongoing card that prevented gates being closed), took me 8 turns to complete. Mark was the perfect person to complete that mystery but was also in the best position to complete the ongoing Mythos card. He was also nowhere near a clue so could not complete the Mythos card and for some reason I didn&#039;t think to solve the mystery first. Lola failed to solve a clue 4 3 turns running and in the end gave up trying. Instead she started trying to tackle some of the monsters at the gates. Mark eventually managed to gain a clue and solve the Mythos card before completing the first mystery 2 turns later.

The second mystery - Arcane Understanding - started off difficult as neither investigator had spells. After a couple of turns they had both managed to gain spells and clues so on the following turn the both performed the spell&#039;s action and complete that mystery. By this point doom was down to 3 and things were not looking good.

The third mystery - The Beyond One - only took 2 turns to complete and that was only because of where each investigator needed to get to in order to help solve the mystery. Unfortunately, before the mystery could be solved I had to complete the Mythos phase. Doom advanced by 3 and Yog Sothoth awoke. The mystery was solved so all I had to do was solve the Final Mystery.

The final mystery was very quick. Lola was next to a gate so moved to it and failed the test causing her to be devoured and doom to be advanced (a gate added to Yog Sothoth). Mark moved to within 1 space of a gate but could not get to it so had to complete a random encounter. The Mythos card caused the Omen track to move around and 2 more doom to be added. With 3 doom (gates) on Yog Sothoth the investigators lost the game. I looked at the next special encounter card to see if Mark would have won the game and he would have successfully passed the tests.

RESULT = LOSS

:thumbsup: - Despite causing me to lose, the Mythos cards were much nicer this time.
:thumbsdown: - This time I never felt like I had a chance of winning. The dice rolls were just not going my way and Doom seemed to advance every turn.
:thumbsdown: - For my style of play I&#039;m not sure Lola Hayes is a good character to play with. She was randomly drawn but if I was choosing characters then I would not pick her.</body>

	<item id="4128504" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="140620" 			
			objectname="Lewis &amp; Clark"
			username="Lumpy75" 
			postdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 19:36:51 +0000" 
			editdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 19:36:51 +0000"
			thumbs="20"
						imageid="1902092">
	<body>Now that this is sitting on the top of the pile, I find I&#039;m drawn to it much more.  The quick setup time helps too :)

Either I was really lucky this time or I&#039;m starting to get this game.  MacKenzie didn&#039;t have a chance.

The key this time was discovering just how powerful Tetoharsky is.  He can move you up to nine mountain spaces a turn without spending a single resource!  I managed to breeze through both mountain ranges with fully laden boats, then spend some fur/equip to recruit a good card, and then immediately use Tuttle to build some canoes before continuing the journey along the river before camping with empty canoes.

I used an even more card-heavy strategy than last time, only using Indians for Tetoharsky&#039;s skill.  I had a team of ten cards at the end having recruited Tuttle (1 wood -&gt; 1 canoe), Tetoharsky (1 Indian -&gt; 1 mountain per 3 resource in boats), Broken Arm (1 equip -&gt; 1 horse), Comcomly (1 wood + 1 fur + 1 equip + 1 food -&gt; 7 river), and Cut Nose (+1 mountain).

I realised a few turns after starting that I wasn&#039;t concentrating when setting up the game, so MacKenzie started in the same space as me.  I made my final camp no less than 7 spaces past the finish line with MacKenzie a further 12 (twelve!) spaces back.  Far and away my best result :cool:</body>

						imageid="2402894">
	<body>Played with the Ravage and started with with 6 vitality cards desolute side up. Added a little bit of tension, when a few Ravage cards came out one after another, but not enough that it drastically changed my play, or the game&#039;s difficulty - Might have gotten lucky with having a hand full of elephants during a period where I was drawing Ravage card after Ravage card. Cycled through my deck far faster than I&#039;ve done previously due to how many Owls I accidentally wound up with in it.

Might try mixing things up with one of the real expansions next time, or shift to the 2 card draw rather than the three card draw means of upping difficulty.

:thumbsup: The game seems to hold up despite me finding it far too easy
:thumbsdown: It might be harder to figure out how to up the difficulty sufficiently to feel challenging than it is to win.
:thumbsdown: Owls might be overpowered if the recruitment phase allows you to get a fair few into your deck, since suddenly you&#039;re able to thin your deck into a lean, mean, fighting machine since you lose one (random) or two (of your choice) cards whenever you shuffle your deck - I had thought that would be a cost previously, so expected the Owls to be about as powerful as the Fish - 3 for 2 which is multiuse rather than just for energy, but which forces you to lose cards faster, but... I think that might have been upside rather than downside, at least in the game I just played.</body>

	<body>Played using Andrew Watson&#039;s [filepage=121756]Evolutama[/filepage] solo variant. This game fits this month&#039;s theme of Waiting for me, since I&#039;ve been waiting for a chance to get Evolution to the table since my first play of it soon after my KS edition of it arrived, on account that my fiance doesn&#039;t enjoy the game, and during this week a link to Andrew&#039;s solo variant was posted somewhere I subscribe.

...And I lost by a landslide, after being crippled early on in the game when it decided to pump up it&#039;s BS of all it&#039;s species the turn I decided to make one of mine a carnivore, which set me back sufficiently that I never really recovered (I think if I had more experience I could have probably recovered, and if not that&#039;s a fault of the game rather than the solo variant in question) Quite like the way this solo variant functions, all being told.

Difficulty wise, this variant seems fine - this is the second time I&#039;ve played Evolution, and the first time was a half game, so being crushed by the bot is fair enough.

:thumbsup: Very smooth AI to run, with enough randomness to be unpredictable (And enough randomness to absolutely hose you if it decides to) but one that definitely plays to a &#039;plan&#039; within that random framework.
:thumbsdown: Currently the info needed to run the Evolutama is spread across a couple of pages of the PDF file, but that should be easily fixable even if it doesn&#039;t get fixed by Andrew in future versions.
:thumbsdown: The Automa makes the tablehogginess of Evolution significantly worse, since now you need to have two players worth of creatures in easy reach of you, which means they&#039;re going to start running into each other, fast.</body>

	<body>I have been waiting to see if the Houston Astros are going to be legitimate contenders in baseball this year. In other words, waiting for them to fail. I have been pleasantly surprised!

I designed a Baseball Highlights: 2045 challenge using a constructed deck premise. You can find the details here:
[listitem=4128682][/listitem]

This was my play-through of the Medium difficulty deck.

Game 1: Win 3-0. Between the automated player and myself, we had 8 cards + one Visitor Save card that canceled hits, turned hits into walks, and removed base runners. This was a very low-scoring game considering the fire-power in play. Rarely can I keep the automated player scoreless. I was ready to have much higher scoring games for the next two.

Game 2: Win 8-6. Barry Sosa was poised to knock in 4 runs for the automated player in the bottom of the 6th inning. CC Clemens canceled his hits! Nice.

Game 3: Win 8-7. Mickey Maris hit a single and home run in the 6th and my defense held off the automated player for tight win. Overall, there was very little defense in this game.

Game 4: Win 6-2. I had 5 players cancel hits or remove runners out of my 6 at bats + Visitor Save. I wiped out what would have been a major offensive effort by the automated player.

[ImageID=2661745 large]
Result: A series sweep and one of my most convincing victories in the solo variant of this game!

Please join in the challenge and get yourself ready for the playoffs and World Series.</body>

	<body>I have now completed three chapters (i.e., missions) in the campaign, and am enjoying this game quite a bit.  The first chapter was very basic, but two and three had some interesting tricks that showed imaginative uses of the villain rules and the board.  My characters are all sporting upgraded abilities, and I found a very useful item on a Side Quest [o]Fear Gas Grenade, that will cause all figures in a space to either fall down or run away, unless I roll a 1[/o] that Pog will carry.  But I am running into tougher villains, and each chapter has rules to create the Event and Villain activation decks so as to up the challenge.

I&#039;m actually tempted to pause my campaign here in order to paint the minis to increase my enjoyment of the final four chapters.  I see no issue in replaying the campaign, as it will not play out exactly the same and I can a few things to adjust the difficulty level.

	<item id="4128778" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="151022" 			
			objectname="Baseball Highlights: 2045"
			username="draines"

			thumbs="21"
						imageid="2262580">
	<body>After winning against the Medium difficulty constructed deck in my challenge (see previous entry for the details), it was time for the Hard difficulty. Wow! This automated team was tough.

Game 1: Win 5-2. I managed to cancel hits with 2 cards and pick off runners with 2 cards to keep the automated player at bay. My deck will be thin on defense for the next two games. Good start.

Game 2: Loss 4-10. Yeah, I was in trouble the whole game. The automated player had too many hits. And then his runners were fast and faster! I licked my wounds and got ready for the third game in the series. You need a short memory in sports!

[ImageID=2661752 large]

Game 3: Loss 6-10. I was challenged to put up any offense. Mickey Maris hit a single and then a grand slam home run in the 2nd to account for most of my runs. I couldn&#039;t slow down the automated player with his multiple hit players. This series is going to end quickly if I don&#039;t do better than this on defense.

Game 4: Win 8-7. I was ahead in a defensive struggle when Bucky Tulo tied it for the automated player in the bottom of the 6th, 5-5. We both scored 2 runs in the 7th, before I managed to eek across a runner in the 8th to win. This was definitely the highlight game of the series. Both teams played well, but I was able to hit when I needed to.

Game 5: Loss 7-8. My team was doing well, but then Big Mo hit a &quot;Quick Eye&quot; homer (followed by 3 singles) to score 3 runs for the automated player. I tried, but never quite caught up. Did Big Mo kill my team&#039;s chance for glory? Could they come back again?

Game 6: Win 7-2. Yes, the team could come back. I drew 6 Free Agents for my hand and coasted to an easy win. The automated player did not have a chance. Now the question was, did I have enough power left in my deck to win the seventh and decisive game?

[o]Game 7: Both defenses played well and kept it tight. I managed to pull ahead 4-3, only to see Barry Sosa come up to the plate in the 5th with two runners on base. This would mean a 4 run inning and a series win for the automated player. My only hope was to cancel the hits. My last card was CC Clemens, who cancels all hits by Naturals!! My superior forecasting of when to play cards left me with the only card in my deck that would save the game. Win 5-3. A series win for my team!![/o]

Please join in the challenge and create your own fantastic story. Have fun!</body>

	<item id="4128884" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="132018" 			
			objectname="Churchill"
			username="Kappa_ap" 
			postdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 23:34:16 +0000" 
			editdate="Wed, 09 Sep 2015 23:34:16 +0000"
			thumbs="22"
						imageid="2467234">
	<body>Just wrapped up my first 3 conference training scenario with a Churchill wins tiebreaker; Churchill and Stalin were tied on 38 points, with Roosevelt/Truman trailing close behind with 37.

Germany had surrendered, the US had the A-bomb however the USSR had not entered Manchuria - I was all set to make it happen but forgot about the USSR declares war on Japan conditional issue - and so Japan did not surrender which led to a condition 3 endgame.

Progressing the Pacific and CBI fronts proved tricky. That said it seems all of the allied fronts requires a concerted, combined allied effort for them to progress easily.

Curiously Stalin, and his crew, were pretty strong during all three conferences with their debating characteristic proving handy. Indeed they won both of their global issues! Also the US and UK spent a fair bit of time worrying about the colonies but Stalin kept snatching the issue away from them.

An interesting and thought provoking game.  

The bots offer useful guidelines to the solo player but I found myself more frequently just playing each in a manner that seemed logical, at least to me anyway!



</body>

	<item id="4129236" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="174570" 			
			objectname="Legendary Encounters: A Predator Deck Building Game"
			username="pusherman42" 
			postdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 03:54:49 +0000" 
			editdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 03:54:49 +0000"
			thumbs="29"
						imageid="2486937">
	<body>[IMG]http://www.superiorpics.com/movie_pictures/mp/1987_Predator/1987_predator_017.jpg[/IMG]

Got my first game of this in. Took on the first move in the jungle. Things started off good enough, working my way through the first objective with not much problem.

[o]The first objective is pretty clever. You have to take out the guerrilla camp, which attaches to the Wilds. You only need 1 attack to do it, but it has to be in an empty space. But cards are always shifting it around, so it&#039;s harder to get a hold of than you might think.

I very much liked this mechanic. Finally I had enough attack to scan a card and kill it, which, when it dies, lets me move the camp (if out) to the left. Doing that put it in an empty space and I had one attack left to level the place.[/o]

The second objective deck started showing up before I&#039;d finished the first, though, and that was going to be tough. Plus, the hazards were piling up on me causing all sorts of problems.

[o]The hazards, which I guess aren&#039;t really spoilers since they show up on the open objective card, but whatever, anyway the hazards attach to the player that flips them up (all me), and then move cards directly to the combat area. First one, then two. That clears the Wilds a bit, but the strikes definitely piled up while I sifted for good cards.[/o]

At this point my deck was at least doing it&#039;s thing. I had lots of red-arrow-symbol-thing cards, meaning I could use Sexual Tyrannosaurus to heal up strikes pretty often. 

[IMG]http://i.ytimg.com/vi/_3rfAjpHOyI/maxresdefault.jpg[/IMG]

My main damage was from a bunch of 2-attack cards I&#039;d bought, and using the Brothers in Arms trait to power up one of the Dutch cards.

Objective 2 was completed quickly, making me feel like I had some time to try and get a hold of the Wilds before things got bad.

[o]Objective two is to set up a defensive position. When the objective comes out, it sits to the side and you have to pay 6 recruit to attach it and finish it off. I just got a lucky draw with all my recruit cards.[/o]

Things then got bad. I started taking strike after strike, and couldn&#039;t keep up with the healing.

[IMG]https://toomanyposts.files.wordpress.com/2014/03/predator-face-off.jpg?w=590[/IMG]

[o]Objective 3 is &quot;survive.&quot; According to the rules, I can kill the predator or use some other Minor Victory card. Never saw either, as I couldn&#039;t stay on top of the stream of bad guys. There were cards that cause strikes even in the Wilds. Another hazard moved more people to the combat zone. Eventually they overcame me and that was it.[/o]

I looked for a picture of what happened next, but they were all a little too violently graphic. It didn&#039;t end well.

--------------------------------

I enjoyed the play. I like the difficulty, that seemed good. There are a few oddities though. For one, the card that you get with your Role requires someone to coordinate with you in order to be used. I don&#039;t like to play 2-handed, so not only are all the coordinate cards not that good for me, now ALL of the roles are blank. All of them.

That seems harsh for solo players. The loss of coordinate is one thing, and I think it helps make the solo game harder, which is good. But losing the entire effect of different roles is a real bummer.

Also, you still start with a 13 card deck. Like Alien. However, the unique card you get does not let you draw a card. So unlike Alien, your starting deck is not a multiple of the cards you draw per turn.

That means you&#039;ll draw 6, use them, draw 6, use those, and then draw 1 and have to shuffle and draw 5 more. I guess that&#039;s fine? It&#039;s just odd. It&#039;s the first deckbuilder I&#039;ve played that does that.

I like the art generally better than Alien. Some of it is still pretty bad, and often times the characters don&#039;t look the way the characters look. Which would be fine if this wasn&#039;t based on an actual visual license where we know exactly what the characters look like because they were in a movie. It&#039;s not like someone having to interpret Tolkien or something. But the Predator art is all pretty good.

I do think I&#039;ll enjoy this one even more when it comes to multiplayer play. The coordinate cards look fun, and the role cards that key off of that mechanic look really fun as well. There were also lots of things that multiple players could all chip in on, which was cool.

For the strictly solo player, though, you&#039;re getting half the game. There&#039;s two movies, not four, so there&#039;s not as much to do. However, you can play both movies as the Predator as well. So there&#039;s just as many cards, and two whole games in the box, but the Predator mode is a competitive mode requiring opponents.

Unless, shameless plug, you join us for [url=https://boardgamegeek.com/article/20117951#20117951]PREDATOR GOLF[/url]. I&#039;m giving away over 400:gg:, so come win some. I&#039;ve been coming up with some crazy hole ideas as well, see what sorts of bizarre ways we can compete using the same cards.

Since I played this once this month, I&#039;ve got to get two more plays of it at least. That&#039;s the rule. I&#039;m looking forward to them! </body>

<comment username="pusherman42" date="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 13:24:02 +0000" postdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 13:24:02 +0000" editdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 13:24:02 +0000" thumbs="4">
[q=&quot;garyrbrooks&quot;]Thanks for the post Jack.  My copy is on it&#039;s way but as I play one handed solo I&#039;m now wondering if I&#039;ve got a bit over excited.[/q]

[q=&quot;topherunhinged&quot;]The loss of roles is very dissapointing and I already thought that coordinate was already far too prevalent in Alien, making solo play feel more limited as a result, but also felt that in a two-handed or two-player game coordinate was insanity over-powered.

Maybe a pass is in order here? Only time will tell as more people report in.[/q]

I feel up and down about it. For one, the role cards do have attack and recruit. So they aren&#039;t dead cards, they&#039;re still pretty good. The role card I used had the Call for Backup ability (meaning, I can use it if someone coordinates with me) of letting me pull a card from my discard and put it on top of my deck.

It also had 2 attack, though. Which is great for a starting card. So it never felt completely useless. Keep in mind that even playing multiplayer, this ability won&#039;t be used every time you have the card because someone will have to coordinate with you. So playing one-handed, you&#039;re going from using it only sometimes to using it none times.

On top of that, one of my biggest criticisms of Alien is that the role card didn&#039;t really do all that much. You use it a few times during the game, it&#039;s power isn&#039;t something you can depend on, it doesn&#039;t really differentiate you all that much from the other roles, and it&#039;ll get drowned out by the time your deck is really getting going. All of those are true of Predator, too, so I can&#039;t really lament the loss of something that I didn&#039;t think was all that huge to begin with. Only difference being that the abilities on these roles look way fun, and I hate to miss them.

You can fix this simply by playing 2-handed. Which, if the posts on the game&#039;s difficulty are to be believed, might even be necessary to do well. Or, you could just say that you can trigger your own Call for Backup ability if you play a card with coordinate on your turn, making both the role and coordinate just a little bit useful.

Overall, though, I wouldn&#039;t say that the loss of the roles is a deal breaker. I liked the scenario quite a bit, it felt more like the predator movie than any of the Aliens scenarios felt like Alien movies to me. It was brutal and close and fun.

Looking forward to doing some golfing! I&#039;ll post the first hole soon, but I won&#039;t put up a due date until well after people have their games.
</comment>

	<item id="4129915" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="135382" 			
			objectname="Shadowrun: Crossfire"
			username="garyrbrooks" 
			postdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 13:27:37 +0000" 
			editdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 13:35:40 +0000"
			thumbs="24"
						imageid="2060466">
	<body>Picked this up from the post office last night and got in my first two games of it.

Played the Crossfire mission using the Ork and Elf.  Not surprisingly I lost both times.

[ImageID=2662589 medium]The end... again.

It&#039;s a deck builder but as some have said it&#039;s not one in the traditional sense.

You only add a few cards to your hand and don&#039;t replenish your hand fully every turn so you have to manage your hand a lot more carefully than in other deck builders and buying the biggest and best card available in the market isn&#039;t necessarily the best thing.

I had heard it&#039;s arbitrarily hard and until I play this some more I can&#039;t comment on that.  It does up the difficulty as those crossfire event cards come out though.

I think there may be more to learn here than a normal deck builder.

I knew not to expect the same as a normal deck builder but think I still made some of those errors - e.g. taking my turns quickly.

I need to spend some more time thinking ahead.

No thumbs yet, too early.  I did enjoy the two games though.  Mechanically this is a hit but time will tell if I like the overall experience.</body>
	
			<comment username="pusherman42" date="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 13:57:46 +0000" postdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 13:57:46 +0000" editdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 13:57:46 +0000" thumbs="3">

<comment username="kerskine" date="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 14:06:26 +0000" postdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 14:06:26 +0000" editdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 14:06:26 +0000" thumbs="5">
If you don&#039;t mind, I&#039;ll offer up some suggestions. None of these are really spoilers. If you want strategy tips, I can help there as well.

Well I&#039;ll give you one tip. The elf is really tough in a 2-player game because of the low HP start. He also starts with 4 cards which in a weird sense is a disadvantage because you need to play something the first round or you&#039;ll only draw one card. If that makes no sense whatsoever, I can explain, but I&#039;d do it in a geekmail or in spoiler tags.

The first few things are rules that are easy to overlook. 
- When you play with two, you don&#039;t draw a crossfire card the first 2 turns. I think most people get this one right.
- Because each character is playing two roles, they each start with an extra Nguyen (I missed that the first 20 plays. It really helps).
- As soon as you kill all enemies on the board, you immediately bury the crossfire card (not discard it). And you don&#039;t choose another one until the start of the first players turn again. So you may start the next scene with the second player, with no crossfire card in play.

The next thing I&#039;ll tell you is that it&#039;s really easy to get the single karma point for aborting the mission. It may seem a bit fishy, but if you can&#039;t see that you&#039;ll survive the next wave, then let one person go staggered, then critical with only one enemy in front of you. survive it for one round and collect your point. In your case, getting that +1 HP for the elf would be really helpful. Once you get past 10 Karma, you can&#039;t get a point for aborting anymore because of the -1 Karma penalty for 11-20.

I would strongly suggest trying the Extraction mission even if you have no Karma upgrades yet. It has scaling for 1-4 characters and I found it considerably easier to win. (Again don&#039;t forget that if you play with more roles, you get an extra Nguyen for each role. So a solo character starts with 3 extra. Because of assists, I&#039;d never play it with less than 2, but I know some like that. Maybe when you get past 20 Karma and have 2 5pt upgrades or a single 20 point upgrade you can go back to Crossfire. 

I&#039;m now at 118 plays of this and I may always have it setup on a table. I have a small round table that is too small for most games, but it works perfectly for a 2-player game of this.
</comment>
<comment username="de_la_poer" date="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 14:09:13 +0000" postdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 14:09:13 +0000" editdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 14:09:13 +0000" thumbs="1">

- Got that right.
- Forgot that both times.  Thanks.
- I buried the card but started with the first player again even if they shouldn&#039;t have. Thanks again.

[q=&quot;kerskine&quot;]The next thing I&#039;ll tell you is that it&#039;s really easy to get the single karma point for aborting the mission. It may seem a bit fishy, but if you can&#039;t see that you&#039;ll survive the next wave, then let one person go staggered, then critical with only one enemy in front of you. survive it for one round and collect your point. In your case, getting that +1 HP for the elf would be really helpful. Once you get past 10 Karma, you can&#039;t get a point for aborting anymore because of the -1 Karma penalty for 11-20.[/q]
I couldn&#039;t keep the second character alive through the abort run either time.

[q=&quot;kerskine&quot;]I would strongly suggest trying the Extraction mission even if you have no Karma upgrades yet. It has scaling for 1-4 characters and I found it considerably easier to win. (Again don&#039;t forget that if you play with more roles, you get an extra Nguyen for each role. So a solo character starts with 3 extra. Because of assists, I&#039;d never play it with less than 2, but I know some like that. Maybe when you get past 20 Karma and have 2 5pt upgrades or a single 20 point upgrade you can go back to Crossfire.[/q]
I&#039;ll try extraction.  I avoided it because of the upgrades thing but I will give it a go. I like the assist thing too so for the moment I&#039;m going to play it two handed.

[q=&quot;kerskine&quot;]I&#039;m now at 118 plays of this and I may always have it setup on a table. I have a small round table that is too small for most games, but it works perfectly for a 2-player game of this.[/q]
I&#039;m still amazed by how much you&#039;ve played this and how I didn&#039;t even notice for ages.  You are a secret shadowrunner. :D
</comment>
<comment username="kerskine" date="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 15:11:52 +0000" postdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 15:11:52 +0000" editdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 15:12:30 +0000" thumbs="2">
You&#039;re correct sorry. No draw if you have more than 3 cards. Lost my mind there. I so rarely have more than 3 after a turn.

On the abort, if you wait until you&#039;re forced to do the abort, then your second character probably isn&#039;t going to make it. If you have two characters low on health and you realize that drawing 4 obstacles in the last scene is going to be insurmountable, then let that last remaining obstacle hit someone twice to critical them. Then the last guy just has to survive that one guy.

Yeah I hear everyone now saying that&#039;s cheesy, but think of it thematically. Would you rush on to a room full of bad guys if you were both bleeding to death? No, you&#039;d abort and live to fight another day. It&#039;s not your fault the rules say you can&#039;t abort until someone is critically hurt. 

As far as extraction. Some things to remember. 
- The client has to survive through to the end of the 6th round. (The 7th one says you win!). 
- You don&#039;t have to kill everything. You just have to survive long enough and keep the client alive.
- Read through the steps so you know when healing is coming.
- Regardless of the number of players, you don&#039;t get any Crossfire free rounds so start drawing from the beginning. My win percentage at this scenario with 2 and 4 players is probably around 80%. I did have at least 5 points in Karma upgrades though, so you may not do as well, but it&#039;s still easier than Crossfire.
- Remember the Client is a human runner so everything that refers to runners applies to him (runner with most hits, runners take a hit ...)
- Also remember that if he draws an obstacle that says &#039;you&#039; can&#039;t buy cards or draw cards or whatever other restriction, well that&#039;s a good thing because the client doesn&#039;t have any cards or Nguyen and he doesn&#039;t share in Nguyen when you kill things. 

Also, if you have the time search on youtube for &quot;shadowrun with the designers&quot; Those 4 videos are fantastic. The last one has them plating Extraction. One color in particular is exceptionally good for extraction. 

Speaking of which, another general hint I&#039;ll give you is that damage is usually better than healing. A mistake a lot of people do is to grab the Doc Wagon card when it isn&#039;t really critical. Kill things and you won&#039;t need as much healing ;)

This may well be my second 10.

</comment>

[q=&quot;Cardboard Conundrum&quot;]Hmmmm... a trick taking game for one...? That&#039;s definitely got me interested - can you play with a standard deck of 52 cards?[/q]

You could maybe emulate it.... the Decktet has 6 suits and  36 cards (no face cards equiv) and 2-9 have two suits a piece while Aces and Crowns (10&#039;s) only have one suit.

That said, the BGG page says it&#039;s based off of [thing=31266][/thing] so maybe that would be better. Haven&#039;t tried it, though.

<comment username="pmagnus" date="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 19:04:09 +0000" postdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 19:04:09 +0000" editdate="Thu, 10 Sep 2015 19:04:09 +0000" thumbs="2">
I&#039;m glad you enjoy the game. :)

[q=&quot;squarepegsys&quot;]....the BGG page says it&#039;s based off of [thing=31266][/thing] so maybe that would be better.[/q]

The bit that&#039;s inspired by Oneonta Whist is trick-taking against a dummy hand. The ability to twiddle the trump and the scoring rule that requires getting each bid exactly are original additions in Gongor Whist.

	<body>While trying to minimize the amount of games on my [geeklist=196079]&quot;unplayed games&quot; - List[/geeklist] the boardgames gods decided to advance preorder deliveries and even kickstarter-deliveries from like 2 years ago to show up this month.

[ImageID=2660238]

As far as I see it&#039;s as unforgiving as the bigger brother [thing=30549]Pandemic[/thing] but with even less projectable outcome because of all the dice rolls.

Would I prefer it over the original Pandemic (with no expansions)? Probably not... for that it&#039;s to light and too much dice luck. But yes, still a good dice chucker with a small enough footprint that I can let a bigger game stay on my &quot;gaming table&quot; during the week.

:thumbsdown: Too much depending on dice luck

	<item id="4131802" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="164167" 			
			objectname="Eldritch Horror: Mountains of Madness"
			username="haenggi"

	<body>Another expansion for I game I really like and another entry from my [geeklist=196079]&quot;Catch up Month&quot; - Geeklist[/geeklist] I wanted to get to the table well knowing it won&#039;t be done in one session.

So the goal was set to play it three times this week but I wanted to really appreciate the different new parts and mechanics of this expansion.

[ImageID=2660235]

I started without any additional Antarctic material except one of the new Elder One and of course all the new cards for exploration deck, item deck, Prologue cards and so on...

My first run against Ithaqua went quite smooth and as soon as I started to use the new focus action it really started to get easy... The three mysteries were solved in no time and I actually scored my [b]FIRST WIN[/b] in this game.

[ImageID=2660237]

I went on with game two and now included the new board and the second new Elder One card (that triggers the Antarctic map). It first struggled a bit with the first two mysteries and wasn&#039;t sure I&#039;ll make it through the demanded 4 (!!!). But at the end my brave heroes won again :arrrh:

[ImageID=2663752]

To round up the expansion experience I started a third game with the one Prologue-Card that let you use the Antarctic map too... And with a EO I never beat before... Cthulhu himself.

Already looking forward to my third win in a row I started really optimistic into that game. But as it turned out it became a struggle for life and death... One character got insane and the other simply died... With probably the last round I could make it through I managed to keep Cthulhu sleeping and solved the third mystery.
But I have to admit, that I probably wouldn&#039;t have made it if the expedition cards from the expansion would had advance the mysteries at least two times.

[ImageID=2663753]

Overall a really good expansion for a great narrative game.
I found several discussions on the BGG board about how this expansion would make the game easier... And I have to admit that out of my 9 games only the three with the expansion included I was able to win. And yes, with the focus action it feels a little bit easier.

:thumbsup: Great artwork and components quality
:thumbsup: The new board and all the new cards really add tension, replayability and even more fun to the base game.
:thumbsup: It definitely makes it more possible to win.</body>

	<item id="4131804" 
			objecttype="thing"
			subtype="boardgame" 
			objectid="135382" 			
			objectname="Shadowrun: Crossfire"
			username="garyrbrooks" 
			postdate="Fri, 11 Sep 2015 09:51:02 +0000" 
			editdate="Fri, 11 Sep 2015 09:51:02 +0000"
			thumbs="20"
						imageid="2060466">
	<body>I don&#039;t normally post twice in a month about the same game but this definitely deserved a second post.

Played three more games (Crossfire mission) and two other aborted games (one due to not drawing crossfire cards :shake: and one that was going well until at the start of scene three I realised I&#039;d only fought two obstacles in scene two :shake:).

I felt my brain adapting to the game with every play.  I was starting to learn the cards a bit more.  I was starting to think about what I should play this turn and what I could do next turn, as well as what my other character could do on their turn and could they assist me now or me on theirs, what was in the black market that could help us now or maybe later.

The hand management is really important and I love hand management games.  As soon as my brain clicked in to that mode this definitely changed as an experience.

It really is about playing the game rather than the turn which is what most deck builders make you do.  They are all about the now - buy the best card, do the most damage, etc and do it now.  That&#039;s not a criticism, just that they require a different mindset.

This is about planning ahead and deciding what will be better in the long term.  You also have to build taking damage into your thinking.  It&#039;s OK to take some licks and clear your buddy&#039;s obstacles.  Using some cards so they are in your discard pile also helps as you or the other character can use them on the next turn.

Lot&#039;s to think about.  Lot&#039;s of potential here.  

Anyway, in the third game (my fifth overall) I won.

[ImageID=2663763 medium]
It ended like this.

My Dwarf (male) was facing off against the final obstacle in scene three.  A Gunslinger Adept.  You can&#039;t damage him until you discard a weapon or spell card.

Luckily my Troll (female) could assist with &#039;Backdoor&#039; which removed that ability and did 1 damage.

My Dwarf then used &#039;Pair Programming&#039; (2 damage) to play &#039;Black Market Contacts&#039; (1 damage) out of the Troll&#039;s discard pile which also allowed me to buy a black market card immediately and put it in my hand.  I bought &#039;Co-ordinated Assault&#039;.

The Drawf then played 2 x &#039;Mark&#039;, a &#039;Mana&#039; and a &#039;Quick Shot&#039; to finish off the the first three levels of the obstacle.  They used &#039;Co-ordinated Assault&#039; to finish off the next level and that allowed the Troll to draw a card and play a card.  They played &#039;Mana&#039; and the last level was gone.

What a turn (Mage Knight-esque), what a win and what a feeling. I&#039;m now excited to play again.

:thumbsup: A deck builder with a difference.  It combines many of my favourite mechanics to make this feel deeper than most deck builders.

:thumbsdown: It has taken support from people here and the videos by the designers to expose what this game really is about.  That&#039;s a shame as this (after 5 plays anyway) is a real gem if you know what to expect.</body>

<comment username="garyrbrooks" date="Fri, 11 Sep 2015 13:18:32 +0000" postdate="Fri, 11 Sep 2015 13:18:32 +0000" editdate="Fri, 11 Sep 2015 13:18:32 +0000" thumbs="2">
[q=&quot;koinskyz&quot;]Thank you Gary for over-ruling your own rule ([i]&quot;I don&#039;t normally post twice in a month about the same game&quot;[/i]), if I may say so.

I didn&#039;t pay much attention to your previous post, on the basis it&#039;s a deck-building game, but now I&#039;m all &#039;eyes&#039; with this second post.

I guess I&#039;ll spend the evening watching some videos and reading some rules :) [/q]

Thanks Delphine.  I&#039;m glad you enjoyed it.

Definitely watch the youtube videos by the designers that everyone suggested to me.  Really helped me understand the game and avoid normal deck building decisions.

This does still have deck building elements but so does Mage Knight.  I wouldn&#039;t call that a deck builder in the sense of Legendary or Star Realms.

You don&#039;t get to scrap cards and some turns even if you can afford it you don&#039;t buy cards.  My Troll bought 8 and my Dwarf 7 in that last game.  In this game it is more about what you buy, when you buy them and when you use them.

Everything Kevin and others have said about this game is right.  Once you realise you aren&#039;t playing a Dominion style deck builder this game comes to life.
</comment>

:thumbsdown: This game really has a ridiculous amount of shuffling in it. I think I make this point every time I play it.

	<body>One more time with time to kill, one more solo game of Legendary. Actually I don&#039;t have real time to kill since I have work to do, but laziness is a bitch.
So, using [user=redvulture][/user] randomizer [url=http://tablemonkey.net/Legendary]Wheel of Fate[/url] I ended up with this set up for an Advanced solo mode:
- Heroes: Daredevil, Forge and Moon Knight;
- Mastermind: Loki;
- Villains: Enemies of Asgard and Phalanx.
- Scheme: Replace Earth&#039;s Leaders with Killbots.

It was my first experience with a hero from the Paint the Town Red expansion and I got to say that Moon Knight did an excellent job. His combinations with Forge gave em a lot of power. Daredevil also helped in this fight, but the main role were given to the first two, no doubts.

About Loki and the villains, my main problem were the wounds they got me. Since there was only one kind of cards with [i]Strength[/i] and none with [i]Ranged[/i] I got some wounds along the game. But, at the same time, I recruited a lot of heroes so they were mixed and a lot of times I was able to use them with Forge to discard.

The scheme at first seemed at first seemed way too easy, but then the Killbots started to get more power and when they were 7 I started to be a little worried (I already had one escaped). At the end, with MK and DD rare cards and some combos I was able to defeat Loki without any more escapes.

Final score: 29pt
3 Master strikes occurred
5 Scheme twists revealed
2 Villains escaped
